Title: Venezuela Suspends Flights From Colombia To Prevent 'Entry Of Mercenaries'
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Venezuela Suspends Flights From Colombia To Prevent 'Entry Of Mercenaries'</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/world/venezuela-suspends-flights-from-colombia-to-prevent-entry-of-mercenaries-5860927">Authored by Yeny Sora Robles via The Epoch Times</a> (emphasis ours),</em></p>

<p><strong>Venezuelan Security Minister Diosdado Cabello on May 19 announced the suspension of flights from Colombia due to the possible entry of “mercenaries,” </strong>days before the legislative and regional elections scheduled for May 25..</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2880%29_0.jpg?itok=z15OlSC3" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2880%29_0.jpg?itok=z15OlSC3"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="e5c8344a-348a-4a2e-9821-f80000f38fa6" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2880%29_0.jpg?itok=z15OlSC3" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>A passenger shows a Venezuelan passport as he waits for news after the cancellation of his flight to Caracas at El Dorado International Airport in Bogota on May 19, 2025. Venezuela's ruling reghime said on that day that it had suspended flights arriving from neighboring Colombia after what it called a cross-border infiltration of "mercenaries" allegedly planning to disrupt upcoming legislative and regional elections on May 25. Raul Arboleda/AFP via Getty Images</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>Cabello claimed these “mercenaries” are part of a plan to destabilize the country.</p>

<p>“<strong>We have given instructions that all flights from Colombia to Venezuela be immediately suspended because the information we have is related to this type of movement of people,</strong>” Cabello <a href="https://youtu.be/G4aVIRLxCJQ?si=bUBacJLRHU9RaNVe&t=772">said</a> in a televised broadcast.</p>

<p>“These are people who come with clear objectives and will enter Venezuela like any other tourist,” he added.</p>

<p>The elections for governors, state legislators, and National Assembly deputies are marked with questions about the legitimacy of Nicolás Maduro’s presidency following allegations of electoral fraud and state repression after the July 2024 presidential elections.</p>

<p><strong>A May <a href="https://www.oas.org/fpdb/press/Report_2025.pdf">report</a> from the Organization of American States documented an increase in human rights violations targeting the opposition, including the state’s use of widespread enforced disappearance as a tool of repression.</strong></p>

<p>The report said electoral repression in Venezuela has reached a critical turning point and gave examples such as state-confirmed murder of protesters, an unprecedented scale of arbitrary detention accompanied by reports of torture and sexual violence, as well as the formal integration of “Colectivos”—armed civilian groups that function as state-enabled actors engaging in home invasions, beatings, arrests, and extrajudicial killings.</p>

<h2>38 People Arrested</h2>

<p>In his broadcast, Cabello also stated that the Venezuelan regime has arrested 38 people in recent days, of whom 17 are foreigners and 21 are Venezuelans. The broadcast, without presenting evidence, said the individuals had intended to detonate explosives in Venezuelan consulates, hospitals, and public service entities, as well as to attack officials of the current Venezuelan regime, with the aim of “sabotaging” the legislative and regional elections.</p>

<p>Cabello, also without providing evidence, accused Venezuelan opposition leader María Corina Machado and Iván Simonovis Aranguren, a former political prisoner living in the United States, of participating in “conspiracy and terrorism” activities against Venezuela.</p>

<p><strong>Machado and Simonovis have not responded to Cabello’s statements and did not respond to a request for comment by the time of publication.</strong></p>

<p>The Colombian Foreign Ministry <a href="https://x.com/CancilleriaCol/status/1924577877367906719">confirmed</a> in a statement posted on social media platform X that it had received information from the Venezuelan regime to suspend general and commercial aviation flights from Colombia for national security reasons until 6 p.m. May 26. “To date, the Colombian Foreign Ministry has not received information regarding the arrest of Colombian citizens,” it said.</p>

<p><strong>LATAM Airlines Colombia announced in a <a href="https://www.latamairlines.com/co/es/prensa/comunicados/latam-airlines-colombia-informa-sobre-sus-vuelos-entre-bogota-y-caracas">statement</a> the cancellation of flights between Venezuela and Colombia from May 19 to May 26, following the Venezuelan regime’s decision.</strong></p>

<p>Another airline, Avianca, <a href="https://x.com/aviancateguia/status/1924667041564237880/photo/1">announced</a> the cancellation of flights on the Colombia–Venezuela route from May 20 to 25.</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>

Title: Supreme Court: Children Of Illegal Aliens Or Tourists Are Not U.S. Citizens
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Supreme Court: Children Of Illegal Aliens Or Tourists Are Not U.S. Citizens</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.americanthinker.com/articles/2025/05/supreme_court_children_of_illegal_aliens_or_tourists_are_not_u_s_citizens.html">Authored by Gabriel Canaan via American Thinker</a>,</em></p>

<p>On the very day Donald Trump became president again, <strong>he signed an executive order prospectively eliminating birthright citizenship for children born to aliens unlawfully present in the United States.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/gavel1.JPG?itok=xe0Y7Ydz" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/gavel1.JPG?itok=xe0Y7Ydz"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="c87b659d-a0ba-4e01-b703-9c41859759bb" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="317" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/gavel1.JPG?itok=xe0Y7Ydz" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Immediately, lawsuits were filed in a half-dozen jurisdictions across the country challenging this order.</strong></p>

<p>The groups bringing these suits claim the order disrupts long-standing legal norms governing citizenship. Yet, in fact, Trump’s contention — that birthright citizenship is not possessed by children of illegal aliens under the “correct interpretation of the law” — is exactly right.</p>

<p><strong>Birthright citizenship is conventionally understood to apply to any child born in the United States</strong>, regardless of the immigration status of that child’s parents. This view is based on the common law principle of <em>jus soli </em>(“right of soil”), which is said to be incorporated in the Citizenship Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. <strong>This understanding of the Citizenship Clause, however, despite its prevalence in academia and political commentary, is based on a mistaken and incomplete reading of controlling Supreme Court precedent.</strong></p>

<p>In fact, birthright citizenship, as provided for in the Citizenship Clause, as that clause has been authoritatively construed by the Supreme Court, is possessed only by children born in the United States to at least one parent who is lawfully residing in the United States.</p>

<p>Ratified in the aftermath of the Civil War with the aim of remedying the injustices of the <em>Dred Scott </em>decision, <strong>the Fourteenth Amendment granted citizenship to “all persons born ... in the United States, and subject to the jurisdiction thereof.”</strong> This latter phrase has been wrongly equated with “subject to the <em>laws</em> thereof,” and thus to entail that all persons born in the United States are U.S. citizens, <strong>with only a few narrow exceptions, such as children born to diplomats.</strong></p>

<p><strong>Yet the Supreme Court has construed the phrase “subject to the jurisdiction” more narrowly, most notably in seminal cases that have been taught — well or ill — in law schools ever since.</strong></p>

<p>In the 1884 case <em>Elk v. Wilkins</em>, decided when American Indians were increasingly integrating into mainstream American society, presented the constitutional issue of whether Indians who had been born within the allegiance of a tribe were “subject to the jurisdiction” of the United States at birth, and thus born American citizens under the Fourteenth Amendment.</p>

<p><strong>The Court ruled that they were not “subject to the jurisdiction” of the United States,</strong> on the ground that “jurisdiction” in the Citizenship Clause meant complete jurisdiction, which implied “direct and immediate allegiance” to the United States. The parents of children born in the allegiance of a tribe had only indirect and intermediate allegiance to the United States, through their tribe. (Today, by a subsequent act of Congress, Indians born on reservations are U.S. citizens at birth.)</p>

<p><strong>Twelve years later, in <em>Wong Kim Ark v. United States</em>, the citizenship status of an American-born man of Chinese descent was the issue.</strong></p>

<p>Wong Kim Ark had been born in San Francisco to Chinese nationals, and had been denied entry to the United States after returning from a visit to China as an adult<em>. </em>At the time, Chinese nationals were precluded by treaty from naturalizing as U.S. citizens. Nevertheless, after recounting the history of the common-law <em>jus soli</em> doctrine, and its influence on our Constitution, the Court held that, because the petitioner had been born to parents lawfully residing in the United States, he had been born within the “allegiance and protection” of the United States, and therefore at birth was “subject to the jurisdiction” of the United States<strong>. He was thus born a citizen under the Fourteenth Amendment.</strong></p>

<p>That the petitioner’s parents had resided here with the permission of the United States was central to the Court’s holding. <strong>Chinese nationals who remain “subjects of the Emperor of China…are entitled to the protection of and owe allegiance to the United States, <em>so long as they are permitted by the United States to reside</em> <em>here</em>,</strong>” the decision reads, “and are ‘subject to the jurisdiction thereof,’ in the same sense as all other aliens [lawfully] residing in the United States” (emphasis added). The Court explained that to “reside,” in this usage, means to live in a place with the intent to remain there, but not necessarily indefinitely. It is a broader category than “domiciled,” and could apply to long-term visa holders, as well as to lawful permanent residents.</p>

<p><strong>The Court’s interpretation of the Citizenship Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment thus limits its application to children of aliens residing in the country with permission.</strong> This requirement implies that children born to foreign nationals living in the country <em>without </em>permission are <em>not</em> subject to its jurisdiction, and that mere tourists, since they are only visiting and do not reside here, also are not so subject. This crucial qualification of common law birthright citizenship by the requirements of both residence and permission therefore excludes from citizenship at birth children both of tourists and of those residing in this country without permission — that is, illegal aliens.</p>

<p><strong>To disregard these requirements would involve interpreting the Court to mean that illegal aliens are within the “allegiance and protection” of the United States.</strong></p>

<p>But the Court specifically stated otherwise, holding that Chinese nationals who were not permitted to reside in the United States were not within its allegiance and protection. The Court could hardly have held otherwise. The phrase “allegiance and protection” describes the reciprocal obligations of citizens and the state that are foundational to a nation. Since illegal aliens are at all times subject to apprehension and deportation, they can hardly be regarded as within the “protection” of the United States.</p>

<p>In further evidence that <em>Wong Kim Ark </em>held that illegal aliens are not subject to the jurisdiction of the United States for citizenship purposes, the Court cited to its own earlier ruling in another immigration case, from 1893, <em>Fong Yue Ting v. United States</em>. There, the Court addressed the legal status of non-resident or unlawfully-present aliens: while they are subject to our laws, they remain outside the government’s “complete jurisdiction.” Had the Court held in <em>Wong Kim Ark </em>that all children born in the United States and subject to its laws — such as illegal aliens—were citizens, it would have run afoul of the combined holdings of <em>Elk</em> — that jurisdiction for citizenship purposes means complete jurisdiction — and of <em>Fong Yue Ting </em>— that illegal aliens and non-resident aliens are outside the complete jurisdiction of the United States. The residence and permission requirements of <em>Wong Kim Ark</em> are therefore necessary to harmonize that case with those prior cases.</p>

<p><em>Wong Kim Ark</em>’s inclusion of residence and permission requirements marks the Court’s departure from the English common law understanding of birthright citizenship in favor of one more compatible with American constitutional principles.</p>

<p>Indeed, <strong>leading constitutional scholars at the time noted that the American approach required residence while the British did not.</strong></p>

<p>The doctrine of <em>jus soli</em> as articulated by common law scholars such as Coke and Blackstone is a product of feudalism: a subject owes a duty of perpetual loyalty to the Crown under the protection of which he is born.</p>

<p>In stark contrast, the American Revolution severed the colonies’ duty to the king in favor of a compact operating by consent of the governed rather than by perpetual, unchosen duty. The purpose of the Civil Rights Act and the Fourteenth Amendment was not to reinstate the common law version of birthright citizenship; rather, it was to extend the principles of the Declaration of Independence to freed slaves and to nonwhite immigrants such as Chinese-Americans.</p>

<p>As it is currently applied, <strong>birthright citizenship not only returns us to a feudal past, but also undermines the ability of the people of the United States to set forth standards by which children born to foreign nationals may become citizens</strong>. It incentivizes “birth tourism” and mass illegal immigration, both of which treat the United States as a provider of material benefits rather than a political community towards which one owes allegiance and duties. Unlike illegal aliens and temporary guests, lawful permanent residents are incentivized to invest in their political community, and to adopt the customs and civic responsibilities of that community. Their children’s subsequent inheritance of those responsibilities further facilitates assimilation and social cohesion.</p>

<p>The rule of <em>Wong Kim Ark v. United States</em> reflects the compact approach to self-government inherent in the founding principles of this country while serving the purpose of the Fourteenth Amendment. Applying the rule as it was intended to be understood would remedy the above-mentioned policy deficiencies of an over-expansive view of birthright citizenship without the need to amend the Constitution, and efficiently resolve the flurry of lawsuits against President Trump’s executive order.</p>

<p><em>Gabriel Canaan is an attorney at the </em><a href="http://www.irli.org"><em>Immigration Reform Law Institute</em></a><em> (IRLI) in Washington, DC.  A native of Southern California, he is a graduate of William & Mary Law School, and, prior to joining IRLI, served as a law clerk on the U.S. Senate Committee on Homeland Security & Governmental Affairs.</em></p>
</div>

Title: Senate Nullifies California's Signature Gas-Car Ban, Sends Bill To Trump
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Senate Nullifies California's Signature Gas-Car Ban, Sends Bill To Trump</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>The U.S. Senate voted 51–44 to overturn California's ban on gasoline-powered vehicles by 2035, sending the measure to President Trump's desk for signature.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/GrkALekWQAAy7YS-1.png?itok=A3hagDh2" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/GrkALekWQAAy7YS-1.png?itok=A3hagDh2"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="c3933174-50ea-4477-ba2c-392e9398f099" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="285" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/GrkALekWQAAy7YS-1.png?itok=A3hagDh2" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The vote nullifies a Biden-era Environmental Protection Agency waiver that allowed California to set stricter emission standards than federal rules under the Clean Air Act. The vote also marks a significant blow to leftist climate radicals pushing de-growth green policies aimed at shaping vehicle emission standards at a national level. </p>

<p>Nearly all Democrats voted against repealing the EV mandate, except Senator Elissa Slotkin (D-Mich.), who broke ranks to support the measure—likely due to her home state's deep ties to America's legacy automakers in Detroit. Senate Majority Leader John Thune (R-S.D.) blasted the Biden-era EPA waiver, calling it an "attempt by the Biden administration to impose an electric vehicle mandate across the country." </p>

<p>As of May, eleven states, plus Washington, D.C., have adopted California's plan to phase out new gasoline-powered car sales by 2035. The new requirements faced strong opposition from the Alliance for Automotive Innovation, an auto trade group representing BMW, Ferrari, Ford, General Motors, Honda, and many other manufacturers. Also, the U.S. Chamber of Commerce argued the 2035 target was unrealistic and would harm the economy because it was de-growth in nature. </p>

<p>Republicans, led by West Virginia Senator Shelley Moore Capito, called Biden-era EPA waiver a federal overreach and a threat to consumer choice and jobs. </p>

<p>"Today, the Senate voted to end California's EV mandate and send my joint resolution of disapproval under the CRA to President Trump's desk. The Biden administration and Congressional Democrats tried to block the will of the American people from this attempt by extreme unelected California and Biden EPA bureaucrats to ban gas-powered cars throughout the country, but Congress has now spoken and soundly rejected this rule," Capito stated. </p>

<p>She continued, "The impact of California's waiver would have been felt across the country, harming multiple sectors of our economy and costing hundreds of thousands of jobs in the process. I'm proud to have led this effort to protect American workers and consumers from this radical and drastic policy." </p>

<p>Democrats in the Senate are watching key climate policies—linked to the Green New Deal—begin to unravel under President Trump's first four months in office. The rollback is evident not only in the automotive sector, with efforts to block EV mandates, but also in utilities, where fossil fuel generation is desperately needed to stabilize fragile power grids amid the surge in demand from AI data centers and overall electrification trends. </p>

<p>Environmental groups, such as the Natural Resources Defense Council, were furious with the vote, calling the move by Republicans "an unprecedented and reckless attack on states' legal authority to address the pollution causing asthma, lung disease, and heart conditions." </p>

<p>"It is going nuclear," Minority Leader Chuck Schumer said on Wednesday evening, adding this would enable MAGA Republicans to hijack the rules, erode "away at the Senate and undermine this institution they claim to care about."</p>

<p>Meanwhile, the climate change policies have sparked a number of national security threats, first being the potential for unreliable power grids, plus flooding the nation with foreign solar panels has created a major issue:</p>

<ul><li><em><a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/rogue-devices-found-hidden-chinese-solar-panels-could-destroy-grid">"Rogue" Devices Found Hidden In Chinese Solar Panels Could "Destroy The Grid"</a></em></li>
</ul><p>And risk plunging into a net-zero death like Spain several weeks ago... </p>

<ul><li><a href="https://zerohedge.com/commodities/natgas-generators-rescued-spain-net-zero-death-after-power-collapse">NatGas Generators Rescued Spain From Net Zero Death After Power Collapse</a></li>
</ul><p>All in all, the Trump administration is bringing back energy policy common sense after four years of disastrous climate change nonsense that only boosted inflation. </p>
</div>

<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-22T18:25:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/22/2025 - 14:25</span>


Title: After House Victory, Trump Tells Senate: "Get To Work" On 'Big, Beautiful Bill'
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">After House Victory, Trump Tells Senate: "Get To Work" On 'Big, Beautiful Bill'</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong>Update (0830):</strong></p>

<p>President Trump has finally weighed in with a lengthy Truth Social post after his "Big, Beautiful Bill" narrowly cleared the House in a last-minute 215–214 vote.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>"THE ONE, BIG, BEAUTIFUL BILL" has PASSED the House of Representatives! This is arguably the most significant piece of Legislation that will ever be signed in the History of our Country! The Bill includes MASSIVE Tax CUTS, No Tax on Tips, No Tax on Overtime, Tax Deductions when you purchase an American Made Vehicle, along with strong Border Security measures, Pay Raises for our ICE and Border Patrol Agents, Funding for the Golden Dome, "TRUMP Savings Accounts" for newborn babies, and much more! Great job by Speaker Mike Johnson, and the House Leadership, and thank you to every Republican who voted YES on this Historic Bill! Now, it's time for our friends in the United States Senate to get to work, and send this Bill to my desk AS SOON AS POSSIBLE! There is no time to waste. The Democrats have lost control of themselves, and are aimlessly wandering around, showing no confidence, grit, or determination. They have forgotten their landslide loss in the Presidential Election, and are warped in the past, hoping someday to revive Open Borders for the World's criminals to be able to pour into our Country, men to be able to play in women's sports, and transgender for everybody. They don't realize that these things, and so many more like them, will NEVER AGAIN happen!</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_08-26-49.png?itok=U_UXgeSm" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_08-26-49.png?itok=U_UXgeSm"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="c5346544-21d5-4e94-9e6e-7eb27f3c428d" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="293" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-22_08-26-49.png?itok=U_UXgeSm" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p> </p>

<p>*   *   * </p>

<p>President Donald Trump's multi-trillion-dollar tax package—also known as the "Big, Beautiful Bill"—cleared the House in a <strong>last-minute 215–214 vote on Thursday morning</strong>. The bill now moves to the Senate, where Republicans are calling for major revisions ahead of an expected vote in August. It aims to prevent a year-end tax hike and a potential debt default but would significantly increase the near-term federal deficit.</p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>The <strong>215-214 House vote, with one abstention,</strong> was met with loud cheers by House Republicans. <strong>Some of the key provisions include</strong>:</p>

<ul><li>
	<p><em>Extension of Trump-era tax cuts and new relief, such as exempting tips and overtime from taxation.</em></p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><em>The state and local tax (SALT) deduction cap will be increased to $40,000, with phase-outs for high earners.</em></p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><em>Cuts to safety-net programs such as Medicaid and food stamps, alongside new work requirements starting in December 2026.</em></p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><em>Rollbacks on clean energy tax credits, boosting fossil fuel incentives. </em></p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><em>Major increases in military and border security spending.</em></p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><em>New taxes targeting elite universities (e.g., Harvard and other Ivy Leagues) and immigrant remittances.</em></p>
	</li>
	<li>
	<p><em>The elimination of EV tax credits, replaced by interest deductions on U.S.-built vehicle loans</em></p>
	</li>
</ul><p>It is interesting to note that Reps. Warren Davidson of Ohio and Thomas Massie of Kentucky were the only Republicans to vote against the Big, Beautiful Bill. They warned about mounting deficits that would result if the bill were passed. </p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p><strong>In the bond market</strong>, the US 30-year Treasury yield moved higher after the bill narrowly passed the House, hitting 5.12%, the highest level since October 2023. This level is nearing its highest point since 2007. </p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/bfmE665.jpg?itok=dhAFB1fY" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/bfmE665.jpg?itok=dhAFB1fY"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a5622e4d-a6c0-4e44-9018-9d6c1555dfdb" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="290" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/bfmE665.jpg?itok=dhAFB1fY" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>With Treasury yields soaring, perhaps it's time for Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent to fire up the "big toolkit"...</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_07-35-20.png?itok=QZo9ipY9" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_07-35-20.png?itok=QZo9ipY9"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="f6598391-d81e-442a-9b21-d5bd1d741e42" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="159" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-22_07-35-20.png?itok=QZo9ipY9" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Rep. Nathaniel Moran (R., Texas) stated: "<strong>This bill is our opportunity to deliver on the promises we made. At its core, the one big, beautiful bill is about more than dollars and cents. It's about liberty and empowering the American people</strong>."</p>

<p>The Wall Street Journal noted,<strong> "Republicans are aiming to get the bill to Trump's desk by July 4. The real deadline might be a bit later." </strong></p>

<p>Democrats blasted the bill as taking money away from the social safety net to fund tax cuts for the wealthy...</p>

<p>"It's really one big broken promise," said Rep. Suzan DelBene (D., Wash.), adding, "Republicans have spent months fighting over how many Americans they’re going to kick off Medicaid and how fast."</p>

Title: Trump Admin Blocks Harvard From Enrolling International Students, Requires Current Foreign Students To Transfer 'Or Lose Legal Status'
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Trump Admin Blocks Harvard From Enrolling International Students, Requires Current Foreign Students To Transfer 'Or Lose Legal Status'</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Harvard is having a really bad year. From feds <a href="https://hsph.harvard.edu/news/trump-administration-freezes-2-2-billion-in-grants-to-harvard/">yanking</a> billions in <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/harvard-hammered-feds-yank-additional-450-million-grants">grants</a>, to House Republicans alleging <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/house-republicans-press-harvard-transparency-over-alleged-ties-chinese-military">ties to the Chinese military</a>, to President Trump threatening their tax-exempt status, to detained <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/russian-born-harvard-scientist-detained-us-charged-smuggling-clawed-frog-embryos">embryo-smuggling</a> scientists (and most of that's just this month), <strong>the university has now been blocked from enrolling international students - which constitute <a href="https://www.highereddive.com/news/will-harvard-lose-its-ability-to-enroll-foreign-students/745674/?utm_source=chatgpt.com">nearly 1/3</a> of Harvard admissions. </strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Harvard-University-1a_1.jpg?itok=8Itd1Zap" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Harvard-University-1a_1.jpg?itok=8Itd1Zap"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="ac6cb547-03da-405b-9009-158d38afcac6" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="332" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Harvard-University-1a_1.jpg?itok=8Itd1Zap" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>"I am writing to inform you that <strong>effective immediately, Harvard University’s Student and Exchange Visitor Program certification is revoked</strong>," according to a letter sent to the university by DHS Secretary Kristi Noem, which they promptly shot over to the <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2025/05/22/us/politics/trump-harvard-international-students.html?searchResultPosition=1"><em>NY Times</em></a>. The university has <strong>72 hours to hand over requested information.</strong></p>

<p>The decision followed a back-and-forth in recent days over the legality of a wide-ranging records request by the Department of Homeland Security.</p>

<p>According to <em>Bloomberg</em>, <strong>existing foreign students must transfer or lose their legal status, </strong>the notice reads.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">This administration is holding Harvard accountable for fostering violence, antisemitism, and coordinating with the Chinese Communist Party on its campus.<br /><br />
It is a privilege, not a right, for universities to enroll foreign students and benefit from their higher tuition payments… <a href="https://t.co/12hJWd1J86">pic.twitter.com/12hJWd1J86</a></p>
— Secretary Kristi Noem (@Sec_Noem) <a href="https://twitter.com/Sec_Noem/status/1925612991703052733?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 22, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>In April DHS threatened to block Harvard from enrolling international students if the university refused to hand over detailed records about the student body containing "relevant information" on student visa holders who have been involved in "known illegal" or "dangerous" activity.</p>

<p>"<strong>It is a privilege to have foreign students attend Harvard University, not a guarantee,</strong>" Noem wrote in an April <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2025/04/17/us/harvard-letter-signed.html">letter</a>. "The United States government understands that Harvard University relies heavily on foreign student funding from over 10,000 foreign students to build and maintain their substantial endowment."</p>

<p><strong>Harvard dug in last month </strong>following the Trump admin's demands - with president Alan Garber saying in a statement "No government — regardless of which party is in power — should dictate what private universities can teach, whom they can admit and hire, and which areas of study and inquiry they can pursue."</p>

<h2>Not So Fast?</h2>

<p>Concurrently, a federal judge in California has blocked the Trump administration from terminating the legal status of international students nationwide while a court case challenging previous terminations is pending.</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>The order by U.S. District Judge Jeffrey S. White in Oakland <strong>bars the government from arresting or incarcerating the plaintiffs and similarly situated students</strong>; from transferring any of them outside the jurisdiction of their residence; from imposing any adverse legal effect on students and from reversing the reinstatement of the legal status until the case is resolved. Students can still be arrested for violent crimes. -<a href="https://apnews.com/article/students-trump-administration-arrest-deportation-7fc4cb9ebc1b10d3ec0d564313067846">AP</a></em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>According to White, the government's actions "wreaked havoc not only on the lives of Plaintiffs here but on similarly situated F-1 nonimmigrants across the United States and continues do so."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/zerohedge-waxed-canvas-hat/?m=direct" data-image-href="https://store.zerohedge.com/zerohedge-waxed-canvas-hat/?m=direct" data-link-option="2" href="https://store.zerohedge.com/zerohedge-waxed-canvas-hat/?m=direct"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="6f333567-346b-483f-aa99-58e864b2db8d" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="224" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/hats%20back%20in%20stock_4.png?itok=yc7ylThV" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Read Noem's letter below (emphasis ours):</p>

<blockquote>
<p><strong>Harvard's Student and Exchange Visitor Program Decertification</strong></p>

<p>I am writing to inform you that effective immediately, Harvard University's Student and Exchange Visitor Program certification is revoked.</p>

<p><strong>As I explained to you in my April letter, it is a privilege to enroll foreign students</strong>, and it is also a privilege to employ aliens on campus. All universities must comply with Department of Homeland Security requirements, including reporting requirements under the Student and Exchange Visitor Program regulations, to maintain this privilege. As a result of your refusal to comply with multiple requests to provide the Department of Homeland Security pertinent information while perpetuating an unsafe campus environment that is hostile to Jewish students, promotes pro-llamas sympathies, and employs racist "diversity, equity, and inclusion" policies, you have lost this privilege.</p>

<p>The revocation of your Student and Exchange Visitor Program certification means that <strong>Harvard is prohibited from having any aliens on F- or J- nonimmigrant status for the 2025-2026 academic school year</strong>. This decertification also means that <strong>existing aliens on F- or J- nonimmigrant status must transfer to another university in order to maintain their nonimmigrant status.</strong></p>

<p>This action should not surprise you and is the unfortunate result of Harvard's failure to comply with simple reporting requirements.</p>

<p><strong>On April 16, 2025, I requested records</strong> pertaining to nonimmigrant students enrolled at Harvard University, including information regarding misconduct and other offenses that would render foreign students inadmissible or removable. On April 30, 2025, Harvard's counsel provided information that he represented as responsive to my request. It was not.</p>

<p>As a courtesy that Harvard was not legally entitled to, the Acting DHS General Counsel responded on my behalf and afforded Harvard another opportunity to comply. Harvard again provided an insufficient response.</p>

<p><strong>Consequences must follow to send a clear signal to Harvard and all universities that want to enjoy the privilege of enrolling foreign students, that the Trump Administration will enforce the law and root out the evils of anti-Americanism and antisemitism in society and campuses.</strong></p>

<p>If Harvard would like the opportunity of regaining Student and Exchange Visitor Program certification before the upcoming academic school year, you must provide all of the information requested below <strong>within 72 hours.</strong></p>

<p><strong>Please be</strong> advised that providing materially false, fictitious, or fraudulent information may subject you to criminal prosecution under 18 U.S.C. § 1001. Other criminal and civil sanctions may also apply.</p>

<p><strong>I expect full and complete responses to the following requests:</strong></p>

<ol><li>Any and all records, whether official or informal, in the possession of Harvard University, including electronic records and audio or video footage, regarding illegal activity whether on or off campus, by a nonimmigrant student enrolled in Harvard University in the last five years.</li>
	<li>Any and all records, whether official or informal, in the possession of Harvard University, including electronic records and audio or video footage, regarding dangerous or violent activity whether on or off campus, by a nonimmigrant student enrolled in Harvard University in the last five years.</li>
	<li>Any and all records, whether official or informal, in the possession of Harvard University, including electronic records and audio or video footage, regarding threats to other students or university personnel whether on or off campus, by a nonimmigrant student enrolled in Harvard University in the last five years.</li>
	<li>Any and all records, whether official or informal, in the possession of Harvard University, including electronic records and audio or video footage, regarding deprivation of rights of other classmates or university personnel whether on or off campus, by a nonimmigrant student enrolled in Harvard University in the last five years.</li>
	<li>Any and all disciplinary records of all nonimmigrant students enrolled in Harvard University in the last five years.</li>
	<li>Any and all audio or video footage, in the possession of Harvard University, of any protest activity involving a nonimmigrant student on a Harvard University campus in the last five years.</li>
</ol></blockquote>

<p><em>Developing...</em></p>

<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-22T18:12:52+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/22/2025 - 14:12</span>


Title: COVID Vaccine "Safe and Effective" Narrative Collapses On Camera
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">COVID Vaccine "Safe and Effective" Narrative Collapses On Camera</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.vigilantfox.com/p/covid-vaccine-safe-and-effective">Authored by The Vigilant Fox via vigilantfox.com</a>,</em></p>

<p>The “safe and effective” narrative collapsed on camera during Senator Ron Johnson’s <strong><a href="https://x.com/i/broadcasts/1rmxPyqrLMYKN">explosive Senate hearing</a></strong> on COVID-19 vaccine injuries Wednesday afternoon.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2Ff99e1a71-e1e3-40d2-a7f0-516d60983bf6_4000x2250_png_92.jpg?itok=klK27Ezl" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2Ff99e1a71-e1e3-40d2-a7f0-516d60983bf6_4000x2250_png_92.jpg?itok=klK27Ezl"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="c2652d87-2075-49b4-ab33-807d44cee3e1" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2Ff99e1a71-e1e3-40d2-a7f0-516d60983bf6_4000x2250_png_92.jpg?itok=klK27Ezl" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p><strong>Senator Ron Johnson brought the receipts, exposing how the Biden administration DELIBERATELY hid vaccine harms from the public.</strong></p>

<p>Then Dr. James Thorp (OB-GYN) revealed miscarriage data so disturbing, it left the room silent.</p>

<p>This is the Senate hearing they never wanted you to see.<strong> I turned <a href="https://x.com/i/broadcasts/1rmxPyqrLMYKN">three hours of footage</a> into a five-minute read.</strong></p>

<p>Senator Ron Johnson opened the hearing with a bombshell: the Biden administration knew about deadly heart risks tied to the COVID shots, and deliberately kept it from the public.</p>

<p>Johnson released newly subpoenaed records exposing a detailed timeline of what officials knew and when. While Pfizer and Moderna received insider updates, doctors and citizens who raised concerns were silenced.</p>

<p>In February 2021, Israeli health officials warned the CDC of “large reports of myocarditis, particularly in young people” following Pfizer injections, just two and a half months after the vaccine received emergency use authorization.</p>

<p><strong>By April, the CDC was already reviewing myocarditis data from Israel and the Department of Defense. But instead of alerting the public, they stayed quiet.</strong></p>

<p>By the end of that month, VAERS had recorded 2,926 deaths, nearly half of which occurred within three days of injection. “Somebody ought to be looking at it,” Johnson said.</p>

<p>In May, the CDC considered issuing a formal health alert—but scrapped it. They replaced it with watered-down guidance that removed a key warning for doctors to restrict physical activity in myocarditis patients.</p>

<p>Francis Collins, then director of the NIH, brushed it all off. “Senator, people die,” he told Johnson.</p>

<p>In just six months, the toll was staggering: 384,270 reports of adverse events, 4,812 deaths, and 1,736 of those occurred within just <strong>48 hours of injection</strong>.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">BREAKING: The Biden administration KNEW about deadly heart risks from COVID shots and DELIBERATELY kept it from the public.<br /><br />
Sen. Ron Johnson just released subpoenaed records exposing a damning timeline of what officials knew and when.<br /><br />
Pfizer and Moderna got insider updates from… <a href="https://t.co/od4fqSiaUh">pic.twitter.com/od4fqSiaUh</a></p>
— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1925257764252918239?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 21, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Dr. Peter McCullough then took the floor and upended the narrative that vaccine-induced myocarditis is “rare.”</p>

<p>Before COVID, McCullough had seen just two myocarditis cases in his entire career. After the rollout, everything changed.</p>

<p><strong>He says he’s now “examined thousands of patients with this problem.”</strong></p>

<p>“There’s 1,065 papers in the peer-reviewed literature on COVID vaccine myocarditis,” he explained, pointing to a 2021 case published in the New England Journal of Medicine. A 42-year-old man developed vaccine-induced myocarditis. “The infection is ruled out,” McCullough said. “It’s the vaccine.” Three days after his Moderna shot, the man was dead.</p>

<p><strong>McCullough cited a shocking case from Korea</strong>—a young man who died within eight hours of hospitalization after a Pfizer shot. His heart had been, in McCullough’s words, “fried with inflammation.”</p>

<p>Then came a case from Connecticut: two teenage boys, 16 and 17, died in their sleep just days after Pfizer. Their parents found them unresponsive.</p>

<p>“These cases… should have gotten everyone’s attention,” McCullough said. “We should never have someone die after taking a vaccine that’s directly caused to the vaccine.”</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">

— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1925262894498750696?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 21, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Alabama-based physician Dr. Jordan Vaughn followed up with a chilling estimate—up to 15 million Americans may be suffering from long COVID or COVID vaccine injuries.</p>

<p>He now treats teenagers who can’t stand up and previously healthy adults who are suffering strokes with no clear cause.</p>

<p><strong>According to Vaughn, the spike protein’s S1 subunit is far from harmless. “It triggers inflammation, it disrupts endothelial barriers, it induces fibrin resistant to breakdown, and it promotes a lot of amyloid aggregates,” he said.</strong></p>

<p>These effects impair oxygen delivery, damage blood vessels, and trigger a wave of symptoms—racing heart, brain fog, shortness of breath, and post-exertional crashes.</p>

<p>In his clinic, Vaughn uses immunofluorescent microscopy to detect the spike protein’s damage, showing up in patients who were once thriving.</p>

<p>He warned that the mRNA injections led to uncontrolled spike protein production, which spread throughout the body, reaching the heart, brain, ovaries, and testes.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">REPORT: Up to 15 MILLION Americans may be suffering from the devastating effects of the COVID shots, says Alabama-based physician Dr. Jordan Vaughn.<br /><br />
In his clinic, he now sees teenagers who can’t stand and previously healthy adults suffering strokes with no identifiable cause.… <a href="https://t.co/sngD0F6COL">pic.twitter.com/sngD0F6COL</a></p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Regulators claimed the vaccine stayed in the arm. That was a lie. A Yale study now shows some people are still producing spike protein <a href="https://news.yale.edu/2025/02/19/immune-markers-post-vaccination-syndrome-indicate-future-research-directions">more than 700 days after their last injection</a>.</p>

<p>We didn’t just inject people. We turned them into spike protein factories.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F4a3a57c1-3b93-4046-bd4e-533282d24ed3_3354x2712_png_92.jpg?itok=Ns3M3Vxx" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F4a3a57c1-3b93-4046-bd4e-533282d24ed3_3354x2712_png_92.jpg?itok=Ns3M3Vxx"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="9b61b91d-0f55-4ed9-a4a5-ef9227fa1778" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="404" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F4a3a57c1-3b93-4046-bd4e-533282d24ed3_3354x2712_png_92.jpg?itok=Ns3M3Vxx" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>OB-GYN Dr. James Thorp delivered one of the most haunting moments of the hearing.</p>

<p>He said the COVID shots “<strong>MIRRORED</strong>” the effects of chemical abortion drugs—and the government knew what it was doing.</p>

<p>Dr. Thorp pointed to the now-infamous Shimabukuro study published in the New England Journal of Medicine, which claimed a 12.6% miscarriage rate following COVID vaccination.</p>

<p>But when you isolate the data for women vaccinated in the first trimester, the miscarriage rate rises to 82%, Dr. Thorp said. This 82% claim remains a topic of debate within the scientific community.</p>

<p>If true, “<strong>This figure mirrors the effects of chemical abort drugs</strong>,” Dr. Thorp lamented.</p>

— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1925343525660401833?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 22, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>He added, “Recently, animal studies revealed the mRNA COVID vaccine causes the destruction of <strong><a href="https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC12031016/">60 PERCENT of the ovarian reserve in rats</a></strong>.”</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F695c0d80-d040-4488-bd69-0bb1d4e3ba01_1562x842_png_92.jpg?itok=ISp-h05V" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F695c0d80-d040-4488-bd69-0bb1d4e3ba01_1562x842_png_92.jpg?itok=ISp-h05V"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0b25f267-85c7-46d5-98e2-65c20448c624" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="270" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F695c0d80-d040-4488-bd69-0bb1d4e3ba01_1562x842_png_92.jpg?itok=ISp-h05V" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>If that effect translates to humans, it could be a catastrophic blow to fertility and the future of entire generations.</p>

<p>Dr. Thorp said pregnant women were deliberately targeted, and their unborn children paid the price.</p>

<p>“This must stop now,” he said.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F16eca6c0-27d6-489f-ba96-f5a7d057c5b1_876x770_png_92.jpg?itok=qyrogzE9" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F16eca6c0-27d6-489f-ba96-f5a7d057c5b1_876x770_png_92.jpg?itok=qyrogzE9"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="56470deb-3cab-4fe0-bc1d-0aaf12bab910" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="439" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/https-3A-2F-2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com-2Fpublic-2Fimages-2F16eca6c0-27d6-489f-ba96-f5a7d057c5b1_876x770_png_92.jpg?itok=qyrogzE9" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Attorney Aaron Siri then delivered a little-known history lesson on vaccine liability.</p>

<p>“For every product on the market, you can SUE the manufacturer for harm,” Siri said. “There’s only ONE product in America you CANNOT sue the manufacturer to claim it could have been made safer—and that’s VACCINES.”</p>

<p>He explained how the 1986 National Childhood Vaccine Injury Act gave pharmaceutical companies sweeping immunity, not just for three vaccines, but for every new childhood shot added to the CDC schedule.</p>

<p>The result? A schedule that exploded from 3 shots to 29 in the first year of life, with zero accountability.</p>

<p>“They don’t have the financial incentive to make them safer,” Siri said. “In fact, they have the disincentive.”</p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Senator Ron Johnson confronted Hawaii Gov. Josh Green, who was defending the COVID jabs at the hearing.</p>

<p>“<strong>I could fill this room with photos of people who are DEAD because of the COVID injection</strong>,” Johnson said. “I could fill the room,” he reiterated.</p>

<p>He made the comment after calling out how the vaccine-injured are still being ignored, gaslit, and denied care.</p>

<p>Johnson pointed to VAERS data showing 38,607 reported deaths after the shot, 9,228 of them within two days.</p>

<p>Multiply that by a conservative underreporting factor of 10, and the death toll climbs to <strong>over 386,000</strong>.</p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Dr. Peter McCullough delivered one of the most powerful moments of the hearing.</p>

<p>Senator Blumenthal had previously claimed the COVID vaccines “saved three million lives.”</p>

<p>Dr. McCullough quickly dismantled that false narrative. He delivered a three-part reality check on what actually brought COVID deaths down:</p>

<p><strong>1. Natural immunity did the heavy lifting.</strong></p>

<p><strong>2. Early treatment kept people out of hospitals.</strong></p>

<p><strong>3. The virus mutated into a milder form.</strong></p>

<p>“The vaccine cannot be falsely credited with saving millions of lives,” McCullough said.</p>

<p>“We can’t allow false drug advertising to be put up on a poster behind one of our public servants. We cannot accept that.”</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-conversation="none">

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Sen. Ron Johnson delivered another crushing blow to the “safe and effective” narrative—this time with a devastating chart that exposed that lie.</p>

<p>The chart showed that one of the biggest spikes in COVID cases and deaths occurred <em><strong>AFTER</strong></em> the vaccine rollout began in December 2020.</p>

<p>By mid-2021, over half the U.S. was “fully vaccinated.” But instead of improving, the numbers got worse.</p>

<p>If the vaccine had worked, cases and deaths would have dropped. They didn’t—and this chart makes that impossible to ignore.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-media-max-width="560">

— The Vigilant Fox 🦊 (@VigilantFox) <a href="https://twitter.com/VigilantFox/status/1925345273804652953?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 22, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Sensing the narrative was slipping, Senator Richard Blumenthal (D-Connecticut) scrambled to defend public health officials.</p>

<p>He became visibly agitated at the suggestion that vaccine risks had been covered up.</p>

<p>“I may be sounding a little bit like a lawyer, not a physician, but purposeful concealment, intentional hiding, is essentially undocumented by the evidence released by this report itself,” Blumenthal said.</p>

<p>He brushed off the myocarditis concerns as “rare” and insisted that officials like Rochelle Walensky took “multiple steps” to warn the public.</p>

<p>So his message quietly shifted from “safe and effective” to “<strong>We did our best with what we knew at the time</strong>,” a clear sign that the vaccine narrative is running out of ground to stand on.</p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Vaccine-injured physician Dr. Joel Wallskog captured the pain of the vaccine-injured better than anyone.</p>

<p>“If I could describe one word that I think all, if not most, vaccine-injured will say… it’s <strong>ABANDONMENT</strong>.”</p>

<p>He explained how people like him have been attacked from both sides.</p>

<p>“The right says we’re stupid… the left calls us anti-vaxxers, which is one of the most ignorant things to say.”</p>

<p>He reminded the room that he was injured because he got vaccinated.</p>

<p>Dr. Wallskog and vaccine-injured associate Brianne Dressen met multiple times with FDA vaccine chief Dr. Peter Marks over two years.</p>

<p>“We have been placated, we have been blown off,” he said. “He thanks us, he says he’ll get back to us… <strong>he never does</strong>.”</p>

<p>Dr. Wallskog added that the idea that federal agencies are trying to help is “the farthest from the truth.”</p>

<p><strong>【12:08】</strong></p>
<p>恒生生物科技指数午盘收涨1.89%。医药板块活跃，昭衍新药涨超10%，泰格医药涨13%，康龙化成涨7%，药明康德涨2.76%。荣昌生物再涨超4%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/141f1291-ac93-4162-90d9-168dbf33d2cb.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="394" data-wscnw="798"/></p>
<p>消息面，据<span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/eeBRWI-2eMPTfiJ3ix02Hg" target="_blank" rel="noopener">券商中国</a></span>，百济神州、科伦博泰生物、亚盛医药等多家创新药企业宣布将在5月30日至6月3日举办的2025年美国临床肿瘤学会(ASCO)年会上展示创新药物研究成果。ASCO年会是世界上规模最大、学术水平最高、最具权威性的临床肿瘤学会议，被认为是行业风向标，受到全球医药行业和投资者关注。</p>
<p>另外，恒瑞医药在港上市首日的亮眼表现也提振了市场信心。今日早盘，恒瑞医药H股一度暴涨超37%，截至午间收盘，涨幅仍达30.87%。</p>

<p>还有分析称，受益于三生制药与辉瑞达成的PD-1/VEGF双抗SSGJ-707全球权益合作的消息催化，中国创新药企通过技术授权加速融入全球产业链，市场对于国产创新药出海预期被放大。</p>
<p>中航证券认为，国产创新药板块展现出显著的投资价值。在创新药企业出海持续推进的背景下，国内创新药行业正经历深刻变化，企业核心优势不断叠加，持续强化自身竞争力，逐步从创新追随者转变为国际竞争中的重要力量，并从国内市场走向国际舞台。</p>

Title:  鸿鹄二期资金落地，新华保险公告出资100亿元 
Description:  <p>新华保险最新披露对外投资进展。</p>
<p>2025年5月22日，新华保险出资100亿元认购国丰兴华鸿鹄志远二期私募证券投资基金（以下简称“鸿鹄基金”）的份额。</p>
<p>鸿鹄基金是新华保险与中国人寿共同出资成立的私募产品，基金管理方是国丰兴华私募，同样也是两家险资巨头出资成立的私募平台，专注于二级市场投资。</p>
<p>鸿鹄基金自2024年正式开始以来，成为险资加大中国股票投资的新模式，突破了以往通过保费产品组合、险企自有资金直接投资的方式。</p>
<h2>签订鸿鹄二期合同</h2>
<p>据公告，新华保险与基金管理人国丰兴华及基金托管人广发银行股份有限公司北京分行签署《国丰兴华鸿鹄志远二期私募证券投资基金基金合同》。</p>
<p>根据基金合同，上述二期基金成立规模为200亿元，本公司出资100亿元认购私募基金份额。</p>
<p>结合此前公告，鸿鹄基金二期的认购方穿透后是新华保险旗下的新华资产管理公司，亦有中国人寿旗下的国寿资产管理公司。</p>
<p>基金管理费率为0.10%/年，托管费率为0.002%/年。</p>
<p>上述最新公告标志着，鸿鹄基金二期的资金已经到位，“入市”箭在弦上。</p>
<h2>“入市”买什么资产</h2>
<p>资事堂梳理新华保险历史公告，这家险资曾透露鸿鹄基金二期的投资方向：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“通过低频交易、长期持有的方式以获得稳健股息收益，提升长期投资回报，实现资金保值增值······中证A500指数成分股中符合条件的大型上市公司A+H股。标的公司应当公司治理良好、经营运作稳健、股息相对稳定、股票流动性相对较好，与保险资金长期投资需求相适应”。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>另据公告，上述私募基金存续期限为10年，按照基金合同约定履行相应变更手续后，私募基金存续期限可以相应延长。</p>
<h2>险资巨头联手</h2>
<p>2024年一季度，鸿鹄基金正式成立，第一期规模为500亿元人民币，中国人寿和新华保险各出资500亿元，投资方向是具有较大市值、流动性好以及较高市场影响力的优质上市公司。</p>
<p>实际上，大型险企正在不断推进保险资金投资的改革。</p>
<p>5月22日，金融监管总局新闻发言人、政策研究司司长郭武平在国新办新闻发布会上表示，保险资金长期投资改革试点的首批试点规模为500亿元，第二批试点为1120亿元，最近还要做第三批600亿元的批复，规模合计为2220亿元。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:   结怨特朗普，股价跌跌不休，苹果“摊上事儿了” 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">特朗普公开批评苹果CEO Tim Cook在美国境外建厂之际，苹果股价连续七个交易日下跌。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据彭博5月23日报道，特朗普本月表示他“与Tim Cook之间有一点小问题”，并声称曾要求苹果停止在印度建设工厂。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">与此同时，特朗普曾公开赞扬英伟达CEO出席了沙特投资论坛，但Tim Cook并未出席这场活动。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">特朗普与Tim Cook的“矛盾”或已对苹果股价造成冲击。五月初苹果还是全球市值最高的公司，但目前已跌至第三位。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">美东时间5月23日，苹果股价收跌0.36%，延续七连跌颓势，市值较月初蒸发逾3000亿美元，将全球市值王座拱手让与微软、英伟达。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/2709bafe-ef03-463a-9928-9075f893e399.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="488" data-wscnw="687"/></p>

<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">特朗普不断针对苹果并似乎对他们有所不满，这对我来说是个危险信号。这并不意味着特朗普会采取进一步行动，但你无法预测接下来会发生什么，这让我保持谨慎。</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">值得注意的是，苹果还面临AI军备竞赛掉队风险、中国市场增长乏力等压力。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">日前，OpenAI宣布收购苹果前首席设计师艾维的AI硬件初创公司，加剧压垮市场对苹果的信心。分析师普遍认为，苹果在生成式AI领域布局滞后，核心产品线面临颠覆风险。CBOE苹果波动率指数虽从月内高点回落38%，但仍处近三年高位，显示市场对其转型能力的质疑。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">此外，苹果最新财报显示，<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3746413" target="_blank" rel="noopener">来自大中华区的营收为160.02亿美元同比下降2.26%</a>，叠加中国本土品牌崛起，Tim Cook“东线战略”遭遇严峻考验。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  美债下跌何时会冲击美股？很近了 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">据高盛最新分析，当10年期美债收益率收益率在一个月内上涨约60个基点达到4.75-4.80%时，股市可能面临重大压力。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">5月23日周五，美股期货在盘前交易中继续走低，延续了昨日美债拍卖后的大幅下跌态势。这一走势与今晨美国国债收益率的上涨相互呼应。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">数据显示，美债收益率在参议院通过特朗普“大漂亮法案（One Big Beautiful Bill）”后明显攀升。10年期美债收益率现处于4.520%水平附近。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/a194b8ec-b8dc-420a-861a-37b2ac4583fb.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="345" data-wscnw="500"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/aa201e1f-0310-4d13-ab0a-8b2455935c2b.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="290" data-wscnw="500"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">而日本债券市场的动荡和英国通胀数据走高进一步推高了全球收益率。在这一背景下，投资者最关心的问题变得非常简单：股市何时会开始对债券收益率上涨产生反应？</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []"><strong>根据高盛的分析，答案是：就是现在！</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>该行研究发现，当10年期美债收益率在一个月内上涨2个标准差，即收益率在一个月内上涨约60个基点达到4.75-4.80%时，或将冲击股市。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">从历史上看，影响股市的并非只有收益率的绝对水平，重要的还有上涨速度。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">这意味着如果当前美债收益率的上涨趋势持续，可能很快就会达到影响股市的临界水平。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/dee2f204-edef-4b0f-bfe9-ea781366a476.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="300" data-wscnw="500"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">换句话说，我们已经非常接近临界点。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>

Title: Trump administration finds Columbia violated Jewish students' civil rights
Description: <p><a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/05/03/columbia-investigation-education-department" target="_blank">Columbia University</a> violated federal civil-rights law by "acting with deliberate indifference towards student-on-student harassment of Jewish students" from <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/10/07/october-7-anniversary-israel-hamas-gaza-war" target="_blank">Oct. 7</a>, 2023, through the present, a Trump administration investigation found Thursday.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>The college was last year an epicenter for <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/04/30/columbia-protestors-expulsion-occupied-building" target="_self">students protesting</a> the <a href="https://www.axios.com/world/israel" target="_blank">Israel</a>-Hamas war and the <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">Trump</a> administration announced in March it was <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/07/trump-columbia-antisemitism-protests-federal-money" target="_blank">pulling some $400 million</a> in federal grants and contracts over its dissatisfaction at Columbia's response to antisemitism allegations.</p><hr><ul><li>"We understand this finding is part of our ongoing discussions with the government," a Columbia spokesperson said in an emailed statement.</li><li>"Columbia is deeply committed to combatting antisemitism and all forms of harassment and discrimination on our campus. We take these issues seriously and will work with the Department of Health and Human Services and the Department of Education to address them."</li></ul><p><strong>Details: </strong>An investigation found that Columbia violated Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, which protects against discrimination on the basis of race, color, or national origin, per Thursday <a href="https://www.hhs.gov/press-room/ocr-columbia-violates-federal-civil-rights-law.html" target="_blank">statement</a> from the Department of Health and Human Services' civil-rights office.</p><ul><li>Among the findings were that Columbia allegedly failed to "investigate or punish vandalism in its classrooms, which include the repeated drawing of swastikas and other universally recognized hate images."</li><li>No fresh action against Columbia was announced following the investigation findings.</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying: </strong>"The findings carefully document the hostile environment Jewish students at Columbia University have had to endure for over 19 months, disrupting their education, safety, and well-being," said Anthony Archeval, Acting Director of the Office for Civil Rights at HHS, in a statement. </p><ul><li>"We encourage Columbia University to work with us to come to an agreement that reflects meaningful changes that will truly protect Jewish students."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>The Trump administration <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/17/universities-trump-harvard-columbia" target="_blank">has targeted</a> educational institutions, <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/16/harvard-columbia-demands-trump-vision-universities-influence" target="_self">pressuring universities</a> to meet its demands or risk losing funding and tax-exempt status, Axios' <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/22/harvard-warning-universities-noem-dhs" target="_blank">Sareen Habeshian notes</a>.</p><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a "That's why I believe that it should not go forward, and if it does, it does, it should not be done electronically or over mail."</li><li>Kenyatta said at the meeting that he "fundamentally" believes that the election was fair.</li></ul><p><strong>What's next: </strong>If most DNC members vote to redo the election, there will be an electronic vote for a male vice chair on June 12-14 and an any gender vote for a second vice chair, according to a timeline shared at the meeting.</p><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/18/house-democrats-david-hogg-primary-dnc" target="_blank">House Democrats fume at David Hogg's plan to oust lawmakers</a></p><p><em>Editor's note: Axios' Andrew Solender contributed reporting.</em></p>

Title: Scoop: Primary challengers circle Thomas Massie after Trump-defying vote
Description: <p>President Trump's political operation has been fielding calls from Republicans interested in waging a primary challenge to Kentucky Rep. <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/nrcc-trump-hudson-republican-primaries" target="_blank">Thomas Massie</a>, according to a person familiar with the talks.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The conversations are evidence that Trump — and his <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/10/trump-maga-inc-power-fundraising" target="_blank">$500 million political apparatus</a> — is actively entertaining the best way to back a primary opponent against Massie, who has drawn Trump's ire for voting against his "one big, beautiful bill."</p><hr><ul><li>"Massie is about to be in the fight of his life," said Kentucky-based GOP strategist Jake Cox. "Just wait until he sees the money a Trump-backed candidate can raise simply from the President saying their name into a camera or opening up his email list."</li><li>Two possible primary challengers being mentioned in Kentucky Republican circles are state Sen. Aaron Reed and state Rep. Kimberly Moser.</li><li>A statewide Kentucky GOP official tells Axios: "Massie has had weak primary opponents in previous cycles and made mincemeat of them, but I think this time is different. Supporting Trump is the No. 1 — and sometimes the only — issue in GOP primaries at the moment."</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying:</strong> Trump has privately wondered what the point is of having a Republican in Massie's seat if "they're going to vote with Democrats and trash Republicans all the time."</p><ul><li>Trump's anger boiled on Tuesday, when he told reporters in the Capitol that the congressman should be "<a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/trump-house-republicans-medicaid-salt" target="_blank">voted out of office</a>."</li><li>The president's political lieutenants piled on. "Some guys just prefer to be in the minority," White House deputy chief of staff James Blair said of Massie on X.</li><li>When asked during a Thursday briefing whether Trump believed — as well as Rep. Warren Davidson (R-Ohio), who also voted "no" — should be primaried, White House press secretary Karoline Leavitt responded: "I believe he does and I believe he does not like to see grandstanders in Congress."</li></ul><p><strong>The background: </strong>Massie and Trump have clashed for years.</p><ul><li>In 2019, Massie joined House Democrats in opposing Trump's declaration of a national emergency at the southern border.</li><li>After Massie opposed a COVID relief package in 2020, Trump called on the congressman to be thrown "out of the Republican Party."</li><li>Massie was one of six House Republicans to endorse Florida Gov. Ron DeSantis over Trump during the 2024 Republican presidential primary.</li><li>After Massie opposed a Trump-backed government spending bill in March, Trump wrote on Truth Social that the congressman was a "GRANDSTANDER."</li></ul><p><strong>Behind the scenes: </strong>During the transition, Trump privately asked DeSantis for advice on how to deal with Massie.</p><ul><li>"Give him raw milk," DeSantis said, referring to one of Massie's <a href="https://massie.house.gov/news/documentsingle.aspx?DocumentID=395642" target="_blank">legislative priorities</a>, according to a person briefed on the conversation.</li></ul><p><strong>The other side: </strong>Massie told Axios he was skeptical Trump allies would find a strong candidate to run against him. </p><ul><li>Massie noted he had easily fended off primary challenges in the last three elections and said his private polling showed him popular in his conservative central Kentucky district.</li><li>"If somebody got in this race and they were a reasonable person, not crazy to run against me, I would call them up and say: 'You know what you should do before you dedicate the next year and a half of your life to getting your a** kicked? You should do a poll,'" Massie said.</li><li>Massie also said Trump's attacks on him were helping him fundraise, pointing out he had raised $47,000 this week and had a series of donor events lined up in California next week.</li><li>The congressman's allies say his independent streak endears him to voters.</li></ul><p><strong>The intrigue: </strong>Massie said he spoke to Trump a few weeks before the election and a few weeks after, but not since. After Massie's mother passed away in June 2024, Trump left him a voicemail expressing his condolences, Massie said.</p><ul><li>During the call after the election, Massie told Trump he would be interested in serving as his agriculture secretary, an idea Trump passed on. </li><li>"I would have taken it," Massie said.</li></ul>

Title: "You don't have to die in this place": House Dems want age reckoning after Connolly's death
Description: <p>Some younger House Democrats are preparing to push for a long-delayed, caucus-wide intervention on age after the tragic passing of yet another one of <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/21/gerry-connolly-dies-oversight-committee-virginia" target="_blank">their septuagenarian colleagues</a>, Axios has learned.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The impacts of the party's aging membership were keenly felt Thursday when House Republicans <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/22/house-passes-trumps-big-beautiful-bill" target="_blank">passed their sweeping tax cut bill</a> by just a single vote, 215 to 214.</p><hr><ul><li>Several House Democrats argued that vacancies created by the deaths of Reps. Gerry Connolly (D-Va.), <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/13/raul-grijalva-dies-cancer-77" target="_blank">Raúl Grijalva</a> (D-Ariz.) and <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/05/sylvester-turner-house-democrat-texas-dies" target="_blank">Sylvester Turner</a> (D-Texas), all in their 70s, may have been outcome-determinative.</li><li>"You see where we are, we can't afford to lose anymore members. ... We're down three people because they passed away," one lawmaker told Axios just off the floor as the House was voting on the bill.</li><li>Said another ahead of the vote: "The tragic reality is, when ... this vote passes and the difference is the number of members who passed away this Congress, I think it's going to really infuriate many of our supporters."</li></ul><p><strong>By the numbers: </strong>The eight members of Congress who have died in office since November 2022 were all Democrats, with an average age of 75.</p><ul><li>A half dozen of those deaths were just in the 13 months since last April.</li><li>Grijalva's seat won't be filled until a <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/phoenix/2025/03/26/democratic-candidates-lining-up-for-cd7-special-election-to-replace-grijalva" target="_blank">special election</a> is held in late September. Texas' Republican Gov. Greg Abbott has scheduled the election for Turner's seat <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/houston/2025/04/08/bayou-buzz" target="_blank">on Nov. 4</a>, to the fury of Democrats.</li><li>Some Democrats fear Virginia's Republican governor may similarly drag his feet on scheduling a contest to replace Connolly.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>Of the House's 10 oldest members, seven are Democrats, Axios' <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/21/congress-ages-gerontocracy-members-gerry-connolly" target="_blank">April Rubin reported</a>.</p><ul><li>"Some folks have given their life to this place, and we're so grateful and commend them for it — you don't have to die in this place," the first House Democrat said. </li><li>"I definitely think that someone in leadership needs to have some hard conversations and say … 'you don't [have to] keep doing this.'"</li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>In interviews with a dozen House Democrats on Wednesday and Thursday, many said the time for those difficult discussions has come.</p><ul><li>Most spoke on the condition of anonymity to offer candid thoughts about a highly sensitive topic without facing backlash from their colleagues.</li><li>"This is something that Democrats come up to me [and ask about] all the time, everywhere I go, like, 'You guys need a fresh face. A fresh message and a fresh face,'" said a third House Democrat.</li><li>A fourth told Axios it's nothing personal to older members, but "the people don't own the seats, and we just look so f**king out of touch."</li><li>"I think this could force a conversation," a fifth House Democrat said of Connolly's passing on Wednesday.</li></ul><p><strong>What to watch: </strong>It is not yet clear what reforms younger Democrats will pursue, though several floated a renewed push for committee leadership term limits as a way to incentivize older members to retire.</p><ul><li>Republicans "don't have seniority over there. We do. That could be something that gets discussed," the fifth House Democrat said.</li><li>"The incentives, on our side, cause people to be here a long time," said a sixth lawmaker. "There's a conversation to be had there."</li><li>A seventh told Axios that when committee term limits were instituted in their state legislature, "I think it ended up being for the better. ... It was exciting to be on a team where it felt like everyone had an equitable shot."</li></ul><p><strong>The intrigue: </strong>Rep. Bill Foster (D-Ill.), Democrats' <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/11/22/house-democrats-leaders-age" target="_blank">long-suffering champion</a> of committee term limits, said he is handing off the baton as he nears 70 in an attempt to lead by example.</p><ul><li>"I've passed the torch to the next generation. It was a little bit ironic that it was a couple of boomers arguing for generational change," the 69-year-old, who was first elected to Congress in 2008, told Axios.</li><li>The fourth House Democrat who spoke anonymously said there are "a bunch of us" planning to make that push — but that "it can't happen right now" in the immediate wake of Connolly's death.</li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but: </strong>House Democrats' older members aren't about to concede anything.</p><ul><li>More than half of the 30 House Democrats over 75 years old <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/15/house-democrats-age-members-reelection-biden" target="_blank">are running again</a>, and many attest to their vigorous health. A sizable portion of them are facing or are expected to face <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/24/house-democrats-primary-challenges" target="_blank">primary challenges</a>.</li><li>Reps. Stephen Lynch (D-Mass.), 70, and Kweisi Mfume (D-Md.), 76, have expressed interest in <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/30/democrats-connolly-aoc-crockett-lynch-oversight" target="_blank">running to replace Connolly</a> as the ranking member of the House Oversight Committee. </li><li>They may face 47-year-old <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/06/robert-garcia-aoc-oversight-committee-democrats" target="_blank">Robert Garcia</a> (D-Calif.), a member of House Democratic leadership who could try to use his strong relationships with colleagues to overcome his relative lack of seniority.</li></ul><p><strong>The bottom line: </strong>That this issue is bubbling up to the surface amid <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/22/biden-original-sin-book-oversight-committee" target="_blank">new revelations about President Biden's health</a> only gives it more urgency, lawmakers said.</p><ul><li>"It's important. It's just more symbolically important. We've got Joe Biden hanging over here ... like a huge albatross," said the third House Democrat.</li><li>"Then you add to this that the face of Congress just seems older. ... People keep hearing about all these older people who we have here and are like, 'Wait, what?'"</li></ul>
