Title: 22 More People, Entities Charged In Arizona Medicaid Fraud Scheme
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">22 More People, Entities Charged In Arizona Medicaid Fraud Scheme</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/22-more-people-entities-charged-in-arizona-medicaid-fraud-scheme-5860806?utm_source=partner&utm_campaign=ZeroHedge&src_src=partner&src_cmp=ZeroHedge">Authored by Bill Pan via The Epoch Times</a> (emphasis ours),</em></p>

<p><strong>An Arizona grand jury has indicted 22 individuals and entities linked to a massive Medicaid fraud scheme involving sober living homes.</strong></p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2872%29_0.jpg?itok=bN-Nx4Dq" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2872%29_0.jpg?itok=bN-Nx4Dq"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="96bd8bef-dc83-462a-9fb0-f49f562ef661" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2872%29_0.jpg?itok=bN-Nx4Dq" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>The Arizona and American flags blow in the wind in Terra Vista, Ariz., on March 5, 2025. John Fredricks/The Epoch Times</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p><strong>The charges include money laundering, theft, conspiracy, fraudulent schemes, patient referral fraud, and forgery, </strong>Arizona Attorney General Kris Mayes <a href="https://www.azag.gov/press-release/attorney-general-mayes-announces-22-new-indictments-sober-living-home-fraud-case">announced</a> Tuesday.</p>

<p>These indictments are part of an ongoing investigation into a <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/doj-charges-nearly-200-people-in-2-7-billion-health-care-fraud-crackdown-5676509">$2.7 billion fraud</a> that exploited Arizona’s health care system, particularly targeting Native Americans seeking treatment for drug and alcohol addiction.</p>

<p>According to the <a href="https://www.azag.gov/sites/default/files/2025-05/Happy%20House%20Behavioral%20Health%20LLC%20Indictment_Redacted%2005.19.25%20%281%29.pdf">charge document</a>, the 20 individuals indicted are associated with a church and a mental health organization called Happy House Behavioral Health. <strong>Prosecutors allege that Happy House was paid over $60 million for services that were either never rendered or only partially completed.</strong> Some of the billing, they say, was for clients who were deceased or incarcerated.</p>

<p>Prosecutors also allege that <strong>sober living facilities referred clients to Happy House, which in turn received funds from the Arizona Health Care Cost Containment System (AHCCCS), the state’s Medicaid agency.</strong> Happy House then allegedly paid the referring sober homes for those client placements, an arrangement at the center of the fraudulent scheme charges.</p>

<p>Among the money laundering charges is a $5 million payment that Happy House allegedly made in July 2023 to Hope of Life International Church, which later transferred $2 million to an entity in Rwanda.</p>

<p>Lawyers representing Happy House and Hope of Life International Church could not be immediately reached for comments.</p>

<p><strong>More than 100 individuals and multiple companies have so far been <a href="https://www.azag.gov/media/interest/behavioral-health-fraud-indictments">charged</a></strong> in cases cases tied to Arizona’s sweeping crackdown on Medicaid fraud and unlicensed sober living homes, many of which specifically targeted members of Native American tribes.</p>

<p>Starting around 2019, scammers lured individuals into fraudulent treatment programs by promising food, shelter, and addiction recovery services. Instead, they were placed in sober living homes where operators often allowed or even encouraged continued drug and alcohol use, according to state officials. Victims were often cut off from family contact, and in some cases held against their will, the charges allege.</p>

<p>“<strong>Isolated by these organizations, people had to escape out of windows and jump over fences in the middle of the night just to access a phone to reach the outside world</strong>,” said Arizona Gov. Katie Hobbs in 2023, during the announcement of a crackdown that suspended payments to 102 providers.</p>

<p>Meanwhile, the scammers overbilled the American Indian Health Program, a Medicaid plan for tribal members, for services that were never provided. AHCCCS said between 2019 and 2022, outpatient behavioral health claims surged from $53 million to $668 million.</p>

<p>In response to what Hobbs described as a humanitarian crisis, the state <a href="https://www.azag.gov/press-release/attorney-general-mayes-announces-tribal-nation-and-non-profit-recipients-6-million">launched</a> a $6 million grant in November 2024 to support tribal communities harmed by the scam.</p>

<p>In April, Hobbs signed <a href="https://apps.azleg.gov/BillStatus/BillOverview/82688">a law</a> tightening oversight of sober living homes. Under the new law, the Arizona Department of Health Services will establish standards for facilities to ensure a drug- and alcohol-free environment and promote recovery. The department will also have authority to suspend or revoke licenses, or fine violators up to $1,000 for each day a violation remains unaddressed.</p>

<p>At a minimum, the law requires the department to conduct annual inspections, track complaints, and report to lawmakers how many led to investigations or enforcement actions.</p>

Title: Trump's 'Big, Beautiful Bill' Strips Al Capone-Era Tax On Suppressors
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Trump's 'Big, Beautiful Bill' Strips Al Capone-Era Tax On Suppressors</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Gun rights groups celebrated Thursday morning after the House narrowly passed President Trump's "<a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/political/trumps-big-beautiful-bill-narrowly-passes-house-215-214-vote">Big, Beautiful Bill</a>" in a 215–214 vote. Organizations like Gun Owners of America praised the legislation for including the Constitutional Hearing Protection Act (CHPA), which eliminates both the federal registration requirement and the $200 tax on firearm suppressors. The provision drew sharp criticism from anti-gunners and leftist media outlets as the bill now heads to the Senate. </p>

<p>"The<strong> House of Representatives passes GOA-backed language 215-214 to ELIMINATE the unconstitutional taxation & registration of suppressors under the NFA</strong>," GOA wrote on X, adding, "<strong>The bill heads to the Senate, where GOA will fight to include protections for short-barreled firearms too</strong>." </p>

He thanked the millions of GOA members who have supported their efforts.</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">THANK YOU to our members, supporters, & 2A allies who helped make suppressor deregulation a reality in the House.<br /><br />

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Since being classified under the Al Capone-era National Firearms Act, suppressors have been subject to a $200 tax stamp imposed by the ATF. <strong>If President Trump signs the Senate version of the "Big, Beautiful Bill," purchasers only need to pass an FBI background check to acquire a suppressor</strong>.</p>

<p>"Shall not be infringed—or taxed. I'm proud that we secured the elimination of taxation and registration of suppressors in budget reconciliation. <strong>It's past time we restore our constitutional 2A rights,</strong>" stated Rep. Andrew Clyde (R-GA), who originally introduced CHPA. </p>

<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Clyde said, "<strong>This is a massive 2A victory</strong> — one that takes important steps toward restoring our constitutional freedoms."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/guns_11.jpg?itok=Mj7qy1cg" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/guns_11.jpg?itok=Mj7qy1cg"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="cf82312c-9ed0-418b-a56e-f80da1dc198a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/guns_11.jpg?itok=Mj7qy1cg" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>GOA Founder Erich Pratt stated, "<strong>Eliminating the suppressor registration and tax is a major step forward for liberty and safety</strong>. This would not have happened without Rep. Clyde's resolve and strategic leadership. <strong>Gun owners have one less unconstitutional hurdle to worry about — but we're not done</strong>. The Senate needs to deliver on President Trump's campaign promise to protect gun owners from another <strong>ban on short-barreled firearms like the Biden Pistol Brace Ban</strong>."</p>

<p>Meanwhile, leftist corporate media melted down...</p>

Title: What The Biden Health Coverup Reveals About The Political Class
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">What The Biden Health Coverup Reveals About The Political Class</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://mises.org/mises-wire/what-biden-health-coverup-reveals-about-political-class">Authored by Connor O'Keefe via the Mises Institute</a>,</em></p>

<p><strong>Over the weekend, the Biden family announced that former President Joe Biden has been <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2025/05/18/us/politics/biden-prostate-cancer.html">diagnosed</a> with stage IV prostate cancer.</strong> The statement said that the cancer was characterized by a Gleason score of 9 out of 10, indicating it is highly aggressive, and that it has already spread to the bone.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/BidenCoverup_Wire_jpg_webp_92.jpg?itok=JU4gkBBN" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/BidenCoverup_Wire_jpg_webp_92.jpg?itok=JU4gkBBN"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="cfa23ad1-8a04-404f-a6ba-9e749a8c758c" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="375" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/BidenCoverup_Wire_jpg_webp_92.jpg?itok=JU4gkBBN" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Well-wishes poured in from both the former president’s allies and political opponents as the Bidens reportedly reviewed treatment options.<strong> But it didn’t take long for people to note a few questionable details about the nature and timing of this announcement.</strong></p>

<p>First, it happened to come a little over thirty hours before the release of a highly-anticipated <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Original-Sin-President-Cover-Up-Disastrous-ebook/dp/B0DXCMSHVL">book</a> by CNN’s Jake Tapper and <em>Axios</em>’s Alex Thompson that detailed Joe Biden’s mental decline while in office and the effort by people around him to cover it up <strong>and deny it was happening at all</strong>. While other books have already come out claiming to tell this story, none have come from journalists as highly respected by the political establishment as Tapper and Thompson.</p>

<p>Also, the day before the announcement,<strong> <em>Axios</em> released the <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GNjkE_tDZts">full recording</a> of Biden’s interview with special counsel Robert Hur,</strong> where the president’s difficulty answering straightforward questions was on full display at the same time his allies in the media were trying to <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1kKUye23KBQ">claim</a> he was “as sharp as a tack.”</p>

<p><strong>That convenient timing and speed at which some Biden allies, like <a href="https://www.foxnews.com/video/6373058221112">David Axelrod</a>, came out and said that talk of the former president’s decline should now be set aside</strong> because of this diagnosis led to some skepticism about the claim that the cancer was discovered only a few days ago.</p>

<p>That <a href="https://www.reuters.com/world/us/bidens-cancer-diagnosis-prompts-new-questions-about-his-health-while-office-2025-05-19/">skepticism</a> only grew as doctors began reacting with <a href="https://www.dailywire.com/news/doctors-raise-questions-about-timing-of-biden-cancer-diagnosis-unbelievable-this-was-missed">disbelief</a> that cancer at this late a stage could have either just developed in the past few months or gone undetected for years while Biden was president. That’s especially true considering that prostate cancer is typically easier to discover early than most other cancers due to <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/prostate/psa-fact-sheet">antigens</a> it releases in the blood that can be detected with a simple blood test—a blood test we know both presidents Obama and Trump had <a href="https://news.grabien.com/story/msnbc-s-dr-gupta-bush-obama-and-trump-all-had-this-prostate-test-and-i">taken</a> while they were in office.</p>

<p>It is certainly possible that no physical health problems were covered up during Biden’s presidency, that his cancer was only detected for the first time a few weeks ago, as his office has said.<strong> But many of those most aggressively denying that anything shady is happening with the timing of this announcement will have a much harder time getting the public to believe them </strong>because of the blatant and unsuccessful attempt to censor, hide, and deny Biden’s deteriorating mental state in the lead up to the 2024 election.</p>

<p>The lengths to which establishment politicians and major media figures went to gaslight the American public into dismissing something that was obvious to anyone who was looking should never be forgotten because it exposed the true nature of the political class. They lied, shamelessly, to further their political ambitions.</p>

<p>While that’s far from unusual, rarely are their lies as blatantly and immediately obvious as <a href="https://www.newsweek.com/what-top-democrats-said-then-now-about-joe-bidens-decline-2073468">saying</a> Biden was sharp and <a href="https://deadline.com/2024/06/biden-age-wall-street-journal-morning-joe-1235959576/">highly engaged</a> behind closed doors and that every video that purported to show otherwise was <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/news/cheap-fake-biden-videos-burst-100000427.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAAmD5xX-aXtkm5eGm1zG5jlTdQUDJ1ygaTiaTAIHn8Fm_wdGgoPXdxs5RCRMLJO4HttHkgBThlkLvaAYxFEFWSA0skUeq2B8f43qMeJ3L2dPBKOQp26E14Aa0kFtdF05YU1TrggASorr_ivGzUOtLx3u3g4eC2Z2z1DGDnt6DjrS">fabricated</a> by far-right video editors.</p>

<p><strong>It’s also rare for the establishment’s lies to blow up in their faces as quickly and extensively as this one did at the now famous June 2024 <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-v-8wJkmwBY">presidential debate</a>.</strong> Once it became obvious that the lie would not hold, virtually the entire anti-Trump political scene flipped on a dime and began parroting concerns that they were mocking people for voicing mere hours before.</p>

<p>The political class is still struggling to run damage control. The most promising strategy—seemingly embodied by Tapper and Thompson’s new book—is to try to pin the blame on a handful of staffers, claiming they hid the truth from media figures like Tapper who then unintentionally <a href="https://nypost.com/2025/05/14/media/jake-tapper-slammed-for-rewriting-history-to-cash-in-on-book-covering-bidens-decline/">spread</a> the lie to the rest of the world. But that would be a much easier sell if millions of Americans had not spent years openly talking about the very thing that was apparently being hidden from them. Still, the establishment will throw as many staffers under the bus as they need to avoid admitting they lied. They do not want the takeaway from this episode to be that they need to lie less.</p>

<p>And beyond that,<strong> if the establishment admitted they knowingly supported an increasingly cognitively impaired man, not only to remain in office but to serve an entire second term, it would <a href="https://mises.org/mises-wire/biden-not-running-government-so-who">shatter the illusion</a> that our government is truly run by a president who embodies the wishes of the voting public</strong>, like we learned in elementary school. It would reveal the fact that, as long as they don’t actively speak out against or draw attention to all the ways the political class is ripping the American public off, the person sitting in the Oval Office is essentially irrelevant.</p>

<p>Whether the timing of Biden’s cancer announcement is a particularly disgusting part of the scheme to cover all this up or truly a complete coincidence, the last few days have made it clear that the damage the political class did to its credibility with its attempted cover-up of Joe Biden’s condition has not gone away. And that is duly deserved.</p>
</div>

Title: AI, Chips, Humanoid Robots: Top Takeaways From Computex 2025
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">AI, Chips, Humanoid Robots: Top Takeaways From Computex 2025</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Computex 2025 in Taipei, Taiwan, entered its fourth day on Thursday. Tech blog <a href="https://www.tomsguide.com/news/live/computex-2025">Tom's Guide</a> said the spotlight this week has been on AMD's Radeon RX 9060 XT and Nvidia's RTX 5060 gaming GPUs. Other top highlights include Intel's early reveal of next-gen laptop CPUs for 2026 and MSI's debut of its first AMD-powered gaming handheld, the Claw A8.</p>

<p>Breaking down Asia's top AI tech show, <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-05-22/computex-2025-five-takeaways-from-asia-s-biggest-ai-tech-event">Bloomberg</a> highlighted <strong>five key takeaways from this week:</strong></p>

<blockquote>
<p><strong>Consumer AI Needs More Time</strong></p>

<p><em>There was scant mention of consumers this year. In 2024, Qualcomm Inc. devoted its presentation to how AI would make everything better and we'd never again need our laptop chargers on the move. This time around, it flipped to a script focused on enterprise applications for AI.</em></p>

<p><em>Foxconn, also known as Hon Hai Precision Industry Co., used its first keynote address at the show to go big on heavy-duty AI, from making cities smarter to bringing robots to manufacturing and making EV design more efficient. The company that assembles the bulk of the world's iPhones had nothing to excite consumers.</em></p>

<p><em>Asustek Computer Inc. offered a sobering outlook on the prospects of so-called AI PCs.</em></p>

<p><em>Samson Hu, co-chief executive officer of the Taiwanese computer gear maker, said AI PCs will take a year or two before they go mainstream. That's because the software is still immature, plus new tariffs from the US are likely to flatten near-term growth. Asus may have to hike prices in the US by as much as 10% to deal with those levies, Hu said.</em></p>

<p><strong>DeepSeek Changed AI</strong></p>

<p><em>The debut of DeepSeek in January changed the nature of AI, highlighting China's advances in the field while dismantling basic assumptions about computing needs.</em></p>

<p><em>Huang was among the few executives who addressed that first openly, saying that China is "incredible" at software development and has the resources to make up for any technological gap.</em></p>

<p><em>DeepSeek also popularized reasoning models, which require more raw computing power. "And so now the reasoning model is not one shot, but it's hundreds of shots," Huang told reporters this week. "DeepSeek increased the amount of computing need by maybe 100 to 1,000 times."</em></p>

<p><strong>China Looms Large </strong></p>

<p><em>The most-clicked headlines centered around Nvidia's delicate position as the US pursues chip restrictions intended to curtail China's tech ascent. That came to a head Wednesday, when Huang branded that effort a "failure" and called for Washington to back away.</em></p>

<p><em>If the US doesn't allow Nvidia to sell within China, local companies like Huawei Technologies Co. will fill the void, he warned. "The local companies are very, very talented and very determined," Huang said. "And the export controls gave them the spirit, the energy and the government support to accelerate their development." </em></p>

<p><em>While key officials in Washington buy that argument as it applies to the rest of the world, US President Donald Trump's administration has doubled down on measures targeting Beijing. </em></p>

<p><em>Executives in Taiwan no doubt took note of two related developments. Huawei hosted its AI developer gathering the same week, touting the Ascend chips that Beijing wants to see supplant Nvidia's silicon. And Xiaomi Corp. happened to announce it's developed its own advanced 3-nanometer mobile chip to compete with Qualcomm.</em></p>

<p><strong>Taiwan Charm Offensive</strong></p>

<p><em>Intel Corp.'s new boss worked hard to mend ties with the Taiwanese partners, after his predecessor Pat Gelsinger raised concerns about the island's dominance in semiconductors.</em></p>

<p><em>Lip-Bu Tan praised local supply chain partners during a company event in Taipei celebrating its 40th anniversary on Monday.</em></p>

<p><em>Even Nvidia dedicated much time and floor space at the conference to lauding its Taiwanese partners. SoftBank Group Corp. founder Masayoshi Son was also in town for the week, though like Tan he was keeping a low public profile.</em></p>

<p><strong>No Bubble? </strong></p>

<p><em>There was little public discussion about one of the most pressing questions for tech investors: have we overestimated the need for datacenters? Tech stocks from Nvidia to Meta Platforms Inc. and Microsoft Corp. have gyrated wildly in 2025 in part because of that overarching uncertainty.</em></p>

<p><em>To be sure, most of the attendees benefit directly from spending on the servers and components needed to power datacenters and AI development. Nvidia's CEO echoed the sentiment.</em></p>

<p><em>"We're several hundred billion dollars into tens of trillions of dollars of AI infrastructure buildout," Huang said.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>With all the major announcements already made earlier in the week, the Computex conference will wrap up on Friday.</p>

<p>Goldman analyst Eddy Kuo attended the conference. In a note on Thursday, he pointed out that Nvidia CEO Jensen Huang "is optimistic for humanoid robotics and commented it will be the core of the future economy, and Taiwan is playing a key role in this area integrating AI and humanoid robots." </p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">As Taiwan faces nursing shortages and an aging population, COMPUTEX 2025 showcases innovative robotics solutions, including Foxconn's Nurabot for healthcare and Pegatron's Simba robot dog for dangerous environments.<br />
★ <a href="https://t.co/ynzSGjhc12">https://t.co/ynzSGjhc12</a> ★ <a href="https://t.co/qERUmznDUJ">pic.twitter.com/qERUmznDUJ</a></p>
— TVBS World Taiwan (@tvbsworldtaiwan) <a href="https://twitter.com/tvbsworldtaiwan/status/1925500393444024699?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 22, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>"Computex will conclude today and color on the ground here the Computex onsite is super packed yesterday even more crowded than Tue and expect today to reach the peak and lots of interests on ASIC related supply chain," Kuo said. </p>
</div>

Title: Far-Left Activist Charged In Jewish Museum Killings, Shot Couple Multiple Times As They 'Attempted To Crawl Away'
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Far-Left Activist Charged In Jewish Museum Killings, Shot Couple Multiple Times As They 'Attempted To Crawl Away'</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><strong><u>Update(1817ET)</u>:</strong> Elias Rodriguez, a 30-year old man from Chicago, has been charged in last night's fatal shooting of two Israeli embassy employees in Washington, outside an event hosted at the Jewish Museum.</p>

<p>He is accused of <strong>opening fire on an entire group of people</strong> who were exiting an event hosted by an advocacy group that supports Israel. He faces two counts of first-degree murder for the deaths of <strong>Sarah Lynn Milgrim and Yaron Lischinsky</strong>.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/Lischinsky-Milgrim.jpg?itok=w84GfALb" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/Lischinsky-Milgrim.jpg?itok=w84GfALb"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="2065aa79-18f5-4018-beb6-edbb5a319456" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/Lischinsky-Milgrim.jpg?itok=w84GfALb" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Yaron Lischinsky and Sarah Lynn Milgrim were killed by a gunman as they left an event at the Capital Jewish Museum in Washington, D.C., on Wednesday night.</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>Court filing shows brutal execution-style murders, after which Rodriguez shouted "free Palestine!" as police apprehended him and took him away.</p>

<p><strong>He shot the young woman in the back after she was hit the first time, and as she struggled to stay alive</strong>.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/policeresponsedc.jpg?itok=23Vy_IgT" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/policeresponsedc.jpg?itok=23Vy_IgT"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="e6027b47-3905-49b5-be6b-b893e9f57e6d" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="282" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/policeresponsedc.jpg?itok=23Vy_IgT" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The shooting occurred across the street from the FBI’s Washington Field Office, which is located very near to the museum, and Israeli embassy officials are working with local law enforcement and the FBI.</p>

<p>It has further been confirmed that the Israeli ambassador is safe, and was not involved in the incident, and was not present at the time of the shooting.</p>

<p>Underscoring the seriousness of the killings, which appear to have targeted an event which took place at the Jewish Museum, <strong>US Attorney General Pam Bondi amd acting US Attorney for DC Jeanine Pirro are currently on the scene in the aftermath</strong>. </p>

Title: Gold And The Great American Monetary Resets: From 1792 To Today
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Gold And The Great American Monetary Resets: From 1792 To Today</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://internationalman.com/articles/gold-and-the-great-american-monetary-resets-from-1792-to-today/">Authored by Nick Giambruno via International Man</a>,</em></p>

<p><strong>Gold has been at the heart of the US monetary system since the nation’s founding, evolving from a direct anchor for the dollar to a strategic reserve asset.</strong></p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/gold-reset-shutterstock_1571108095_jpg_92.jpg?itok=JNgyMWBA" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/gold-reset-shutterstock_1571108095_jpg_92.jpg?itok=JNgyMWBA"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="883a2c15-1f46-4200-8ecd-47d38b8c4247" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="263" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/gold-reset-shutterstock_1571108095_jpg_92.jpg?itok=JNgyMWBA" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Though it no longer backs the dollar, gold remains a cornerstone of central bank reserves, a discreet but powerful force in global finance.</p>

<p>Throughout American history, monetary resets have been a recurring theme—and more often than not, they have revolved around gold because gold is money.</p>

<p>Understanding this history isn’t just about the past—it’s about the future. And if history is any guide, another reset may be coming sooner than most expect.</p>

<h3>1775: Continentals and the American Revolution</h3>

<p>Before the Revolution, gold and silver coins were the backbone of trade in the American colonies.</p>

<p><strong>When war broke out, the Continental Congress lacked the authority to levy taxes, forcing them to seek an alternative way to finance the war.</strong></p>

<p>In 1775, Congress began issuing “Continental Currency”—the first fiat paper money in US history. These notes, known as “Continentals,” were supposed to be redeemable in gold and silver after the war, but that promise lacked credibility.</p>

<p>Continentals quickly became worthless amid hyperinflation. <strong>The phrase “Not worth a Continental” became synonymous with worthlessness.</strong></p>

<p>By 1781, Continentals had lost over 99% of their value, and the US government effectively abandoned them, leaving holders with massive losses.</p>

<p>This disaster deepened distrust in fiat money and cemented the belief among the Founders that gold and silver must be the foundation of any stable monetary system.</p>

<h3>1792: The Coinage Act and the Birth of the US Monetary System</h3>

<p>After the disastrous failure of Continental Currency, the Coinage Act of 1792 created the first official US monetary system, ensuring stability by tying the dollar to both gold and silver.</p>

<p>Gold was set at $19.39 per ounce, while silver was also legal tender.</p>

<p>The Founders aimed to prevent another Continental-style collapse by anchoring the currency to hard money.</p>

<h3>The First Bank of the United States (1791–1811)</h3>

<p>The First Bank of the United States, the nation’s first central bank, was established under the leadership of Alexander Hamilton to stabilize the economy, issue a national currency backed by gold and silver, and manage federal deposits.</p>

<p>However, it quickly became a political flashpoint, facing fierce opposition from Thomas Jefferson and states’ rights advocates, who feared it concentrated too much financial power in the hands of the federal government.</p>

<p>When the bank’s 20-year charter expired in 1811, Congress refused to renew it.</p>

<h3>The Second Bank of the United States (1816–1836)</h3>

<p>In the wake of the financial chaos following the War of 1812, the US established another central bank, the Second Bank of the United States, in 1816.</p>

<p>Like its predecessor, it was designed to regulate credit, stabilize the currency, and hold federal deposits.</p>

<p>However, it quickly became a political lightning rod, particularly under President Andrew Jackson, who saw it as a corrupt institution that served elite interests at the expense of ordinary Americans.</p>

<p>Jackson vetoed its recharter in 1832, waged a successful campaign against it, and ultimately dismantled the bank in 1836.</p>

<h3>1834: First Major Price Change ($20.67 per Ounce)</h3>

<p>The Coinage Act of 1834 officially raised the gold price to $20.67 per ounce, effectively devaluing the US dollar (since more dollars were now needed to buy an ounce of gold).</p>

<p>The $20.67 per ounce gold price remained unchanged for nearly a century until FDR’s intervention in 1933.</p>

<h3>1862: Lincoln’s Greenbacks – The Civil War Fiat Experiment</h3>

<p>During the War Between the States (1861–1865), President Abraham Lincoln introduced a fiat paper currency known as “Greenbacks” to finance the war effort. This marked a major departure from the gold and silver-based system that had defined US money.</p>

<p>The war demanded enormous financial resources, but the government lacked sufficient gold and silver reserves to cover costs. Traditional borrowing through bond sales proved insufficient, and policymakers were reluctant to impose heavy taxation on the public. In response, Congress passed the Legal Tender Act of 1862, authorizing the issuance of paper money not backed by gold or silver—these notes became known as “Greenbacks” due to their distinctive color.</p>

<p>Although Greenbacks allowed the government to fund the war, they were not backed by hard assets, leading to debasement. After the war, the US took steps to restore confidence in the monetary system and return to a gold-backed standard.</p>

<p>In 1869, the Public Credit Act was passed, pledging that Greenbacks would eventually be redeemable in gold, reassuring creditors. This was followed by the Specie Payment Resumption Act of 1875, which mandated that by 1879, Greenbacks would once again be convertible into gold. By then, the US had reduced the number of Greenbacks in circulation, successfully returning to a gold-based monetary system and ending their fiat status.</p>

<p>Although Greenbacks were a temporary fiat currency, their detachment from gold foreshadowed future monetary shifts.</p>

<h3>1913: The Federal Reserve Act</h3>

<p>The creation of the Federal Reserve—the nation’s third central bank—marked a significant shift toward centralized control over the US monetary system.</p>

<p>While gold remained part of the system, the Federal Reserve’s ability to expand credit beyond physical gold reserves weakened gold’s direct role in the monetary system. This shift set the stage for future monetary interventions, inflationary policies, and the eventual abandonment of gold convertibility in 1971.</p>

<h3>1933: FDR’s Gold Confiscation (Executive Order 6102)</h3>

<p>In 1933, President Franklin D. Roosevelt (FDR) issued Executive Order 6102, forcing Americans to turn in their gold coins and bullion to the US Treasury. This move was intended to give the government greater control over the money supply and combat deflation during the Great Depression.</p>

<p>Citizens were paid $20.67 per ounce for their gold, but shortly after, the government revalued gold at $35 per ounce, effectively devaluing the dollar by 41%. The change allowed the government to print more dollars without increasing gold reserves.</p>

<p>In a national radio address on October 22, 1933, Roosevelt justified the decision, stating:</p>

<p>“The United States must take firmly in its own hands the control of the value of our dollar.”</p>

<p>Gold ownership was banned for private citizens until 1974, and much of the nation’s gold was centralized in Fort Knox. This marked a decisive step in the government’s tightening control over the monetary system.</p>

<h3>1944: The Bretton Woods Agreement – The Dollar Becomes the Global Reserve Currency</h3>

<p>It’s been rightly said that “he who holds the gold makes the rules.”</p>

<p>After World War 2, the US had the largest gold reserves in the world by far. Along with winning the war, this let the US reconstruct the global monetary system around the dollar.</p>

<p>The new system, created at the Bretton Woods Conference in 1944, tied the currencies of virtually every country in the world to the US dollar through a fixed exchange rate. It also tied the US dollar to gold at a fixed rate of $35 per ounce.</p>

<p>However, the Bretton Woods Agreement was doomed to fail.</p>

<p>Runaway spending on warfare and welfare eventually caused the US government to print more dollars than it could back with gold at the promised $35 price.</p>

<h3>1971: Nixon Ends Gold Convertibility (“Nixon Shock”)</h3>

<p>By the late 1960s, the number of dollars circulating had drastically increased relative to the amount of gold backing them. This encouraged foreign countries to exchange their dollars for gold, draining the US gold supply at an alarming rate.</p>

<p>As a result, the US gold supply dropped by more than half, from 574 million troy ounces at the end of World War II to around 261 million troy ounces in 1971.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/word-image-65622-1_png_92.jpg?itok=CpCTGWEr" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/word-image-65622-1_png_92.jpg?itok=CpCTGWEr"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="be07e069-9c27-4d92-8656-12256322f5a4" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="311" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/word-image-65622-1_png_92.jpg?itok=CpCTGWEr" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The situation pressured the US government to make a drastic decision.</p>

<p>It could do nothing and watch its gold holdings evaporate, which would mean losing enormous financial and geopolitical power. Or it could default on its promise to redeem the dollar for gold.</p>

<p>On Sunday night, August 15, 1971, President Nixon interrupted the scheduled TV programs and made a surprise announcement to the nation—and the world.</p>

<p>Nixon said he was temporarily suspending the dollar’s convertibility into gold.</p>

<p>The most obvious lie was Nixon’s claim that the suspension would only be “temporary.” It’s still in place today.</p>

<p>Another egregious lie was that his move was necessary to protect Americans from international speculators. Instead, money printing to finance out-of-control government spending was the real problem.</p>

<p>Lastly, Nixon said removing the link to gold would stabilize the dollar. However, even by the government’s own rigged inflation statistics, which understate reality, the US dollar has lost over 87% of its purchasing power since 1971.</p>

<p>The truth is that Nixon defaulted on the US government’s promise to redeem the dollar for gold at $35 an ounce. Since then, the dollar has been a pure fiat currency with no backing.</p>

<h3>1972 – The Smithsonian Agreement Adjusts the Gold Price to $38</h3>

<p>After the Nixon Shock, world leaders met in December 1971 to try and stabilize the international monetary system. The Smithsonian Agreement attempted to:</p>

<ul><li>Raise the official gold price from $35 to $38 per ounce, effectively devaluing the dollar by 8.5%.</li>
	<li>Allow major currencies to fluctuate within a 2.25% band instead of being strictly fixed.</li>
</ul><p>However, confidence in the dollar continued to erode, and the agreement collapsed by 1973, paving the way for the modern floating exchange rate system, where gold would trade freely on the open market.</p>

<h3>1973: The US Dollar and Gold Officially Float</h3>

<p>After multiple attempts to stabilize exchange rates—including the Smithsonian Agreement (1971)—major currencies transitioned to a free-floating system in early 1973, allowing exchange rates to fluctuate based on market forces.</p>

<p>As the US dollar continued to weaken, another official devaluation occurred in February 1973, raising the official gold price from $38 to $42.22 per ounce. This represented a total devaluation of 20.7% compared to the original $35 peg established under Bretton Woods.</p>

<p>However,<strong> despite these adjustments, it became clear that the US could no longer control gold’s value in global markets.</strong></p>

<p>By March 1973, the Smithsonian Agreement collapsed, and major currencies—including the US dollar—shifted to a fully floating exchange rate system. This marked the end of government-controlled gold pricing as the US stopped setting an official price. Gold began trading freely on the open market, and its price was determined by supply and demand rather than government decree.</p>

<p>While August 15, 1971, marked the end of gold convertibility under the Nixon Shock, the US still attempted to maintain an official gold price under the Smithsonian Agreement. However, this system ultimately failed.</p>

<p>Gold officially began trading freely in March 1973, when the floating exchange rate system was adopted, allowing the market to set gold’s value independently for the first time since the nation’s founding.</p>

<p>Below is a chart depicting the 181-year history of gold’s official role in the US monetary system—from the Coinage Act of 1792 to 1973.</p>

<p>Each gold price adjustment marks a rare but significant event, reflecting dollar devaluations and major monetary resets that reshaped the financial system.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/word-image-65622-2_png_92.jpg?itok=LMD_vQOW" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/word-image-65622-2_png_92.jpg?itok=LMD_vQOW"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="b88e7c68-f4fd-423b-b413-dcc38c92677e" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="322" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/word-image-65622-2_png_92.jpg?itok=LMD_vQOW" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<h3>The Rise of Gold as a Financial Asset (1973–Present)</h3>

<p>Before the adoption of a fiat currency standard after the end of Bretton Woods, gold had been mankind’s most enduring form of money—for over 5,000 years—because of unique characteristics that made it best suited to store and exchange value.</p>

<p>Gold is durable, divisible, consistent, convenient, scarce, and most importantly, the “hardest” of all physical commodities.</p>

<p>In other words, gold is the one physical commodity that is the “hardest to produce” (relative to existing stockpiles) and, therefore, the most resistant to debasement.</p>

<p><strong>Gold is indestructible, and its stockpiles have built up over thousands of years. That’s a big reason why the growth of new gold supply—typically 1-2% per year—is insignificant.</strong></p>

<p>In other words, nobody can arbitrarily inflate the supply.</p>

<p>That makes gold an excellent store of value and gives the yellow metal its superior monetary properties.</p>

<p>People in every country of the world value gold. Its worth doesn’t depend on any government or any counterparty at all. Gold has always been an inherently international and politically neutral asset. This is why different civilizations around the world have used gold as money for millennia.</p>

<p>Yet, most people don’t understand this.</p>

<p>They might say the paper dollars in their wallets and the digital dollars in their bank accounts are money, not gold. But that’s only been the case since 1971, a drop in the bucket by historical terms.</p>

<p>The collapse of the Bretton Woods system in 1971 was a turning point, severing gold’s link to the dollar and transforming it from a fixed monetary anchor into a freely traded financial asset. Even though it is no longer legal tender, gold has retained its status as a store of value, trusted by governments, central banks, and investors worldwide. Its role as a hedge against inflation, currency devaluation, and economic instability has only strengthened over time.</p>

<p><strong>Despite abandoning the gold standard, central banks continue to hold and accumulate gold, recognizing its importance as a financial asset.</strong></p>

<p>This is what makes gold fundamentally different from other commodities like wheat, copper, or oil. While those goods are consumed, gold is primarily held as a financial asset, making its price a critical indicator of global economic stability, currency strength, and monetary policy credibility.</p>

<p>The price of gold is a barometer of the fiat currency system itself. It is a real-time measure of confidence (or lack thereof) in the monetary system because it is a free market alternative to government-issued money.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/new-chart_png_92%281%29.jpg?itok=5jGUcQms" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/new-chart_png_92%281%29.jpg?itok=5jGUcQms"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="d4637110-1fcc-48fb-ac25-cadecc8777af" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="311" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/new-chart_png_92%281%29.jpg?itok=5jGUcQms" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Throughout history, every major monetary reset in the United States has revolved around gold—from the Coinage Act of 1792, to FDR’s gold confiscation in 1933, to the collapse of Bretton Woods in 1971. Each time, the dollar was devalued, and gold played a central role in reshaping the financial system.</p>

<p><strong>This is no coincidence—gold has been mankind’s most enduring form of money for thousands of years, making it only natural that it would play a central role in any major monetary shift.</strong></p>

<p>Today, the conditions are ripe for a monetary reset in the US, and history leaves little doubt—gold will once again be at the center of it. If past resets are any indication, a significant dollar devaluation is not just possible, but practically inevitable.</p>

<p>Trump’s Treasury Secretary, Scott Bessent, all but confirmed that a monetary reset is imminent when he recently stated:</p>

<blockquote>
<p>“We’re in the midst of a great realignment, a Bretton Woods realignment in terms of global policy, global trade… I’d like to be part of it, either on the inside or the outside.”</p>
</blockquote>

<p>The stage is set. History shows every major US monetary reset has revolved around gold—and 2025 could be next. With debt exploding, the dollar overvalued, and gold flowing quietly into US vaults, the writing is on the wall.</p>

<p>What happens next could change everything.</p>

<p>That’s why I’ve just released an urgent new report revealing the top three strategies you need to prepare—and profit—from what’s coming next.</p>

Title: Watch: Harmeet Dhillon Exposes DOJ's 'Color Revolution' Wing: Secret 'Resistance' Memos, 'Unhappy Hours,' & 'Crying Sessions'
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Watch: Harmeet Dhillon Exposes DOJ's 'Color Revolution' Wing: Secret 'Resistance' Memos, 'Unhappy Hours,' & 'Crying Sessions'</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>In a revealing interview with Tucker Carlson,<strong> Harmeet Dhillon, Assistant Attorney General for the Civil Rights Division, pulled back the curtain on the entrenched resistance within the Department of Justice</strong>, which she described as a stronghold of the deep state. <strong>Dhillon revealed a culture of anti-MAGA defiance</strong>, marked by resistance memos circulating among career lawyers, instructing them to obstruct directives through bureaucratic tactics. Dhillon also recounted a hilarious scene of <strong>open crying sessions in the DOJ halls</strong> and mass resignations as hundreds of attorneys recoiled at her push to align the division with the Trump administration’s agenda.</p>

<p><iframe allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture; web-share" allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" referrerpolicy="strict-origin-when-cross-origin" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/RFbAQKMZnb4?si=JdiE3A6QbFWONECb&start=264" title="YouTube video player" width="560"></iframe></p>

<p>TUCKER CARLSON: Your assistant attorney general, one of the greatest appointments, from my perspective, in this administration, running the civil rights division. What was it like when you showed up? What did you find when you got there?</p>

<p>HARMEET DHILLON: <strong>The civil rights division is the color revolution wing of the Department of Justice</strong>. Okay, whether it's a Republican or a Democrat administration, there are career lawyers who are very focused on a particular agenda there. <strong>So, when I showed up, or when I was, when the president was elected, I should say, there were over 400 attorneys in the civil rights division and about 200 staff, so a total of about 600 people.</strong> Kristen Clark, my predecessor, anti-police, open racist, got in trouble during her term for not being candid with the Senate during her confirmation hearings on some issues. So, she had a particular agenda. She got in there and she pursued that agenda aggressively. And she had all the staff to do it.</p>

<p><strong>Now, under the first Trump administration, my predecessor in that job pretty much left it untouched. </strong>He told me he kind of, like, there were the career people there, if he wanted to get something done, they went to the U.S. attorney's offices. I came in with a different perspective. I think it's part of the promise of this administration under President Trump to fundamentally reform the government in the way that the people voted for. That means, in the civil rights division, we should be standing up for the civil rights of all Americans, not just some Americans. We shouldn't be weaponizing the law in a particular way. We should apply those federal civil rights statutes, many of which were passed by and signed by Republican presidents and Republican administrations, evenly, and the government shouldn't be putting its heavy thumb on the scale in most cases. But in egregious instances, we should step forward and right these wrongs.</p>

<p><strong>But what I found there was a number of lawyers, I mean hundreds of lawyers, who were actively in resistance mode.</strong> There were memos out there by former government lawyers telling current government lawyers in my department how to resist if you're given a direct order. Ask for clarification, send 20 emails, question it, slow down your response time, say it can't be done. So, I was actually looking out for that when I came. I did my week of training after getting confirmed by the Senate. And then the next week, I was like, "Okay, guys, it's time to get to business. I want everyone to be very clear what the agenda is here.”</p>

<p>So, there are 11 sections in civil rights, and I drafted memos for each of those 11 sections for the lawyers, telling them, these are the statutes. So, for example, Americans with Disabilities Act, this is the statute that we enforce, or Title 7 anti-discrimination, or some of the other federal civil rights statutes. And then that's the baseline. And then this is the president's agenda. These are his executive orders that he's put out there about anti-discrimination, about anti-DEI, about enforcing our laws equally. And that's the job. You are going to apply these statutes within the framework of anti-discrimination, even-handedly and without fear or favor. And this catalyzed hundreds of lawyers to quit the civil rights division.</p>

<p>TUCKER CARLSON: <strong>So, wait, they quit because you informed them of the law? </strong></p>

<p>HARMEET DHILLON: Yes. And the law and the priorities, their pet projects had changed. </p>

<p>TUCKER CARLSON: They weren't going to be able to do those the way that they wanted. And so, they thought that this part of the Department of Justice was just immune to democracy.</p>

<p>HARMEET DHILLON: It has been, I mean, there were career lawyers there who were doing the same thing no matter who's a president. <strong>And so, suddenly, their little fiefdom that had remained untouched, like Shangri-La, was suddenly having to be responsive to elections. </strong></p>

<p>TUCKER CARLSON: That's the definition of the deep state, what you just described. Elections have no effect. It's like there's no way to control these people. They act totally independently from the democratic system. I mean, that's the problem right there.</p>

<p>HARMEET DHILLO<strong>N: Well, that's what I found. And so, in response to my memos, of course, </strong>they began leaking to the press. They began having unhappy hours, which they would invite supervisors, political supervisors, to, to make their point that they were unhappy. We got the point. And they had crying sessions, struggle sessions, crying sessions in the DOJ. </p>

<p>TUCKER CARLSON: They cried? </p>

<p>HARMEET DHILLON: Oh, t<strong>here was open crying in the halls. Crying, crying, crying. Yes.</strong> And then one of my colleagues described to me, it was the last day a couple of weeks ago for some of them. They lined up in a phalanx and approached the elevator together, and then they left the building together, to show their solidarity for one another there, as if they were high school students or adults.These are 30, 40, and 50-year-old career attorneys in the Department of Justice. </p>

<p>HARMEET DHILLON: It's pathetic.</p>

Title: Senators Question Spending Cuts In Key Nuclear, Science Programs
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Senators Question Spending Cuts In Key Nuclear, Science Programs</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em><a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/us/senators-question-spending-cuts-in-key-nuclear-science-programs-5861389">Authored by John Haughey via The Epoch Times</a> (emphasis ours),</em></p>

<p>A day after the Tennessee Valley Authority <a href="https://www.tva.com/news-media/releases/tva-submits-nation-s-first-construction-permit-application-for-bwrx-300-smr">announced</a> it had filed a permit to install the nation’s first small modular nuclear reactor, <strong>Secretary of Energy Chris Wright said the breakthrough marks the dawn of a new era in commercial electrical power and that sustaining momentum in advanced nuclear generation is the nation’s “next Manhattan Project.”</strong></p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2883%29_0.jpg?itok=PjOLXxjn" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2883%29_0.jpg?itok=PjOLXxjn"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a1f460da-2dce-4a7b-979b-656db69a516a" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2883%29_0.jpg?itok=PjOLXxjn" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Test engineer Jacob Wilcox pulls his arm out of a glove box used for processing sodium at TerraPower, a company developing and building small nuclear reactors in Everett, Wash., on Jan. 13, 2022. AP Photo/Elaine Thompson, File</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>“<strong>America must lead the commercialization of affordable and abundant nuclear energy</strong>,” he told the Senate Appropriations Committee’s Energy and Water Development Subcommittee. The Department of Energy “is working to advance the rapid deployment of next generation nuclear technology, including small modular reactors.”</p>

<p>Eventually, perhaps within a decade, small nuclear modular nuclear reactors, or<strong> SMRs, will be mass-produced,</strong> be portable, and ideal for “harnessing our energy potential to power global AI leadership while meeting growing energy demand,” Wright <a href="https://www.appropriations.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/secretary_wright_testimony.pdf">testified</a>, calling commercial deployment of such “next-generation technology … the challenge of our time.”</p>

<p>If so, Democrats and several Republicans wondered during a two-hour <a href="https://www.appropriations.senate.gov/hearings/a-review-of-the-presidents-fiscal-year-2026-budget-request-for-the-department-of-energy">May 21 hearing</a>, why is the Trump administration seeking to cut budgets for the department’s Office of Nuclear Energy by nearly 47 percent and its Office of Science by 87 percent in its <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/Fiscal-Year-2026-Discretionary-Budget-Request.pdf">Fiscal Year ( FY) 2026 spending request</a>?</p>

<p>“<strong>On one hand, you and the president say you support U.S. dominance in energy, emerging technologies</strong>,” Sen. Patty Murray (D-Wash.) said, “but then, on the other hand, you are proposing cutting over $1 billion dollars in funding to the Office of Science” and $408 million from the Office of Nuclear Energy.</p>

<p>She said the still-vague spending request, a broad outline crafted by the White House’s Office of Management and Budget and not by the department itself, is counterintuitive to the Trump administration’s pledge to “win the AI race against China.”</p>

<p>The previous FY25 Department of Energy budget earmarked $8.6 billion for the Office of Science and nearly $770 million for the Office of Nuclear Energy, key allocations that leverage federal seed money to induce private investment in financing demonstrations of emerging technologies.</p>

<p>The stark slashes in such funding “really undermines critical research programs for AI, for fusion, for quantum computing, for nuclear energy, and critical minerals,” Murray said. “<strong>How are investors and companies supposed to have confidence in partnering with you when what you say and what your budget says are two different things?”</strong></p>

<p>Sen. Katie Britt (R-Ala.) asked Wright for assurances that the budget will include funding for SMR development and research into other emerging reactor technologies underway in her state, and Sen. Bill Hagerty (R-Tenn.) stressed how important federal support for commercial nuclear power is for his state and for the nation.</p>

<p>“The United States is at a pivotal moment in energy production. It’s not just for our nation, it’s for the entire world,” Hagerty said. “<strong>Tennessee has been at the forefront of what you’ve called yourself ‘the Manhattan Project 2.0.’”</strong></p>

<p>SMRs and emerging nuclear technologies were among an array of topics discussed during the Senate’s first hearing on the Department of Energy’s proposed <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/Fiscal-Year-2026-Discretionary-Budget-Request.pdf">$45.1 billion budget</a>, which cuts $19.3 billion in funding for Biden Era “green energy” initiatives, including slashing three-quarters of approved allocations for energy efficiency and renewable energy programs, which didn’t include nuclear power options.</p>

<p>The tentative request is 9.4 percent less than FY25’s $52 billion department budget. Beyond a 25-percent increase in funding for the National Nuclear Security Administration, which manages the nation’s nuclear weapons programs, it trims spending by 18.2 percent, cutting $15.2 billion in allocations from the 2021 Bipartisan Infrastructure Law and $2.6 billion from the Office of Energy Efficiency and Renewable Energy.</p>

<p>The “green energy” cuts were telegraphed by President Donald Trump during his campaign and in his executive orders but the massive rollbacks in energy innovation investments are surprising, Murray said.</p>

<p>“<strong>It feels like you want to gift-wrap the future and hand it to China</strong>,” she told Wright.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2882%29_0.jpg?itok=-gPYPJmg" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2882%29_0.jpg?itok=-gPYPJmg"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="a5042f4e-a76f-4a8f-a86a-6a2aef84af48" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2882%29_0.jpg?itok=-gPYPJmg" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Sen. Patty Murray (D-Wash.) speaks during the weekly Senate presser in the U.S. Capitol building in Washington on July 9, 2024. Madalina Vasiliu/The Epoch Times</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<h2>More Money Coming</h2>

<p>Wright assured senators that the administration will not cripple research and development of SMRs and other emerging technologies by pulling money from ongoing demonstration programs.</p>

<p>He said his department is reshuffling allocations from Biden era “intermittent” energy programs, such as solar and wind, and reorganizing its offices and staffing to be more focused on advancing technologies that will triple the nation’s electrical capacity in the coming decades.</p>

<p>Wright acknowledged the department has not yet finalized its formal spending request, cautioning that in its tentative state, “Each individual line item does not indicate a policy.”</p>

<p>“<strong>The nuclear industry is quite enthusiastic and quite confident they’re going to have the best environment ever for commercial nuclear power under this administration</strong>,” he said. “What we’re doing is mobilizing tens of billions of dollars of private capital using the government” allocations to anchor those investments.</p>

<p>Wright said the department has offered land near or at its 16 national labs. “We’ve had tons of solicitations to come build on our land,” he said.</p>

<p>Britt said that <a href="https://www.theepochtimes.com/opinion/us-china-nuclear-fusion-race-the-battle-for-energy-and-military-dominance-5828992">communist China</a> has “at least 28 nuclear reactors that are in construction, which is about half of the construction of all nuclear reactors across the entire globe,” so time is of the essence.</p>

<p>Wright said that deregulation and permitting reform are top priorities in ensuring that the United States will meet that challenge.</p>

<p>“China is moving full speed ahead with nuclear. In fact, the most reactors they’re building [are], essentially, a knockoff, a stealing of American reactor technology,” he said. “But they build them much cheaper and much faster, and they don’t have the giant bureaucratic regulatory overhang we have in the United States.”</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2883%29_1.jpg?itok=3LT6xyMN" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/image_92%2883%29_1.jpg?itok=3LT6xyMN"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="6fb0cf85-cfba-4d8d-84ed-a51c2f2f2ba4" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="281" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/image_92%2883%29_1.jpg?itok=3LT6xyMN" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>Artist rendition of NuScale Power’s small modular nuclear reactor plant. NuScale</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>Under current regulations, Wright said, New York’s Grand Central Station “could not be licensed as a nuclear reactor because its radiation is too high.”</p>

<p>The department’s pitch to commercial providers is, “We‘ll be fast, we’ll be efficient. We‘ll help you get going. We’ll arrange creative incentives for you to build nuclear reactors in our space. I think we'll do it.”</p>

<p>Hagerty asked how the department can be play “a central role in advancing and achieving American energy dominance and grid liability” by advancing SMRs at commercial scale.</p>

<p>Wright said it is prudent to be careful when investing in “first-mover” prototypes to ensure that taxpayer money is wisely spent on systems that will work.</p>

<p><strong>“I am all-in with you on advancing nuclear</strong>,” he told Hagerty, and offered an analogy to illustrate why patience is needed while the department restructures loan programs away from renewables to nuclear and other baseload generation.</p>

<p>“Imagine if the Department of Defense sent out a quote to the defense companies, and said, ‘We want to buy tanks. We'll pay full price for high-performance tanks, but you can deliver a tank that only moves some of the time, maybe when the sun’s shining, and will shoot, maybe, when the wind’s blowing,’” Wright said of intermittent power generators.</p>

<p>The Biden administration was paying full price for “an underperforming tank” while providing subsidies to the factories to build them, he said.</p>

<p>“So what do you think is going to happen?” Wright asked. “You’re going to get paid to deliver an inferior tank and a subsidy. Of course, you’re going to do it.</p>

<p>“And then what happens to your army? It’s not just the poor kids that are in those tanks, it’s the kids that are in all the other tanks that now have underperforming partners in the battle that are at risk.”</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>

Title: Iran Will Hold US Responsible For Any Israeli Attack On Nuclear Sites: Foreign Minister
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">Iran Will Hold US Responsible For Any Israeli Attack On Nuclear Sites: Foreign Minister</span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p>Earlier this week CNN had issued an alarming report claiming that Israel is currently <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/geopolitical/israel-subject-unprecedented-pressured-allies-over-gaza-escalation">preparing possible preemptive strikes</a> on Iranian nuclear facilities. It underscored that at this moment it has become very clear that Netanyahu could care less about 'pressure' from Western allies the US, UK, and Canada regarding the Gaza crisis. Israel continues to essentially be at war on multiple fronts.</p>

<p>Parallel to all of this, Washington and Iran have been engaged in productive talks on potentially reaching a fresh nuclear deal - which the Netanyahu fundamentally sees as but an Iranian ploy to buy time as it secretly develops nukes (in Tel Aviv's thinking). <strong>But Iran's leaders are calling for the United States to essentially 'keep its dog on a leash' - as Israel wishes to torpedo a deal</strong>.</p>

<p>In fresh statements, Iran now says it <strong>will hold the United States responsible</strong> in the event of an unprovoked Israeli attack on its nuclear energy sites. Certainly any such attacks would completely derail efforts to reset relations with Washington.</p>
<a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/iranfmfile.jpg?itok=G0s5AILY" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/iranfmfile.jpg?itok=G0s5AILY"><picture><figure role="group" class="caption caption-img inline-images image-style-inline-images"><img alt="" data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="d4b43976-25bd-46d4-a289-a2ecc5b864e4" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="333" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/iranfmfile.jpg?itok=G0s5AILY" typeof="foaf:Image" width="500" /><figcaption><em>via AP/Getty Images</em></figcaption></figure></picture></a>

<p>"Iran strongly warns against any adventurism by the Zionist regime of Israel and will decisively respond to any threat or unlawful act by this regime," Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi stated in a letter addressed to United Nations Secretary-General Antonio Guterres.</p>

<p>"I have called on the international community to take effective preventive measures against the continuation of Israeli threats, which if unchecked, <strong>will compel Iran to take special measures in defense of our nuclear facilities and materials</strong>," Araghchi said.</p>

<p>And as cited in <a href="https://www.reuters.com/world/middle-east/irans-revolutionary-guards-warn-israel-against-any-attack-2025-05-22/"><em>Reuters</em></a>:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>Araqchi said <strong>Iran would view Washington as a “participant” in any such attack</strong>, and Tehran would have to adopt “special measures” to protect its nuclear sites and material if threats continued, and the watchdog International Atomic Energy Agency would be subsequently informed of such steps.</em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>"The nature, content, and extent of our actions will correspond and be proportionate to preventive measures taken by these international bodies in accordance with their statutory duties and obligations," the Iranian top diplomat added.</p>

<p>Washington and Tehran are gearing up for a<strong> fifth round of nuclear talks to be held in Rome this Friday</strong>.</p>

<p>Lately the Ayatollah has weighed in following reports that Iran is ready to halt enrichment altogether and in return get sanctions lifted. Ali Khamenei had called the latest US demands that Iranian enrichment be taken down to zero <strong>"excessive and outrageous,"</strong> <a href="https://www.reuters.com/world/middle-east/iran-reviewing-proposal-5th-round-nuclear-talks-2025-05-20/">according</a> to state media on Tuesday. He further expressed doubts that current nuclear talks with the Trump administration will actually lead anywhere.</p>

<p>Meanwhile in Tehran, the parliament has "reaffirmed the peaceful nature of Iran’s nuclear program, <strong>saying that the Islamic Republic has never sought, nor will it seek, to build an atomic bomb</strong>.”</p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">Sobering insider account from Iran on the state of nuclear talks with the Trump admin: <a href="https://t.co/7tz5x2mwnl">https://t.co/7tz5x2mwnl</a></p>
— Aaron Maté (@aaronjmate) <a href="https://twitter.com/aaronjmate/status/1925473542453256481?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 22, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>Islamic Republic News Agency (IRNA), Iran’s official news agency, reported further on Thursday that "Members of parliament have stated that Iran will never back down from its right to use nuclear technology as a member of the Non-Proliferation Treaty (NPT)."</p>

<p>But again, Israel is not buying this - nor are some hawkish officials and Congressional leaders in Washington. And yet these same voices have warned that Iran has been on the threshold of building a bomb since the 1990s. </p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>
<span property="schema:dateCreated" content="2025-05-22T20:50:00+00:00" class="field field--name-created field--type-created field--label-hidden">Thu, 05/22/2025 - 16:50</span>


Title: ATF Launches "New Era Of Reform", Encourages Revoked Gun Dealers To Reapply 
Description: <span property="schema:name" class="field field--name-title field--type-string field--label-hidden">ATF Launches "New Era Of Reform", Encourages Revoked Gun Dealers To Reapply </span>

            <div property="schema:text" class="clearfix text-formatted field field--name-body field--type-text-with-summary field--label-hidden field__item"><p><em>Submitted by <a href="https://www.gunowners.org/">Gun Owners of America</a>,</em></p>

<p>The Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms, and Explosives (ATF) has just announced that it's "ushering in a new chapter" of "transparency, accountability, and partnership with the firearms industry" on its official web page.</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_14-09-26.png?itok=26BnXFig" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_14-09-26.png?itok=26BnXFig"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0aa952d4-0701-4dd3-8f30-c49748c597bd" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="381" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-22_14-09-26.png?itok=26BnXFig" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>The most notable of these changes is that ATF has invited those Federal Firearms Licensees who had their licenses revoked by the Biden Administration's "Zero Tolerance" policy to reapply and have their license restored. This change is apparently in accordance with President Trump's executive order "Protecting Second Amendment Rights."</p>

<p><a data-image-external-href="" data-image-href="/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_14-10-19.png?itok=2zB3IAz_" data-link-option="0" href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/s3/files/inline-images/2025-05-22_14-10-19.png?itok=2zB3IAz_"><picture><img data-entity-type="file" data-entity-uuid="0e4fc047-c80d-478e-b2bb-a33ca53bb242" data-responsive-image-style="inline_images" height="319" width="500" class="inline-images image-style-inline-images" src="https://assets.zerohedge.com/s3fs-public/styles/inline_image_mobile/public/inline-images/2025-05-22_14-10-19.png?itok=2zB3IAz_" alt="" typeof="foaf:Image" /></picture></a></p>

<p>Other major policy changes were also announced, including a pledge to cease "creating entirely new laws based on executive order." </p>

<blockquote class="twitter-tweet">
<p dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en" xml:lang="en">🚨BREAKING🚨<br /><br />
ATF just published a list of 10 pro-gun achievements & at least 8 more pro-gun actions that are "in progress":<br /><br />
1. Ceasing to "create entirely new laws by administrative order"<br />
2. Reversing the Biden Ban on importation of non-lethal training ammunition.<br />
3. Ending…</p>
— Gun Owners of America (@GunOwners) <a href="https://twitter.com/GunOwners/status/1925287534604820842?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">May 21, 2025</a></blockquote>
<script async="" src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script><p>This is an excellent start to improving the lives of gun owners and dealers. But not to worry, Gun Owners of America is still working on the complete and total abolishment of ATF, starting with the repealing of laws that give the agency the power to regulate. </p>

<p>If those laws are not abolished, the responsibility of enforcement will be inherited by a larger agency, like the FBI or DEA. A larger, more well-funded agency would be harder to fight on the enforcement of those same unconstitutional gun laws. </p>

<p>So, for the time being- while we still have to deal with the ATF, it's good to have it working on bettering its relationship with law-abiding gun owners rather than actively antagonizing them. </p>

<p>GOA's Senior Vice President Erich Pratt had this to say:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><em>"This new chapter marks a rare and welcome shift, as ATF is finally working to repair the damage it's done. Encouraging wrongly targeted dealers to reapply—and pledging to stop inventing laws out of thin air—will be a breath of fresh air for gun owners nationwide. That said, GOA remains committed to the complete abolishment of the ATF. </em></p>
</blockquote>

<p>While these reforms are a step in the right direction, the end goal is to eliminate the agency's power to infringe on the rights of law-abiding gun owners, once and for all."</p>
</div>
      <span rel="schema:author" class="field field--name-uid field--type-entity-reference field--label-hidden"><a title="View user profile." href="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" lang="" about="https://cms.zerohedge.com/users/tyler-durden" typeof="schema:Person" property="schema:name" datatype="" class="username" xml:lang="">Tyler Durden</a></span>

Title: Google’s AI Mode is ‘the definition of theft,’ publishers say, opt-out was considered
Description: <div class="feat-image"><img src="https://9to5google.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/4/2025/05/Google-AI-Mode-cover-2-1.jpg?quality=82&#038;strip=all&#038;w=1600" /></div><p>The AI takeover of Search is in full swing, especially as <a href="https://9to5google.com/2025/05/20/google-ai-mode-expansion/">Google’s new AI Mode is going live for all US users</a>. But for publishers, this continues the existential crisis around how Google Search is changing, with a new statement calling AI Mode “the definition of theft” while legal documents reveal that Google did consider opt out controls that ultimately weren’t implemented.</p>

This article explores the concept of system coexistence, the ability of diverse software systems built across different eras and architectures to function together within shared environments. It delves into practical strategies for achieving coexistence, such as the <a href="https://dzone.com/articles/how-the-strangler-fig-approach-can-revitalize-comp">Strangler Fig Pattern</a>, adapter-based decoupling, and event-driven communication models. The article also addresses critical supporting aspects like data coexistence, <a href="https://dzone.com/monitoring-and-observability">observability</a>, and performance monitoring, emphasizing that coexistence is not merely a transitional phase but a strategic imperative for sustainable growth and innovation. Drawing on real-world examples, such as Netflix’s cloud migration and the HealthCare.gov launch failure, this piece provides a roadmap for organizations to navigate coexistence successfully while preparing for scalable, future-ready systems.</p>
