Title:  爱奇艺已摘到了微短剧的果实 
Description:  <p style="text-align: right;"><img class="wscnph" title="" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/b4fd0e99-4a4c-4ed4-a3af-8d71f8226cec.jpeg" alt="" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnsize="87445" data-wscnh="594" data-wscnw="618"/>作者 | 黄昱</p>
<p style="text-align: right;">编辑 | 刘宝丹</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">作为“爱腾优芒”中唯一独立上市的长视频平台，爱奇艺（NASDAQ:IQ）的业绩一向具有行业风向标意义。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">在长短剧集激战，爆款剧集诞生具有不确定性的背景下，爱奇艺试图通过多种变革来提升业绩增长的确定性，从最新的业绩表现来看，爱奇艺的探索已初见成效。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">5月21日，爱奇艺发布截至2025年3月31日未经审计的第一季度财报。财报显示，一季度，爱奇艺总收入为71.9亿元，虽然同比仍然下滑约9%，但环比增长了9%；此外，Non-GAAP（非美国通用会计准则）运营利润为4.6亿元，同比下降58%，环比增长13%。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">具体业务表现来看，爱奇艺的支柱性收入来源——会员服务收入有所增长环比增长7%至44亿元，同比下降 8%；在线广告服务收入环比下降7%至13.3亿元，同比下降 10%；内容发行收入环比增长53%至6.3亿元，同比下降 32%；其他收入环比增长23.9%至8.3亿元，同比增长16%。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">爱奇艺创始人、首席执行官龚宇在当天财报电话会上表示，一季度取得的业绩环比增长得益于长视频内容强势回归和对微剧的战略投入。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">在他看来，“好内容横竖都看爱奇艺”正在占领用户心智，为未来的商业化创造了机会。这些进展坚定了爱奇艺基于市场和用户需求变化，推进商业模式和内容生态进一步升级的信心。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">长视频内容目前依然是爱奇艺发展的根基。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">云合数据显示，爱奇艺当季长剧集总市占率继续保持第一。从爆款剧集来看，今年一季度爱奇艺“迷雾剧场”新作《漂白》撑起了门面，成为一季度唯一热度值破万的爆款剧集。该剧单集收入位列爱奇艺历史第三，仅次于《狂飙》《赘婿》。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">同期古偶剧《白月梵星》也有不错的表现，虽然没能破万，但热度值也达到了9600。此外，现偶剧《爱你》不仅在国内市场大获成功，也成为爱奇艺国际版表现最好的现偶大陆剧集。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">可以看到，在经历了2024年低谷期后，爱奇艺长剧集正在重新找回节奏。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">2022年和2023年算是爱奇艺比较风光的两年。2022年，爱奇艺共有5部剧集热度值破万，要知道，在此之前爱奇艺仅有两部剧集热度过万。截至2023年底，爱奇艺热度破万的剧集已经达到十二部。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">去年全年，爱奇艺虽然持续产出了《追风者》《唐朝诡事录之西行》《我是刑警》3部爆款剧集，但其竞争对手在去年也都有亮眼的表现，这给其会员收入的增长带来了压力。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">如腾讯视频去年播出了近十部爆款剧集，而曾被外界视作“爱腾优芒”中存在感最弱的优酷，去年先是因为热播的《墨雨云间》重回聚光灯下，下半年又先后推出了《边水往事》《珠帘玉幕》《白夜破晓》等口碑热度都还算不错的剧集。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">在自制综艺上拥有独特优势的芒果TV，去年先后上线的《歌手2024》、《再见爱人4》成为现象级爆款综艺，连在有些“掉队”的剧集内容上，也产出了《小巷人家》这一爆款。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">今年一季度，腾讯、芒果TV、优酷三家在爆款剧集上的表现也都有所表现，如腾讯视频有《大奉打更人》《雁回时》，芒果TV有《国色芳华》，优酷则有《难哄》。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">显然，在行业激烈竞争的背景下，爱奇艺一季度会员服务收入依然面临增长压力。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">在去年12月，爱奇艺还弄丢了曾经长视频平台月活用户第一的位置。据Quest Mobile数据，2024年12月，爱奇艺、腾讯视频的月活用户分别为3.54亿、3.87亿，芒果TV约为2.77亿，优酷则仅为1.84亿。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">从更受关注的会员数来看，爱奇艺日均订阅会员规模已从2023年一季度的1.29亿下降至第四季度的1.003亿，去年开始则不再公布会员数。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">不过，爱奇艺方面透露，今年一季度爱奇艺会员规模健康增长，季度月均单会员收入保持健康水平。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">这背后是，会员产品定位的完善满足了更广泛用户群体的需求。其中，家庭高端星钻会员引入加更礼免费看权益后展现良好增长潜力；高性价比的基础会员规模创新高，受到年轻及下沉市场用户欢迎，其中相当比例为首次订阅。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">据腾讯财报，作为爱奇艺的头号竞争对手，腾讯视频今年一季度日均付费会员数达到1.17亿元。这将为外界评估爱奇艺会员规模提供一定参照。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">此外，不难发现，在会员服务以及在线广告增长乏力的背景下，爱奇艺正通过多举措来强化商业化能力。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">出海已是爱奇艺一大核心战略。一季度，爱奇艺国际版收入同比增长超30%，广告收入同比增长40%，日均会员数创历史新高。过去半年，海外最受欢迎的大陆剧集Top10中爱奇艺自制剧占4席，其中《爱你》收入创国际版现偶大陆剧集历史新高。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">值得关注的是，在去年9月举办的2024爱奇艺iJOY秋季悦享会上，爱奇艺还宣布了要正式进军微短剧领域。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">按照爱奇艺的蓝图，“微剧场”将以每周两部新作的速度，聚焦男女频与银发族群，主打1—5分钟的竖屏内容；而“短剧场”则计划每周更新一部新作，涵盖古言、现偶、悬疑等多种类型，每集时长约在5—20分钟，以横屏呈现。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">到今年1月13日，爱奇艺还宣布与如今势头最猛的短剧平台红果短剧达成深度合作，将启动IP联合开发、联合出品、成品内容授权等合作，共同推出更多精品微短剧。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">然而，双方的合作似乎并不愉快。在今年2月20日，龚宇公开指责红果短剧利用场的主导地位，签署排他协议。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">不过，这样一个插曲似乎没有影响爱奇艺发力短剧的决心。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">春节期间，爱奇艺上线28部精品微剧，首创“微剧春节档”和微剧艺人微博直播接力拜年活动。《家里家外》《请君入我怀》等精品微剧的推出，持续加深用户对“在爱奇艺看微剧”的认知。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">爱奇艺主站App聚焦“会员免费观看”模式，以收费微剧为主；爱奇艺极速版主推免费微剧。目前爱奇艺已拥有超15000部微剧内容，其中免费微剧和会员微剧约各占一半。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">龚宇表示，微剧内容库的建设已经达成阶段性目标，目前片库内容储备充足，未来将重点引入更多头部新片，并全力发展自制内容。第二三阶段将着力通过微剧吸引新会员，特别是渗透率相对较低的下沉市场和高龄用户，让微剧内容助力提升会员服务收入，积极拓展微剧在广告和电商领域的货币化机会。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">据悉，从2024年12月到2025年4月，爱奇艺微剧重度用户，即在爱奇艺主要观看微剧的用户增长了3倍。</p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">短剧之外，4月23日，在“2025爱奇艺世界·大会”上，爱奇艺还宣布启动以内容电商为核心的电商布局。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">爱奇艺方面表示，该战略目的是提升免费微剧业务的货币化能力，进一步发挥爱奇艺在IP、艺人资源以及优质用户等方面的优势。 </p>
<p style="text-align: justify;">如果电商业务能做好，这无疑也将能为爱奇艺在会员和广告之外，开拓新的收入来源。 </p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  微软CTO：AI已经“能力过剩”，行业需要努力缩小模型能力与实际产品交付之间的差距 
Description:  <p>微软CTO Kevin Scott日前接受媒体采访，就AI代理，编程的未来等一系列问题阐述了自己的观点。</p>
<p>在Scott看来，模型的推理能力已经超前于目前实际应用这些模型的方式。整个行业现在需要共同努力，去弥合模型实际能做的事情和交付给用户的产品之间的差距。</p>
<p>为了让代理（agents）真正变得有用，目前AI需要更好的代理记忆系统（以处理更复杂问题），同时需要一个生态系统，它应当像互联网那样（以获取信息）。</p>
<p>“AI代理编程”并不是过去四十年来软件开发第一次经历巨大变革。重点不是怎么做，而是要达成的目标。当工具发生变化时，要保持开放的心态。</p>
<p>以下是访谈重点：</p>
<blockquote>
<p><strong>模型的推理能力已经超前于我们实际应用这些模型的方式。整个行业现在需要共同努力，去弥合模型实际能做的事情和我们交付给用户的产品之间的差距。</strong></p>
<p>除了“推理能力”之外，还有很多其他方面的问题需要解决，才能让代理（agents）真正变得有用。这意味着我们需要更好的代理记忆系统，同时需要一个生态系统，它应当像互联网那样。</p>
<p>如果你真正去想象代理能够做什么、普通用户希望它们变得多有用——你就会发现，我们需要像当年互联网兴起时那样的一系列变革再次发生。这一幕的雏形，比如MCP协议，它就是一个非常好的例子。</p>
<p><strong>“AI代理编程”并不是过去四十年来软件开发第一次经历巨大变革。</strong>不管是软件还是其他东西，重点不是怎么做，而是我要达成的目标。所以我会选择最强大、最方便的方式去实现它。<strong>当工具发生变化时，要保持开放的心态。</strong></p>
<p>我当木工的时间几乎跟我写程序一样久。我十几岁那会儿，圈子里最大的话题是：你如果用了电动工具，你还算是真正的木工吗？真正的木工只用手工工具！<strong>今天这种争论仍然存在，不过换成了：你用了 CNC（计算机控制的数控工具），你还算真正的木工吗？</strong></p>
<p>现在最关键的区别，出现在产品设计者的思维方式上。目前一些初创公司，他们并不是靠搞出一套全新的基础设施来创新的；<strong>他们创新的方式是：他们对某个用户问题的理解，比任何人都更深入。然后他们基于现成的基础设施，或做些微调，就能以世界级水准来解决那个问题。这种方式，才是我们现在真正需要的。</strong></p>
<p>我认为接下来我们会看到，人们用代理去解决的问题会越来越复杂、越来越有雄心。同时，“代理网络”会越来越完整，连接越来越充分；模型的推理与规划能力也会变得更强。这将促使我们从现在的“同步交互”模式，进入到一个更强的“异步交互”时代。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>以下为对谈全文：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>主持人：<br/>Kevin，欢迎来到我们的节目。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>不用谢。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>谢谢你来。一件很有意思的事是，我去年也访问过你。你当时说了两件非常重要的事情。一个是——代理（agents）将会无处不在。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>你说的这件事真的成真了，而且来得非常快。还有一件事，我注意到去年你特别强调“规模定律”（scaling laws），对吧？</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>当时你展示了很多图表，说我们正在建造大规模基础设施，训练更大的模型，而且每两年性能就会有一次飞跃。但今年，你的重点似乎更多放在“代理网络（Agentic Web）”上。发生了什么变化？从去年到今年，我们学到了什么？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>是的，我觉得发生了很多变化。其中一件事是，<strong>去年很多人还处在一种怀疑状态中，他们在怀疑“规模定律”是否还能继续有效。而事实上，我们年复一年已经证明，它们依然有效并且运作良好。所以现在已经不再需要向人们重复这一点了。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>另一件事，说实话，<strong>是模型的推理能力已经超前于我们实际应用这些模型的方式。</strong>我最近一直在谈一个概念，叫做“能力悬空”（capability overhang）。</p>
<p>我认为，<strong>我们整个行业现在需要共同努力，去弥合模型实际能做的事情和我们交付给用户的产品之间的差距。</strong>这也是为什么在今年的 Build 大会上，“规模定律”不像去年那么吸引人的原因之一。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>还有一点我们发现了：随着过去一年代理数量的爆发式增长，以及用户在这些代理中花费时间的增加，我们意识到，<strong>除了“推理能力”之外，还有很多其他方面的问题需要解决，才能让代理真正变得有用。这也是我今天在 Build 大会主题演讲中提到的重点之一：我们需要更好的代理记忆系统。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>目前的代理记忆受限于许多方面，它们更像是一次性的、事务性的——你用它完成某个任务，期间记忆是连贯的，但这个记忆很可能会在下次交互时完全消失，这就使得我们很难将更复杂的任务委托给它们。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>而且还有一个核心问题：如果代理要变得有用，它们就必须能够替你采取行动，能够使用工具，在系统中作出改变，访问丰富多样的信息源。</p>
<p><strong>要实现这些，我们需要一个生态系统，它应当像互联网那样</strong>：如果你是信息源，你已经有了网站、有了 API，那么你必须弄清楚怎么把这些资源接通，让代理能与之通信，并且要让各方的激励机制协同一致，使他们愿意参与到这个“代理网络”中来。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>所以我认为这才是今年最大的故事——我们看到了真正进展的曙光，比如 MCP 这样的超级简单、开放协议，在代理网络中扮演的角色就像 HTTP 在互联网中一样。还有像 NL Web 这样的标准，它在“代理网络”中扮演的角色，就类似 HTML 在网页世界中的作用。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我觉得你将会看到这些系统越来越多地采用简单、可组合、可层叠的结构，开放社区将会非常活跃，最终推动代理真正实现能力的落地。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>那我总结一下我听到的意思：现在我们已经有了代理（agents），而且它们开始真正发挥作用了，对吧？而要让这些代理变得强大，它们就需要访问权限。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>它们需要能够访问互联网上的各种资源、你电脑上的内容，等等类似的信息。也就是说，你基本上需要建立起一套协议和流程，来让代理可以访问这些东西，对吧？</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>所以你现在关注的是整个技术堆栈的不同层级——比如说运行时层面，你们在那儿构建记忆系统、其他组件；然后还有像 MCP（memory coordination protocol）这样的协议，它能把代理连接到更广阔的互联网世界，从而获取信息，让信息流入代理系统中。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>那我想问一下，**这件事对微软来说为什么重要？**你们希望在这个生态系统里扮演什么样的角色？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>嗯，我觉得这里面有两点，也可能是三点特别重要。</p>
<p>第一点是，我们自己在做代理。而我们做的这些代理要对用户真正有用，就必须解决这些底层问题。就算你把范围缩小到企业级代理，<strong>作为微软的 CTO，我一直在推动的一件事就是：我希望我们公司内部所有系统都采用统一的标准协议，能和我们内部构建的代理对话。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>这样我们才能避免把整个世界暴露在所谓“康威定律”（Conway’s Law）之下。你知道，康威定律是软件架构里一个非常有趣的现象。</p>
<p>康威说，一个系统的结构往往会反映出开发该系统的组织结构，比如编译器的阶段数通常由负责这些部分的团队数量决定。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>没错。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>所以你想象一下，如果你在微软这样的大公司内部开发东西，你肯定不希望你造出来的代理，其结构完全是按照你的组织结构拼出来的。</p>
<p>但现实中如果你没有通用的协议和标准服务，这样的“组织图产品”就会反复出现。作为工程师，看到那种低效开发场景，真的很让人抓狂。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>但我认为，更重要的是，如果你真正去想象代理能够做什么、<strong>普通用户希望它们变得多有用——你就会发现，我们需要像当年互联网兴起时那样的一系列变革再次发生。我现在就能看到这一幕的雏形，比如 MCP 协议，它就是一个非常好的例子。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>它是一个非常简单但关键的协议，解决了一个非常重要的问题——不仅是为那些构建代理和平台基础设施的人服务，也同样帮助了系统的最终用户，让他们的体验变得更加有用。它还为那些服务提供方提供了机会，比如有人可能会说：“我也想参与到这个新型的大网络里来。”</p>
<p>但现在的问题是，很多人以前知道怎么去连接某个服务、怎么构建服务，但如今他们面对的是一群代理，坐在那里思考：“我该怎么把我的系统接进来？这对我到底意味着什么？”</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>甚至从商业模式的角度来说，他们也会想：我为什么要接入这个系统？它对我到底有什么价值？</p>
<p><strong>所以第二点就是——我们希望让自己构建的代理变得更有用。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>第三点是，作为一家平台型公司，这一点甚至比我们自己要写的代理更重要。微软已经在构建平台技术这条路上深耕了五十年，我们想要确保，当这个全新的“超级网络”兴起时，我们能够帮助解决其中出现的问题。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>是啊，看到你们现在在 MCP 上投入这么多，并把它整合进整个 Windows 系统，真的很酷，很厉害。这让我想到一个问题——我最近听到一些人在讨论 MCP，他们开始关注它的安全模型问题。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>我很好奇你是怎么看这个问题的。因为你前面提到过很多 MCP 技术栈和互联网技术栈之间的类比。而我们知道，互联网是有一套完整的安全机制的，比如“同源策略”（Same-Origin Policy），它确保了网站在执行代码时只能操作自己域名下的数据，对吧？但 MCP 目前似乎还没有类似的机制。所以你觉得，什么样的安全模型才是适合 MCP 的？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>嗯，说实话，我也不敢说我完全知道什么才是“正确”的安全模型。但 MCP 有一点很有趣，就是它的设计极其简洁明了，这其实使得整个社区可以相对容易地就这个问题达成共识。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我们在企业层面上确实有很多非常重视的需求，我们也和 MCP 团队合作得很好，正在推进相关工作。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>比如说，我们需要让代理具有“身份”——这样我们才能建立起权限系统。你可以定义：某个代理是代表某个用户在操作，然后它就有权访问系统中某些资源。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>甚至代理本身可以主动查询多个系统，然后说：“这是我想完成的一件事，要实现这件事，我需要访问以下这些系统。那我需要获得哪些权限才能做这件事？”</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>它可以向被委托给它的用户请求授权，说：“你能不能给我访问这些资源的权限，这样我才能替你完成你交代的任务？”是或否。</p>
<p>然后系统管理员也需要有权限来审查，比如：“我是否允许这些操作发生？”所以，这整个流程虽然并不“简单”，但其实在 MCP 架构上实现起来是可行的、逻辑清晰的。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>而关键在于：我们应该以开放的方式来做这件事。我们并不希望这些机制是专属于微软代理或微软系统的——我们真正需要的是让它像互联网一样运作的生态系统。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>对我来说，这其实是个很有意思的问题。我觉得现在围绕 AI 的发展，有两种可能的模式或者“市场路径”（Go-to-Market）正在浮现，而你们微软似乎都在关注这两个方向。</p>
<p>一种是所谓的“垂直一体化”模式，在这种模式下，你控制模型、应用、整个上下游——一切都在你手中。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>而这种模式的一个好处是：安全性可以得到很强的保障。就像苹果的 App Store 或 iPhone 模式，你可以在多个层面上强制安全策略。</p>
<p>但另一种则是“开放模型”——你牺牲一部分控制权和安全性，但能换来更强的创新活力，因为没有中心化的权威机构去限制开发者。</p>
<p>所以我想问的是，你们在微软是怎么思考要走哪条路的？你们是怎么做出这个决策的？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>是的，你看，这确实是很多人现在在讨论的一个核心问题——但我觉得，那可能是一个伪命题（false dichotomy）。</p>
<p>你知道，在这些开放系统中，它们的特点是“无需许可”（permissionless）。这种开放式创新的能力，确实带来了巨大的优势。对我个人来说，现在最让我兴奋的一件事就是：你可以不经任何人批准就去创新、去构建产品，不需要别人给你发许可，不需要通过什么中介流程才能把你的作品推向世界。</p>
<p>你不再需要通过一堆复杂的守门人机制，在你这个有想法的人与那些可能真正从中受益的人之间设下重重阻碍。</p>
<p>Kevin Scot：<br/>我觉得我们这几年建立起来的那些“中间层”，其实并没有为最核心的两方带来多少价值：一边是辛辛苦苦做出东西的人，另一边是愿意为这些成果付出注意力、金钱或其他资源的用户。</p>
<p>这就是为什么我对开放系统特别兴奋，也正是我们在做战略选择时的重要原因之一。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>但我也认为，在这些系统中，其实是有办法实现强健安全性的。我们可以借助 AI 本身的一些能力，构建出更智能的安全模型。</p>
<p>比如说，你运行的代理可以照顾到你个人的安全需求——哪些信息你愿意分享，哪些你不愿意；它还能做风险评估。</p>
<p>我举个实际例子：今天早上我正准备上台演讲的时候，突然收到一堆邮件，因为我是我妻子的备用安全账户。</p>
<p>有人在她账户上尝试篡改两步验证（2FA）设置。我第一反应是发短信给她，而不是发邮件——因为我担心她的邮箱可能已经被未经授权的第三方访问了。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我发信息问她：“你是不是在改配置？”她回复：“是的，是我。”</p>
<p>所以你可以想象，<strong>如果有一个代理可以接入你多种通信渠道，监测到这种异常行为，并调用各种资源进行“三角校验”，判断这些行为到底是合法的还是非法的，那将是非常有用的。</strong></p>
<p><strong>所以我认为，两种模式是可以共存的。并不是说非得二选一——就像你刚才设想的那样。</strong></p>
<p>主持人：<br/>这很有道理。我还有一个特别好奇的问题是——现在看来，软件工程正在发生根本性变化，对吧？</p>
<p>而你是一个在软件工程领域深耕多年的老兵，我觉得你也很重视“工艺”本身——制作事物的技艺。</p>
<p>我们刚才聊到你平时做陶艺、做包，喜欢亲手参与制作的过程。我觉得很多人对“用代理写代码”有点抵触，觉得这样会削弱那种“手工打造”的感觉，虽然我并不完全同意这个观点。</p>
<p>但我还是很想知道，<strong>作为一个真正关心编程工艺的人，你怎么看待未来的“代理编程”？</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我先说一句，我真的很欣赏“我的人”——我这里说的“我的人”，指的是广义的创作者群体。</p>
<p>包括软件工程师、机械工程师、木工、陶艺师等等这些人。我们都是从零或者原材料开始创造新东西的人。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>如果你真的热爱你的工作，你一定会对怎么做、用什么工具、用什么材料、如何组合这些细节有非常强烈的主张。这是你成为真正优秀从业者的必备条件。</p>
<p>但有趣的是——人们的观点五花八门。</p>
<p>正如你刚才提到的，我做这行已经很久了——我写第一个程序的时候只有 12 岁，也就是说我编程已经有 41 年了。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>如果你在一个领域坚持得够久，你就会看到：这并不是过去四十年来软件开发第一次经历巨大变革。每次这种变革发生时，人们都会对其含义有非常强烈的反应。</p>
<p>但现实是，人们是有选择权的。</p>
<p>我现在仍然喜欢用文本编辑器。说实话，我可能不该说这个，因为我们公司做了 Visual Studio Code（笑），但我就是一个老古板——我还在用 vim。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>至少我会用 vim，但我最爱的还是那种古早的编辑器。我就是不愿意换别的工具。</p>
<p>尽管我知道，这在某种程度上已经降低了我的效率，但我还是出于“自主选择”的理由坚持使用它。</p>
<p>但在我做的其他项目中，比如不管是软件还是其他东西，有时候我也会说：“这里的重点不是怎么做，而是我要达成的目标。”</p>
<p><strong>所以我会选择最强大、最方便的方式去实现它——不管别人会不会因此嘲笑我。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>这种情况无处不在。<strong>比如我当木工的时间几乎跟我写程序一样久。</strong></p>
<p><strong>我还记得我十几岁那会儿，圈子里最大的话题是：“你如果用了电动工具，你还算是真正的木工吗？”</strong></p>
<p><strong>“真正的木工只用手工工具！”</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/><strong>今天这种争论仍然存在，不过换成了：“你用了 CNC（计算机控制的数控工具），你还算真正的木工吗？”</strong></p>
<p>我觉得这种讨论本身就很有意思，但最终大家做出不同选择，是因为他们的价值观不同。</p>
<p>如果你更重视过程，你可能会做出完全不同的选择；而如果你更看重结果，你就可能用别的方式。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>我觉得类似“你算不算是真正的木工”“你是不是个真正的程序员”这种问题，说到底其实是在说：“只有按照我成长时的方式去做，你才是真正的XXX。”这其实是一种有偏见的说法。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>对，是这样。但现实是——这个世界的情况太多样化了，对吧？</p>
<p>所以我要说的是：我绝不会告诉任何人不要对自己的技艺有强烈的主张。你尽管有你的坚持，那很好！</p>
<p>但如果说我有什么建议的话（这不是命令，只是我个人发现有用的建议），<strong>那就是——当工具发生变化时，要保持开放的心态。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我都数不清多少次了，有些新的技术出现在其他“非软件”的创作领域，我一开始都会下意识地抗拒——<strong>比如说我当时对 3D 打印机完全提不起兴趣，我拖了很久才去学怎么用它们。</strong></p>
<p>现在我真的后悔了，因为它们几乎对我做的所有事都非常有用。出于种种复杂的原因，我没有让自己产生好奇心，这是我自己的问题，也确实有点奇怪。</p>
<p><strong>所以我的建议就是：保持好奇，去尝试。如果某样东西适合你，那就用它；如果不适合，也无妨。</strong></p>
<p>主持人：<br/>没错。那么你怎么看“软件工程代理（software engineering agents）”的未来？</p>
<p>会不会出现那种“一个代理统治一切”的局面？还是说我们会同时使用很多具有不同风格的代理？你认为这个生态系统会如何发展？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我认为将来一定是有很多不同类型的代理。这是好事。</p>
<p>我们当然会在 GitHub Copilot 以及我们正在开发的 GitHub Agent 上非常努力，希望成为很多开发者首选的工具，因为我们想让它真的对大家有用。</p>
<p><strong>但要说全世界的开发者都统一使用某一个工具来完成工作中的关键部分，我认为那不现实。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>成为一个开发者的乐趣之一，就是你有权选择工具。你可以尝试各种东西，做一些看起来“非理性”的事，也可以选择完全理性的方式。</p>
<p>这是我在过去四十年程序员生涯中始终观察到的一件事：人们不断更换自己的工具。总是在变化。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>那你有没有想过：这些代理会在哪些维度上有所不同？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/><strong>我觉得最关键的区别，可能会出现在产品设计者的思维方式上。</strong></p>
<p><strong>现在我看到最有意思的一些初创公司，他们并不是靠搞出一套全新的基础设施来创新的；他们创新的方式是：他们对某个用户问题的理解，比任何人都更深入。</strong></p>
<p><strong>然后他们基于现成的基础设施，或做些微调，就能以世界级水准来解决那个问题。这种方式，才是我们现在真正需要的。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>这也会推动代理多样性的形成——哪些代理被用来解决什么问题，最终都会受到这个维度的驱动。</p>
<p>而且说实话，现在你更容易对用户的问题形成这种“细致入微的理解”，也更容易拿起各种工具尝试去解决这些问题。</p>
<p>所以我们会看到大量公司、团队去打造各种东西来尝试解决不同的需求。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>哪怕在“软件开发工具”这个领域都已经开始疯狂了——过去一年冒出来的工具简直数不过来。</p>
<p>而且这些工具都挺有趣的，各有各的特点。</p>
<p>对于像我们这样的软件工具开发公司来说，这确实压力很大，因为你要应对那么多创新和变化。</p>
<p>但从技术角度来看，这真的太有意思了。</p>
<p>我们发现：<strong>只要你对用户的需求有某种细腻的认知，就总会有人愿意尝试你的解决方案。尤其是那些有高容忍度和高兴趣度的用户。</strong></p>
<p>主持人：<br/>是啊。我们时间快到了，但我还有个问题。</p>
<p>假设一年之后我们又在 Build 大会上坐下来聊，你觉得：现在的一些热门话题或大问题，一年后会变得不再重要？而一年后什么会成为真正重要的讨论焦点？你有哪些预测？</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/><strong>我觉得现在那些还在坚持说“这项技术还没准备好”的人——比如说：“我试过了，但稍微有点贵”或者“功能上还差一点点”——如果他们把这些当作不行动的借口，那他们很快就会被远远甩在后面。</strong></p>
<p>因为这些问题都会随着时间变得微不足道：技术每年都会变得更便宜、更强大。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我觉得在 2025 年，这个观点其实已经不需要“游说”了。过去确实有很多人大声说：“技术进展很快就会停滞，大家都会失望。”</p>
<p>虽然现在还有人这么说，但我觉得已经没什么人认真听他们的了。毕竟你听这些“唱衰者”的话，又能获得什么呢？你是在赌失败，而“赌失败”和“赌乐观”之间的成本差异，其实非常大。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/><strong>我认为接下来我们会看到，人们用代理去解决的问题会越来越复杂、越来越有雄心。同时，“代理网络”会越来越完整，连接越来越充分；模型的推理与规划能力也会变得更强。这将促使我们从现在的“同步交互”模式，进入到一个更强的“异步交互”时代。</strong></p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>现在的交互方式是：你坐下来，想着要完成一件事，然后给代理发出指令，等它返回一个结果，然后你基于那个结果再操作。</p>
<p><strong>但到了明年，你可能会看到这样的使用方式：“嘿，去帮我搞定这件事。”</strong></p>
<p><strong>然后代理会花时间去处理：它会调用很多外部系统，它会去整合信息，它会反复迭代，它会不断处理、汇总、推进，最后，在一个非即时但有深度的时间之后，代理会告诉你：“我已经帮你推进到这一步了，接下来轮到你了。”</strong></p>
<p>主持人：<br/>听起来真是我想活在的未来。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>我也这么想，真心的。</p>
<p>主持人：<br/>好吧，Kevin，非常感谢你今天来参加节目。真的非常精彩的谈话。</p>
<p>Kevin Scott：<br/>很高兴能和你聊这场对话，我也非常享受，谢谢你邀请我来。</p>
</blockquote><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  创业板收跌近1%，北证50跌超6%，银行逆势走强，恒科指跌1.7%，百度跌超4% 
Description:  <p>5月22日周四，A股全天震荡调整，三大股指集体收跌，创业板跌近1%，北证50指数大跌超6%，军工、银行逆势走强。港股午后跌幅扩大，恒科指跌2%，科网股普跌，百度跌超4%。</p>
<p><strong>A股：</strong>截至收盘，沪指跌0.22%，深成指跌0.72%，创业板指跌0.96%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/826a5873-6132-473f-9c38-4e3b05600a59.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="330" data-wscnw="668"/></p>
<p>盘面上，个股跌多涨少，沪深京三市下跌个股超4400只，板块方面，银行、军工等板块涨幅居前，宠物经济等新消费概念、固态电池等跌幅居前。银行股逆势走强，浦发银行等多股盘中再创历史新高。军工股一度拉升，四创电子等涨停。宠物经济等新消费方向走低，可靠股份等跌超10%；高位股继续调整，苏州龙杰等跌停。</p>
<p><strong>港股：</strong>港股低开低走，截至收盘，恒指收跌1.19%，恒生科技指数跌1.7%。小鹏汽车涨超5%，公司一季度财报亮眼，预计第四季度实现盈利；联想集团跌超5%；小米集团跌超2%，此前雷军发文称YU7预计7月正式上市，今晚预发布会，不会公布正式价钱，也不会开启小定。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/5f7d4255-128a-4bc7-a1cc-c9857ec507de.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="120" data-wscnw="681"/></p>
<p><strong>债市：</strong>截至收盘，国债期货多数走强，30年期主力合约跌0.04%，10年期主力合约涨0.01%，5年期主力合约持平，2年期主力合约持平。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/b014672f-2b89-4e1c-9738-187454472bbf.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="180" data-wscnw="680"/></p>
<h2>北证50指数跌超6%</h2>
<p>北证50指数低开低走，盘中跌幅扩大，收盘跌超6%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/e47e019f-91e8-4526-a1e9-f218248ec536.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="393" data-wscnw="790"/></p>
<p>消息面，据<span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/BFfk1ql16N_jG4RkwZGkxQ" target="_blank" rel="noopener">券商中国</a></span>，从走势上看，昨天（21日）北证50刚刚创出历史新高。今天就大幅调整，一方面昨天就出现了高位股退潮的现象，比如宠物经济等；二是微盘股指数不断创出新高，中证2000的成交占比已经超过了3月的高点，微盘出现了显著的超买信号。</p>
<p>华创证券研报显示，资金流动性方面，近期资金供给端，两融净流入收缩，股票型ETF流出规模大幅扩大，整体供给端净流出；资金需求端，股权融资、产业资本净减持放大，但南向资金再次净流出，整体需求端收缩。</p>
<h2>创新板块走强</h2>
<p>创新药板块持续走强，三生国健20CM涨停，走出四连板，海辰药业、舒泰神、海翔药业、睿智医药、上海谊众等涨幅靠前。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/663fda6f-ea31-4ca4-be30-0c729fc53b24.jpeg" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="2410" data-wscnw="1173"/></p>
<p>消息面上，港股创新药企三生制药公告称，其与辉瑞公司就前者自主研发的PD-1/VEGF双特异性抗体SSGJ-707签订了独家许可协议。本次协议中12.5亿美元的首付款再次刷新了国产创新药出海首付款金额纪录。</p>
<h2>军工股盘中一度拉升</h2>
<p>航天军工板块表现活跃，盘中一度拉升，截至收盘，四创电子、海特高新、银河电子等涨停，晟楠科技、国睿科技等纷纷走高。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/0919e1c1-35e8-4d75-adcc-a46703b0c367.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="450" data-wscnw="625"/></p>
<p>消息面，据<span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://baijiahao.baidu.com/s?id=1832736918524398466&amp;wfr=spider&amp;for=pc" target="_blank" rel="noopener">新华社</a></span>，外交部发言人毛宁21日表示，美所谓“金穹”计划公然提出大幅增加外空作战手段，将加剧外空战场化和军备竞赛风险，中方对此严重关切。</p>
<p>国新证券认为，近期受地缘冲突的影响，国防军工表现较好，中长期来看，我国军费平稳增长为国防军工行业稳定发展提供坚实基础，行业规模和利润有望保持持续上升态势。</p>
<h2>联想跌超5%、百度跌超4%、小米集团跌2.3%</h2>
<p>截至收盘，联想集团跌5%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/b7818e57-8bae-4a8c-94a1-d4fec7d8dd13.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="395" data-wscnw="808"/></p>
<p>消息面，<span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747614" target="_blank" rel="noopener">华尔街见闻提及</a></span>，受到关税逆风的影响，联想Q4净利润在经历了五个季度的增长后首次出现下滑，净利润暴跌64%，远低于市场预期。公司将下滑归因于非现金的认股权证公允价值损失。</p>
<p>IDC的数据显示，联想在第一季度巩固了对惠普和戴尔科技的领先优势，其全球发货量增长了近11%。鉴于宏观经济前景和人工智能繁荣的可持续性存在不确定性，投资者仍然关注人工智能服务器的需求。</p>
<p>截至收盘，小米集团跌超2%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/4d8fab66-2476-4aa8-b0bc-67e799190296.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="391" data-wscnw="813"/></p>
<p>消息面，此前雷军发文称YU7预计7月正式上市，今晚预发布会，不会公布正式价钱，也不会开启小定。</p>
<p><strong>截至收盘，</strong>百度跌超4%。</p>
<p><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/eed76671-7278-4b2a-b855-3bab81954275.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="393" data-wscnw="816"/></p>
<p><span style="color: #1482f0;"><a style="color: #1482f0;" href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747542" target="_blank" rel="noopener">百度</a></span>发布2025年第一季度财报显示，营收324.5亿元超预期，同比增长3%，利润同比增长42%，智能云增速达42%，萝卜快跑订单量同比增长75%，全球出行服务次数超1100万。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  美银Computex 2025观察：AI需求、供应链、机器人与技术路线图 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">5月19日，本届台北国际电脑展（Computex 2025）拉开帷幕，将持续至23日。本届大会以“AI Next”为主轴，聚焦“智慧运算＆机器人”“次世代科技”以及“未来移动”三大主题。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">目前为止，展会有哪些亮点？据追风交易台消息，5月21日，美银美林Brad Lin、Mike Yang发布研报指出，Computex 2025确认了几个趋势：<strong>AI需求强劲，AI硬件供应链瓶颈缓解，机器人革命临近。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">根据报告，大会上，英伟达、联发科等巨头均展示下一代AI解决方案，显示AI产业已从试验走向大规模部署；大会还显示出AI计算力需求激增、供应链障碍缓解的趋势，投资者关注点从云端AI转向更广泛的物理AI应用和边缘计算部署，预计将为台积电、瑞昱半导体、联发科和信骅等高质量半导体公司提供持续增长动力。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/0cfef5de-a97f-4212-a534-ce315f63d904.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="475" data-wscnw="766"/></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">AI需求从试验转向规模部署，云到边缘集成加速</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告指出，Computex 2025展会确认，在市场对资本支出增加的担忧日益增加之际，AI发展势头仍保持强劲的趋势。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告称，<strong>2025年的叙事已从简单关注AI PC转变为在更广泛的应用范围内实现AI。</strong>包括英伟达、富士康、ARM和联发科在内的行业领导者都强调了“一个由无处不在AI定义的未来”——包括移动设备、汽车、物联网、智慧城市和工业系统，涵盖云端到边缘，由计算、连接和集成方面的持续创新提供动力。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">会议上也有更多关于系统级集成技术的讨论，如英伟达的NVLink Fusion，以及对软件平台和AI模型的持续开发，以支持更加无处不在的AI生态系统。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>尽管市场对ROI和资本支出存在担忧，但AI基础设施建设持续进行。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">富士康表示，看到实用的AI应用正在出现，这支持长期计算需求；ARM将AI称为“比互联网和智能手机更大的事物”，并表示产业正站在AI时代的门槛。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">GB200产能爬坡，供应链瓶颈缓解</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">报告显示，在参加英伟达及其生态系统参与者主办的一系列讨论后，<strong>专家们发现GB200现已全面投产，供应链良率问题的最严重阶段似乎已经过去。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">值得注意的是，GB200机架包含120万个组件，所有这些组件都必须在工厂级别进行集成和可靠性测试，而之前的模型是在数据中心完成此类工作。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">展望未来，英伟达确认，GB300——保持与GB200相似配置——仍然按计划在2025年下半年推出，对订单取消或供应限制的担忧减少。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>报告指出，这对投资者来说是个重要信号，这表明AI硬件供应链正趋于稳定，可能减轻此前影响AI芯片可获得性的瓶颈问题。</strong></p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">从数字AI代理到实体机器人</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">与2024年相比，2025年Computex展会明显增加了对机器人技术的讨论。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>报告称，焦点正从数字AI代理转向物理AI。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">英伟达指出，启用这一功能需要机器人计算机、数字孪生和训练——所有这些都需要大量计算资源。虽然时机尚不明确，但黄仁勋预计还需要2-3个迭代周期。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">这表明机器人技术正成为AI投资的下一个重要领域，可能代表下一个具有万亿美元潜力的市场。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/f6a26a97-2568-4a42-bb59-29c2a5198951.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="374" data-wscnw="517"/></p>
<h2 id="6">行业巨头动态一览</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>英伟达在COMPUTEX 2025上推出了一系列突破性产品和战略举措，强化了该公司在AI和加速计算领域的领导地位。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">黄仁勋称英伟达是AI基础设施公司，并公布了将于2025年第三季度推出的GB300升级版，相比GB200，其推理性能提高1.5倍，HBM内存增加1.5倍，网络性能提高2倍。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">在企业AI方面，英伟达还发布了RTX Pro企业服务器、NVLink Fusion，开放AI基础设施生态系统，推动数据中心基础设施的无缝部署，展示了代理AI在AI 工厂、代理和机器人领域的应用布局。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>高通的展会重点是AI带来的根本性变革。</strong>其骁龙芯片今年将为85台以上的PC提供动力，明年将增加到100个，进一步推动PC计算的边界。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">公司还推出了终端设备代理AI模型Context，通过骁龙的NPU（神经处理单元）提供更高工作效率和更好数据安全性；高通还宣布进军数据中心CPU市场。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/c5c68c9c-f634-43f2-b185-8c1ee6d7cea8.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="309" data-wscnw="768"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>富士康展示了如何打造自己的AI模型FoxBrian，</strong>基于Llama 3/4，更好地支持其三个智能平台并理解制造数据。结合其高雄数据中心和高质量大规模预训练语料库，富士康能够处理跨越100B到1T标记的领域。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/f90e9119-bc13-4333-a0ef-b1c81b16b60c.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="302" data-wscnw="766"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>ARM认为，行业已经进入AI时代，需求正从实验转向规模化部署，预计AI市场将比互联网或智能手机更大。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">ARM预计，截至2025年底，大约50%运往超大规模数据中心的服务器芯片将是基于ARM的；此外，随着数据中心电力需求激增，特别是中国台湾的电力消耗预计到2028年将增长8倍，ARM的能效对于合适的AI规模变得越来越重要。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">ARM也在快速扩展到边缘AI，为99%的智能手机提供支持，并在PC/平板电脑领域占据份额——预计2025年将达到40%以上的出货量。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">AMD展示了在游戏、AI PC和工作站方面的最新成就和产品线。 在游戏产品线方面，AMD推出了Radeon RX 9060 XT 16G，以支持FSR4具有更低延迟的更好性能和功耗效率。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/52b54594-e0f5-4998-8767-464f2944c5a8.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="343" data-wscnw="768"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>联发科展示的亮点包括在高速通信（交换机、PHY）、汽车、Wi-Fi和可穿戴设备方面的强大表现；NXP的演示主要集中在边缘AI，强调其相对于云端中心模型的优势；信骅则展示了加速的产品开发计划。</strong></p>




<p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  美债砸盘、美元也跌，德银警告：这次就算美联储QE也救不了！ 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">美国债券遭遇的拍卖失利，同时美元也在走弱，显示出外国投资者正“罢买”美国资产。德银认为只有国会，而非美联储才能解决这个问题。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据追风交易台消息，德意志银行在最新的报告中表示，这一危机的核心在于外国投资者不再愿以当前价格水平为美国财政与经常账户双赤字提供融资，而且这一问题只能由国会通过紧缩财政来解决，而非美联储的货币政策干预。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">面对这一日益严峻的局势，德意志银行明确警告“为更多波动做好准备”。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">同时，德银表示，美股韧性也将受到考验，而亚洲投资者行为将成为关键风向标，投资者应密切关注亚洲交易时段的美债和美元反应。</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">美股也危险了，亚洲投资者成关键风向标</h2>
<p>德银表示，在这种环境下，美股很难保持韧性。</p>
<blockquote>
<div>2023-24年期间，美国收益率和股票的上涨是市场对美国增长预期的重新评估。这是完全合理的。今天则非常不同。这完全是对美国资产的财政风险溢价的增加，很难证明这种（资本成本上升的负面）驱动因素能对风险资产产生积极影响。</div>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">德意志银行分析师George Saravelos强调，关注亚洲投资者的行为：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">根据其外部净平衡框架，亚洲是美国赤字最主要的资金提供者，其次是欧洲。因此，美国之安全和汇率的表现在非美国交易时段变得尤为关键。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>如果美元/日元在东京交易时段加速下行，这将是资本从美国回流国内市场的强烈信号。</strong>因此，投资者应密切关注亚洲交易时段的市场反应，这可能预示危机的进一步发展。</p>
</blockquote>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">美联储干预没用，只有国会行动：财政紧缩或美债贬值</h2>
<p>德银表示，解决这个问题并不容易，金融抑制的形式，例如SLR改革和在下一次再融资公告中缩短美债发行期限已经被频繁提及。在某种程度上，缩短美国债务组合的久期有助于吸引外国买家，但较低的久期也意味着更高的债务展期风险。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">德银特别强调，只有国会才能解决这个问题，最终解决这一问题只有两种“方案”：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">极端的市场错位可能会促使美联储采取干预措施（QE）以维持市场正常运作，但这实际上无法解决问题的核心，甚至可能因提高通胀预期而适得其反。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>这个问题只有两个“解决方案”：要么美国大幅修改目前国会中的和解法案，以实现更严格的财政政策；要么美国债务的非美元价值需要大幅下降（如美元贬值），直到其变得足够便宜以吸引外国投资者回归。</strong></p>
</blockquote>

Title:  连增三月？OPEC+讨论7月大幅增产，沙特出手惩戒“配额叛徒” 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;">OPEC+将在7月再次大幅增产？油市或面临新一轮下行压力。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据媒体周四报道，<strong>OPEC+正在讨论在6月1日的月度会议上，批准7月再次大幅增产41.1万桶/日，几乎是最初计划的三倍。</strong>如果该计划获批，那么这将成为OPEC+连续第三个月大幅增产。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">消息传出后，<strong>布伦特原油短线下挫至63.92美元/桶，跌破64美元关口，日内跌幅达1.5%。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><img class=" wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/578b1b69-0a8e-40d3-8901-9ad877a27582.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="566" data-wscnw="836"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3744556?keyword=OPEC" target="_blank" rel="noopener">华尔街见闻此前提及</a>，<strong>OPEC+加速增产的决定意在对那些超配额生产的成员国施压，</strong>同时也为这些国家提供更大的机会进行补偿性减产，来弥补过去的“作弊”行为。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">在上次会议上，沙特阿拉伯警告过度生产的成员国称，除非他们遵守配额，否则沙特可能会放大这一历史性政策转变并继续增加产量。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">与特朗普在4月发起贸易战的时间相吻合，OPEC+的意外增产最初对油价造成了沉重打击，导致布伦特原油跌至近60美元的四年低点。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>如果OPEC+确认连续第三月大幅增产，油价可能面临新一轮下行压力。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">尽管OPEC+声称增产是为了满足需求，但市场对供应过剩的担忧正在加剧。上周，国际能源署（IEA）预测，由于“经济逆风”，在强劲的第一季度之后，2025年余下时间全球石油需求增长将放缓。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">高盛据此预测，<strong>在同意7月增产后，OPEC+将暂停进一步增产。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">除了6月的月度会议外，OPEC+的22个成员国还将于5月28日举行第39届OPEC+部长级会议<span id="docs-internal-guid-08ab46b1-7fff-7375-0f3f-b367dcd317ea"></span>，审查2025年和2026年的基本产量配额。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p> 

Title:  连贝克汉姆都上头，Labubu在全球杀疯了！带动泡泡玛特4月欧美销量狂飙，TikTok涨粉68% 
Description:  <p style="text-align: left;"><span style="text-align: justify;">继泰国公主拎爱马仕配Labubu后，贝克汉姆也晒女儿送Labubu礼物，LABUBU3.0风靡欧美明星及KOL圈，并在全球范围内引发一场抢购热潮！</span></p>
<p>近日，足球巨星贝克汉姆在社交媒体上分享了一则温馨内容——他的小女儿Harper送给他的礼物：一个来自泡泡玛特的Labubu玩偶。这一分享迅速在全球社交媒体上引发关注，让LABUBU火热更彻底了。</p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/da9ba602-0c10-430a-bf81-039d09145c31.jpeg" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="1875" data-wscnw="1080" data-wscnsize="304652"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">据追风交易台消息，美银美林最新研究报告指出，泡泡玛特的Labubu 3.0系列已经在全球范围内走红，4月美国及欧洲市场销售同比增长约8倍和5倍，多数零售店前出现大量排队购买的场景。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>更重要的是，Labubu在时尚领域的影响力正在提升，越来越多的名人和KOL将其作为装饰物，</strong>泡泡玛特美国Tik Tok 粉丝数也从3月的43.12万增至72.29万（+68%），4月在Tik Tok零售销售方面排名第一。</p>
<p>根据美银美林报告，随着泡泡玛特全球扩张战略取得实质性进展，公司有望实现“世界泡泡玛特”的目标。<strong>美银预计其未来三年营收和净利润将持续高速增长，并维持买入评级，目标价236港元。</strong></p>
<h2 id="labubu-3-0">名人效应引爆欧美市场，Labubu 3.0销售火爆、粉丝大涨</h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">美银美林报告指出，泡泡玛特正在迈向建立真正全球性平台的新阶段。这一点通过其从东南亚（低垂果实）到西方市场的&#34;真实&#34;渗透率上升得到证实，特别是美国和欧盟市场的具体热度，缓解了市场对这些具挑战性市场发展的担忧。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">令人瞩目的是，美银渠道调查显示：</p>
<blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;">4月份美国/欧盟市场同比增长约8倍/5倍，这进一步印证了Labubu 3.0的成功及其对海外市场的积极推动。尽管美国加征关税导致价格上涨，但似乎并未对其受欢迎程度产生不利影响。</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>在线上渠道，Labubu 3.0发布后，泡泡玛特官方应用在美国App Store购物类别中跃升至第一位。泡泡玛特美国Tik Tok 粉丝数也从3月的43.12万增至72.29万（+68%），4月在Tik Tok零售销售方面排名第一。</strong></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">线下方面，根据美银渠道调查，今年以来公司已新增14家零售店，主要分布在美国、欧盟和东南亚。值得注意的是，泡泡玛特优先选择地标（牛津街）、文化场所（卢浮宫）和高端购物中心（MEGA Bangna）开设零售店，为消费者提供沉浸式体验和社交功能。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong>根据美银预测，泡泡玛特预计将在海外/国内市场新开110/20家零售店，到2025年底总数将达到约650家。</strong></p>
<h2 id="f2cbfd71">国内市场销售加速增长，业绩高增长为估值提供支撑</h2>
<p>与此同时，泡泡玛特在国内市场增长动力依然强劲。</p>
<p><strong>根据Meritco数据库，4月份泡泡玛特通过在线电商平台（包括天猫、京东、抖音）的销售同比增长287%，较2025年第一季度(+223%)加速，其中天猫/京东/抖音分别增长156%/66%/457%。国内线下同店销售增长明显加速，增长50%（相比2025年第一季度+23%）。</strong></p>
<p><img class="wscnph" src="https://wpimg-wscn.awtmt.com/1cc92233-a496-4a0f-9355-cfdb558b82ad.png" data-wscntype="image" data-wscnh="487" data-wscnw="1158" data-wscnsize="67285"/></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">美银维持对泡泡玛特的买入评级，目标价236港元（为市场最高预测）。分析师认为，公司正朝着&#34;世界的泡泡玛特&#34;目标稳步推进全球布局，并将泡泡玛特作为消费板块中结构性增长的首选之一。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">根据美银预测，泡泡玛特2025年营收将达到226.01亿港元，净利润将达到65亿港元，同比增长91%；2026年将达到101.1亿港元，同比增长55.5%。</p>
<p style="text-align: left;">业绩高增长为当前估值提供了有力支撑，目前，泡泡玛特股价约为207港元，对应2025年42.42倍市盈率，2026年27.27倍市盈率。考虑到其高速增长，这一估值水平仍具吸引力。</p>

Title:  摩根大通戴蒙：美国仍面临滞胀风险，美联储不降息是正确的 
Description:  <p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">据彭博社5月22日报道，摩根大通CEO Jamie Dimon在全球中国峰会上接受采访时表示，他无法排除美国经济陷入滞胀的可能性，认为美国正面临地缘政治、财政赤字和物价压力的重大风险。</p>
<p>这位华尔街顶级银行家直言不讳地说道：</p>
<blockquote>
<p>我不同意我们（的经济）正处于最佳状态的说法。</p>
</blockquote>
<p>同时，戴蒙强调美联储保持观望态度、暂不降息的策略是正确的。而这一尖锐立场与市场普遍乐观情绪形成鲜明对比。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">在经济基本面看似稳健但政策变动充满不确定性的背景下，美联储官员今年始终维持利率不变。政策制定者表示，同时应对高通胀与高失业率双重风险的可能性正在上升。这或是滞胀的前兆。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">政策不确定性导致企业投资停滞。特朗普政府混乱的关税政策及缩减政府机构的举措，已引发市场对贸易、通胀、失业及潜在经济衰退的广泛担忧。银行高管透露，众多企业正在暂停扩张计划，包括华尔街投行主导的利润丰厚的并购交易，这进一步加剧了经济放缓的风险。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">此前，对冲基金桥水的创始人达利欧也发出了类似警告。</p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">周二，对冲基金桥水的创始人达利欧在出席活动时，被问及鉴于目前美国的经济状况，美联储是否有降息的空间。对此，<a href="https://wallstreetcn.com/articles/3747495?keyword=%E9%99%8D%E6%81%AF" target="_blank" rel="noopener">达利欧表示，美联储处境艰难，不应当降息。</a></p>
<p data-pm-slice="1 1 []">达利欧认为，美联储当前不应降息，降息并不是合适的货币政策选择。他指出，美联储处在一个非常困难的境地，需要在多种因素间进行权衡。当前存在巨大的不确定性，市场情绪也在恶化，但实际上，实体经济本身还没有出现显著的问题。所以，美联储的处境非常棘手。</p><p>本文来自华尔街见闻，欢迎下载APP查看更多</p>

Title: Trump administration seeks to end basic rights and protections for child immigrants in its custody

Title: There is no excuse for the killing of two Israeli embassy workers | Kenneth Roth
Description: <p>Critics of Israel’s atrocious conduct in Gaza should be clear that their focus is the authors of that violence – not Israeli civilians</p><p>Israel’s campaign of bombing and starving Palestinian civilians in Gaza is inexcusable. It reflects a massive war crime, as the international criminal court has already <a href="https://news.un.org/en/story/2024/11/1157286">charged</a>, and arguably <a href="https://www.kenroth.org/a-case-can-be-made-that-israel-has-genocidal-intent/">genocide</a>. But it in no sense justifies the murder of two young Israeli embassy workers in Washington by a man who then <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/live/2025/05/22/us/israel-embassy-shooting-dc">chanted</a>: “Free, free Palestine”. Nothing justifies violence against civilians.</p><p>The killing of Yaron Lischinsky and Sarah Milgrim <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/live/2025/05/22/us/israel-embassy-shooting-dc/israel-embassy-staffers-killed?smid=url-share">occurred</a> on Wednesday evening outside the Capital Jewish Museum, where the American Jewish Committee was hosting a reception for young diplomats. The suspect, identified as Elias Rodriguez of Chicago, was detained shortly after the shooting. Title: Trump defies ethics warnings with private meme coin dinner
Description: <img src="https://images.axios.com/rZf5wc4GtYh7lrqWpEMtLkpqAOI=/2025/05/22/1747953887783.jpg"> <div><a href="https://truthsocial.com/%40realDonaldTrump/114553573338999017" target="_blank">Screenshot via Truth Social</a></div><p>The president hosted a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/23/trump-meme-coin-dinner" target="_blank">highly anticipated</a> "exclusive" dinner for the largest holders of his meme coin, <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/01/19/trump-meme-coin-what-to-know" target="_blank">Official Trump</a>, at his golf club in Virginia on Thursday night.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>Fight Fight Fight, LLC — a company linked to President Trump's family — <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/01/19/donald-trump-crypto-billionaire" target="_blank">sold a digital token</a> that gave anyone in the world a chance to pay for a night of access to the commander-in-chief.</p><hr><ul><li>The promotion has stunned ethics experts. One Democrat <a href="https://x.com/ChrisMurphyCT/status/1919719580080955807" target="_blank">called it</a> "the biggest corruption scandal in the history of the White House."</li><li>White House press secretary Karoline Leavitt denied any conflicts of interest but refused to release the list of attendees, telling reporters: "The president is attending it in his personal time. It is not a White House dinner."</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>Wealthy donors have long used campaign contributions to gain access to elected officials — but with key guardrails and oversight.</p><ul><li>U.S. law bars foreign money and prohibits politicians from using campaign funds for personal gain.</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying: </strong>"We've never had a president actually try to raise money and get people to buy an interest in a venture of his at the same time that he's sitting in the White House," Richard Painter, President George W. Bush's ethics lawyer, <a href="https://www.politico.com/newsletters/morning-money/2025/05/09/the-blunt-reality-of-trumps-brazen-crypto-conflicts-00337504" target="_blank">told Politico</a>.</p><ul><li>Democrats have <a href="https://www.axios.com/newsletters/axios-crypto-fa5b4790-2c4f-11f0-8ce4-89f34dc9bfc1#story1" target="_blank">proposed at least five bills</a> that would block activity like this, but none of them are likely to see action in a GOP-controlled Congress.</li><li>As Sen. Kirsten Gillibrand (D.-NY) points out, <a href="https://www.semafor.com/article/05/14/2025/senators-tease-passage-of-embattled-crypto-bill-without-language-targeted-at-trump" target="_blank">there are already laws</a> against this kind of thing — but <a href="https://www.justsecurity.org/73148/good-governance-paper-no-15-enforcing-the-emoluments-clauses/" target="_blank">enforcement of those rules is murky</a>, especially with Trump loyalists in charge.</li></ul><p><strong>By the numbers: </strong>Inca Digital, a data intelligence firm, estimates that the top 220 holders <a href="https://www.cbsnews.com/news/trump-meme-coin-top-220-buyers-spent-140-million-analysis/" target="_blank">collectively spent more than $140 million</a> to ensure they got a spot in the meme coin celebration.</p><ul><li>The most spent was $16.4 million.</li><li>The contest was announced on April 23 and ran through May 12. To qualify to attend, a wallet owner had to register with Fight Fight Fight, pass a background check, and hold a high enough <em>average</em> amount of Official Trump over the contest period. </li><li>The token had lost considerable value since <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/01/18/trump-meme-coin-25-billion" target="_blank">its pre-inauguration release</a>, but it's up more than 50% since the dinner was announced.</li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>That price increase has held even after the contest ended, suggesting that holders might expect more perks or access ahead. </p><p><strong>The intrigue: </strong>Only a few attendees were known ahead of time. Crypto billionaire <a href="https://x.com/justinsuntron/status/1925225722559242748" target="_blank">Justin Sun</a>, who at one point was under investigation by the SEC, is probably the best known. </p><ul><li>Kain Warwick, an Australian crypto investor and creator of the decentralized finance platform, Synthetix, <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2025/05/12/us/politics/trump-crypto-coin-auction.html" target="_blank">told the New York Times</a> that he had a spot. </li><li>So did the meme coin startup MemeCore, which acquired a massive stockpile in order to send someone to the event.</li></ul><p><strong>How it works: </strong>Other buyers haven't been publicizing their attendance, but blockchain analysis suggested that much of the buying was happening outside the U.S., according to <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/graphics/2025-trump-memecoin-foreign-crypto-traders/?srnd=homepage-americas" target="_blank">an analysis by Bloomberg</a>.</p><p><strong>What we're watching: </strong>Fight Fight Fight still controls <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/14/trump-meme-coin-40-million" target="_blank">80% of the supply</a> of Official Trump, which it can sell off over time. </p>

Title: Supreme Court says Trump can fire agency heads for now, but insulates Fed
Description: <p>The Supreme Court issued a stay Thursday allowing President Trump's removal of two independent agency heads to remain in force for now — but suggested <a href="https://www.axios.com/economy/federal-reserve" target="_blank">Federal Reserve</a> officials have special protection based on the central bank's unique structure.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The ruling suggests that the court will ultimately vest the president with significant authority to remove the heads of agencies, even when Congress has structured them to be insulated from politics. </p><hr><ul><li>But the decision's carve-out for the Fed will come as a significant relief to markets that were concerned about the central bank's independence.</li></ul><p><strong>Catch up quick: </strong>The court issued a stay Thursday night in a case involving Trump's move to fire members of the National Labor Relations Board and Merit Systems Protection Board.</p><ul><li>"The stay reflects our judgment that the Government is likely to show that both the NLRB and MSPB exercise considerable executive power," and that therefore it is within the executive authority of the president to remove them, the court's majority wrote.</li><li>But is is not a final decision. The question of whether the NLRB and MSPB appointments fall under certain exceptions "is better left for resolution after full briefing and argument."</li><li>The order was unsigned, and the three liberal justices dissented, arguing that a stay should be granted.</li></ul><p><strong>The intrigue: </strong>In issuing the stay, the majority noted a claim by the fired members that their case could have implications for the president's ability to remove members of the Fed's Board of Governors or Open Market Committee.</p><p><strong>What they're saying: "</strong>We disagree. The Federal Reserve is a uniquely structured, quasi-private entity that follows in the distinct historical tradition of the First and Second Banks of the United States," the majority wrote.</p><p><strong>Yes, but: </strong>A dissent by Justice Elena Kagan seemed impatient with the logic of the Fed carve-out. </p><ul><li>"The majority closes today's order by stating, out of the blue, that it has no bearing on" removal of Fed officials.</li><li>"I am glad to hear it," Kagan writes, "and do not doubt the majority's intention to avoid imperiling the Fed."</li><li>"But then, today's order poses a puzzle. For the Federal Reserve's independence rests on the same constitutional and analytic foundations as that of the NLRB, MSPB, FTC, FCC, and so on—which is to say it rests largely on" Humphrey's Executor, a 1935 case establishing the constitutionality of independent agencies.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>From the moment Trump started removing agency commissioners earlier this year, analysts predicted the ultimate target might be more control over the Fed.</p><ul><li>But some hoped past court <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/21/fed-trump-independent-agencies" target="_blank">comments</a> about the central bank as a unique entity might insulate it from such action. </li></ul><p><em>Editor's note: This story has been updated with new details throughout. </em></p>

the publication of his report last year.</li></ul><p><strong>What to watch: </strong>Comer said he is seeking responses by May 29 and testimony scheduled between June 2 and 25.</p><ul><li>A spokesperson for Biden declined to comment.</li></ul><p><em>Editor's note: This story has been updated with additional reporting. </em></p>

Title: Trump admin nixes Harvard's ability to enroll international students
Description: <p>The <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">Trump</a> administration pulled <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/06/harvard-trump-grant-funding" legal status," per DHS.</li><li>Noem said the administration is "holding Harvard accountable for fostering violence, antisemitism, and coordinating with the Chinese Communist Party on its campus."</li><li>She said in a statement that the university lost their program certification "as a result of the failure to adhere to the law," calling it "a warning to all universities and academic institutions across the country."</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying: </strong>Harvard spokesperson Jason Newton called the government's action unlawful. </p><ul><li>"We are fully committed to maintaining Harvard's ability to host international students and scholars, who hail from more than 140 countries and enrich the University – and this nation – immeasurably," he said in an emailed statement.  </li><li>He said the university is working quickly to provide guidance to the campus community. </li><li>"This retaliatory action threatens serious harm to the Harvard community and our country, and undermines Harvard's academic and research mission," Newton said.</li></ul><p><strong>Context: </strong>The administration has for months been discussing plans to try to block certain Title: What to know about the Israeli Embassy employees killed in D.C.
Description: <p>Yaron Lischinsky and Sarah Lynn Milgrim were identified Thursday as the two people killed <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/22/israeli-embassy-staff-killed-shooting-capital-jewish-museum-dc" target="_blank">in a shooting</a> Wednesday night outside the Capital Jewish Museum in Washington, D.C.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>The suspect, who authorities believe acted alone, was arrested by a museum security guard after he entered the building following the shooting. FBI Deputy Director<strong> </strong>Dan Bongino called the shooting an "act of targeted violence" in a <a href="https://x.com/FBIDDBongino/status/1925420904500085116" target="_blank">post to X.</a></p><hr><ul><li>The Metropolitan Police Department identified the suspect as Elias Rodriguez, 30, of Chicago.</li><li>Metropolitan Police Chief Pamela Smith said in a press briefing that Rodriguez chanted "free, free Palestine" while being arrested.</li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>Lischinsky, 30, and Milgrim, 26, both worked for the Israeli Embassy, the Israel Foreign Ministry said in a statement <a href="https://x.com/IsraelMFA/status/1925459648028545364" target="_blank">shared to X</a>.</p><ul><li>The pair met while working at the Embassy and were soon to be engaged, Israeli Ambassador to Washington Yechiel Leiter said at a press briefing.</li><li>Lischinsky and Milgrim were set to travel to Israel on Sunday, Milgrim's father, Robert Milgrim, told the <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2025/05/22/world/middleeast/israel-embassy-dc-shooting-victims-sarah-milgrim-yaron-lischinsky.html" target="_blank">New York Times</a>. While there, she was going to meet his family for the first time and Lischinsky had planned to propose, he said.</li></ul><p><em>Here's what we know about the victims so far:</em></p><h2>Yaron Lischinsky</h2><p><strong>Lischinsky was a research</strong> assistant at the Israeli Embassy in D.C. since September 2022, according to his <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/yaron-lischinsky/" target="_blank">LinkedIn</a>. </p><ul><li>He was previously a desk officer at the Population and Immigration Authority in Jerusalem. </li></ul><p><strong>Lischinsky received</strong> a Bachelor's degree from the Hebrew University of Jerusalem, where he studied international relations and Asian affairs. </p><ul><li>He also received a Master's degree in government, diplomacy and strategy from Reichman University with a focus on diplomacy and conflict studies. </li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>Originally from Germany, Lischinsky moved to Israel at 16, per the New York Times.</p><ul><li>The German Embassy did not immediately respond to Axios' request for comment. Germany's Foreign Minister Johann Wadephul told reporters Lischinsky was an Israeli diplomat and held German citizenship. </li><li>He grew up with a Jewish father and a Christian mother and was a practicing Christian, the New York Times reported.</li></ul><p><strong>Ron Prosor, </strong>Israel's ambassador to Germany, called Lischinsky "bright, curious, engaged" in a <a href="https://x.com/Ron_Prosor/status/1925484186023895257" target="_blank">post to X</a>. </p><ul><li>Prosor said he had taught Lischinsky when he was a student at Reichman University and also worked with him as a diplomat. </li><li>"He was a Christian, a true lover of Israel, served in the IDF, and chose to dedicate his life to the State of Israel and the Zionist cause," Prosor wrote.</li></ul><p><strong>Nissim Otmazgin,</strong> the Dean of Humanities at Hebrew University, <a href="https://www.cnn.com/us/live-news/israeli-embassy-washington-dc-shooting-05-21-25#cmazf9tfe000q3b6m30j28rl2#cmazf9tfe000q3b6m30j28rl2#cmazf9tfe000q3b6m30j28rl2" target="_blank">told CNN</a> that Lischinsky's "dream was to become a diplomat." </p><ul><li>"In many ways, I think for me, he symbolizes the hope of Israel," Otmazgin said, adding that he was "idealistic" and "trying to do good for their country."</li><li>"So in this sense, it is not only a personal tragedy, it's also kind of public tragedy," he said.</li></ul><h2>Sarah Lynn Milgrim</h2><p><strong>Milgrim had been working</strong> at the embassy since November 2023 in its Department of Public Diplomacy, according to her <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/sarah-milgrim/" target="_blank">LinkedIn</a>. </p><ul><li>She previously worked at Tech2Peace in Tel Aviv, where she focused on "the role of friendships in the Israeli-Palestinian peacebuilding process," per LinkedIn. </li><li>She obtained a Bachelor's degree in environmental studies from the University of Kansas. Her LinkedIn also showed two Master's degrees — one from the University for Peace and the other from American University. </li></ul><p><strong>KU Hillel,</strong> a Jewish student group at Kansas University, said <a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/DJ9SZpAK8Ha/?hl=en" target="_blank">in a statement </a>that Milgrim's "bright spirit and passion for the Jewish community touched everyone fortunate enough to know her." </p><ul><li>"Those closest to her describe her as 'the definition of the best person," the statement continued.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>Her father said he saw news alerts for the shooting Wednesday night and<strong> </strong>his wife checked their daughter's location, only to see it at the crime scene. </p><ul><li>"I pretty much already knew," he told the New York Times. "I was hoping to be wrong."</li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/22/israeli-embassy-staff-killed-shooting-capital-jewish-museum-dc" target="_blank">2 Israeli Embassy staff killed near Capital Jewish Museum in D.C., officials say</a></p><p><em>Editor's note: This story has been updated with additional information.</em></p>

Title: Hurricane season expected to be above normal, NOAA says
Description: <p>The <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2025/05/09/fema-chief-fired-cameron-hamilton-louisiana" target="_blank">2025 Atlantic hurricane season</a> is expected to be above normal, NOAA meteorologists said Thursday in their annual forecast.</p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> The outlook comes as the Trump administration explores downsizing or <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/21/trump-fema-hurricane-season-disasters" target="_blank">dismantling FEMA</a>, the federal agency tasked with responding to storms and other natural disasters.</p><hr><p><strong>The big picture:</strong> This year is likely to have 13 to 19 named storms, with three to five of those being Category 3 hurricanes or stronger, according to National Weather Service director Ken Graham.</p><ul><li>This season isn't expected to be as active as <a href="https://www.noaa.gov/news-release/noaa-predicts-above-normal-2024-atlantic-hurricane-season" target="_blank">last year's</a>, he said, but it only takes one takes one storm to hit where you live. </li><li>Colorado State University's forecast last month lines up with NOAA's — <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/tampa-bay/2025/04/03/2025-hurricane-season-storm-activity-forecast" target="_blank">"above-normal" activity</a> with 17 named storms, nine hurricanes and four major hurricanes. </li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>In response to questions about staffing cuts, Graham and acting NOAA administrator Laura Grimm told reporters Thursday they are confident in their forecasting ability for the season.</p><ul><li>Graham also told Axios that NWS this year is seeing the same level of interest in weather briefings from their federal partners, including FEMA, as compared to last year, despite those cutbacks.</li><li>"We are fully staffed at the Hurricane Center, and we definitely are ready to go," Grimm said.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out:</strong> Michael Brennan, director of the National Hurricane Center, is slated to give his annual congressional briefing Thursday afternoon about hurricane season preparedness.</p><p><strong>Meanwhile, </strong>U.S. Homeland Security Secretary Kristi Noem earlier this week reiterated the administration's priority to shift FEMA's responsibilities to states.</p><ul><li>"Our goal is that states should manage their emergencies and we come in and support them," she said at Tuesday's meeting to reform FEMA, according to <a href="https://www.reuters.com/business/environment/fema-should-take-new-name-states-should-bear-costs-dhs-head-noem-says-2025-05-20/" target="_blank">Reuters</a>.</li><li>President Trump — <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/Fiscal-Year-2026-Discretionary-Budget-Request.pdf" target="_blank">whose budget</a> proposes more than $646 million in cuts to FEMA — has signed executive orders aimed at <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/presidential-actions/2025/01/council-to-assess-the-federal-emergency-management-agency/" target="_blank">streamlining the federal disaster agency</a> and <a href="https://www.presidency.ucsb.edu/documents/executive-order-14239-achieving-efficiency-through-state-and-local-preparedness" target="_blank">shifting more responsibility</a> to the states, Axios' Natalie Daher writes. Fully eliminating FEMA would require an act of Congress.</li><li>Other <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/28/noaa-layoffs-threaten-weather-climate-forecasts" target="_blank">staffing cuts</a> and <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/27/noaa-merges-climate-prediction-center" target="_self">changes</a> being made to NOAA and its agencies, including the NWS, are raising concerns about <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/20/noaa-federal-layoffs-weather-forecasting-threat" target="_self">reduced forecasting abilities</a>.</li></ul><p><strong>Between the lines: </strong>David Richardson, the current acting head of FEMA as of earlier this month, has no experience managing natural disasters and acknowledged in private meetings that the agency doesn't yet have a fully formed hurricane response plan, the <a href="https://www.wsj.com/politics/policy/fema-hurricane-season-no-plan-39042ee6?mod=hp_lead_pos2" target="_blank">Wall Street Journal reported</a>.</p><ul><li>"As FEMA transforms to a smaller footprint, the intent for this hurricane season is not well understood," warned an internal review <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2025/05/15/politics/fema-review-concerns-hurricane-season" target="_blank">obtained by CNN</a> last week. "Thus FEMA is not ready."</li><li>Since that leak, FEMA appears to be taking steps to bolster its disaster response efforts, according to <a href="https://www.cnn.com/2025/05/21/politics/fema-hurricane-prep-kristi-noem" target="_blank">CNN</a>.</li></ul><p><strong>Threat level:</strong> Louisiana, Texas and Florida could face the greatest financial burdens in a world with less federal relief assistance, Axios' Alex Fitzpatrick writes, based on <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2025/04/16/louisiana-fema-payouts-hurricanes-season" target="_blank">new analysis</a> from the Carnegie Disaster Dollar Database.</p><ul><li>Louisiana residents also have received the <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2024/10/09/fema-money-louisiana-assistance-hurricanes" target="_blank">most FEMA direct assistance</a> since 2015, according to Carnegie.</li><li>Louisiana's congressional delegation <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2025/05/09/fema-chief-fired-cameron-hamilton-louisiana" target="_blank">expressed concern</a> earlier this month to Axios about the federal government's ability to respond to a large-scale disaster.</li></ul><p><strong>The intrigue:</strong> NOAA's leadership gave the forecast in Gretna, a suburb of New Orleans, in recognition of the 20th anniversary of Hurricane Katrina's devastation in the region.</p><p><strong>How it works: </strong>Atlantic hurricane season officially starts June 1, but storms can form any time.</p><ul><li>NHC began its daily tropical outlook May 15, and so far all has been quiet in the Gulf, Caribbean and Atlantic.</li><li>Historically, the most active period for strong storms in the Gulf and the Atlantic is August and September.</li></ul><p><strong>What's next:</strong> Authorities urge residents to prepare now for the season by <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2023/05/31/hurricane-emergency-kit-checklist" target="_blank">gathering emergency supplies</a>, <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2024/05/31/preparation-checklist-hurricane-season-home-vehicle-pets" target="_blank">preparing their home</a> for storms and making an <a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2024/06/27/hurricane-evacuation-plans-contraflow" target="_blank">evacuation plan</a>.</p><p><em>Editor's note: This story has been updated with additional information.</em></p><h2>Go deeper:</h2><ul><li><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/13/fema-state-funding-trump-executive-order" target="_blank">These states would suffer the most without FEMA</a></li><li><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/21/trump-fema-hurricane-season-disasters" target="_blank">Trump's FEMA risks "flying blind" into hurricane season</a></li><li><a href="https://www.axios.com/local/new-orleans/2024/06/27/hurricane-evacuation-plans-contraflow" target="_blank">Contraflow is dying as a New Orleans hurricane evacuation option</a></li></ul>

Title: 2 Israeli Embassy staff killed in shooting near Capital Jewish Museum in D.C., officials say
Description: <p>Two <a href="https://www.axios.com/world/israel" target="_blank">Israeli</a> Embassy staff were fatally shot at close range while leaving an event Wednesday night at the Capital Jewish Museum in D.C., the embassy's spokesperson in Washington, Tal Naim Cohen, told Axios.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>The suspect, who was apprehended by a museum security guard minutes after the shooting, chanted "free Palestine" as he was arrested, Metropolitan Police Chief Pamela Smith said at a press <a href="https://www.facebook.com/MayorMurielBowser/videos/1221158726321259/" target="_blank">briefing</a>.</p><ul><li>The victims were identified by the <a href="https://x.com/IsraelMFA/status/1925459648028545364" target="_blank">Israel Foreign Ministry</a> on Thursday morning as Yaron Lischinsky and Sarah Lynn Milgrim.</li></ul><hr><ul><li>Israeli Ambassador to Washington Yechiel Leiter called them a "beautiful couple" and said Lischinsky had "purchased a ring this week with the intention of proposing to his girlfriend next week in Jerusalem."</li><li>Police identified the suspect as 30-year-old Elias Rodriguez of Chicago, Illinois and said they believe he acted alone.</li></ul><p><strong>The latest: </strong>Attorney General Pam Bondi visited the shooting scene Thursday and told reporters that the suspect "will be prosecuted to the fullest extent of the law." </p><ul><li>"No parents should have to be called and told that their children were violently murdered leaving a religious event at the Jewish Museum. That should never happen in this world and not in our country," she said. </li><li>Bondi did not offer any updates on the case and would not confirm if the Justice Department would seek the death penalty. </li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying:</strong> President Trump and Israeli Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu spoke on Thursday, the prime minister's office said in a statement.</p><ul><li>Trump expressed "deep sorrow over the shocking murder in Washington of two Israeli embassy staff members," and Netanyahu thanked Trump for his efforts to combat antisemitism in the U.S., the statement said.</li><li>Trump had previously offered condolences to the victims' families in a Truth Social <a href="https://truthsocial.com/%40realDonaldTrump/posts/114549529250052858" target="_blank">post</a>, saying "These horrible D.C. killings, based obviously on antisemitism, must end, NOW! Hatred and Radicalism have no place in the USA," he said.</li><li><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/trump-wants-netanyahu-end-gaza-war" target="_blank">Netanyahu</a> has <a href="https://x.com/IsraeliPM_heb/status/1925428916811894955" target="_blank">ordered</a> the strengthening of security at Israeli missions around the world and for state representatives in response to the shooting.</li></ul><p><strong>Details: </strong>Smith said police were alerted just after 9pm ET Wednesday about a shooting in the area around the museum in downtown D.C., which is near government buildings including the FBI's Washington Field Office and tourist attractions.</p><ul><li>"Prior to the shooting, the suspect was observed pacing back and forth outside of the museum," Smith said.</li><li>Rodriquez was not previously known to the police, Smith said at the briefing. </li><li>A LinkedIn page shows Rodriquez is an employee of American Osteopathic Information Association (AOIA). Mayor Muriel Bowser said at the briefing, "We will not tolerate any acts of terrorism, and we're going to stand together as a community in the coming days and weeks to send a clear message that we will not tolerate antisemitism."</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>The American Jewish Committee was hosting at the museum the annual Young Diplomats Reception, which "brings together Jewish young professionals ... and the D.C. diplomatic community for an evening dedicated to fostering unity and celebrating Jewish heritage," per a <a href="https://www.ajc.org/events/washington" target="_blank">post</a> by the Jewish advocacy group advertising the event.</p><p><em>Editor's note: This article has been updated with new details throughout.</em></p>

Title: Iran threatens to move nuclear material to secret sites to thwart Israeli strike
Description: <p><a href="https://www.axios.com/world/iran" target="_blank">Iran</a> threatened on Thursday to move its nuclear material to undeclared sites to protect it from a potential Israeli military strike. </p><p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> The threat, made in an <a href="https://x.com/iran_un/status/1925569265987363091?s=46" target="_blank">official letter</a> from Iran's Foreign Minister Abbas Araghchi to the UN secretary-general and International Atomic Energy Agency (IAEA) director-general, signal the risk of an unprecedented escalation in the Iranian nuclear crisis. </p><hr><ul><li>The IAEA is currently able to access and monitor Iran's enriched uranium stockpiles, which are stored in declared sites. </li><li>If that material is moved, it will be much harder to know whether Iran is building a nuclear weapon or not. </li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>The threat comes after CNN and Axios reported that <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/21/israel-strike-iran-nuclear-facilities" target="_blank">Israel has been making preparations</a> to swiftly strike Iran's nuclear sites if U.S.-Iran nuclear talks break down in the coming weeks. </p><ul><li>One source told Axios that <a href="https://www.axios.com/world/israel" target="_blank">Israel</a> believes its operational window for a successful strike could close soon.</li></ul><p><strong>What they are saying:</strong> "Under conditions wherein threats made by the Zionist fanatics persist, the Islamic Republic of Iran shall be left with no recourse but to implement special measures for the protection of its nuclear facilities and materials, the relevant particulars of which shall thereafter be communicated to the IAEA," Araghchi wrote. </p><p><strong>Driving the news:</strong> Araghchi and White House envoy Steve Witkoff will hold a fifth round of <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/15/iran-deal-proposal-witkoff-enrichment" target="_blank">nuclear talks</a> in Rome on Friday, with Oman's foreign minister mediating.</p><ul><li>The negotiations have hit a roadblock over the fact that Iran says it will only sign a deal that allows a domestic enrichment capability, and the U.S. has said enrichment is its red line.</li><li>Israeli Strategic Affairs Minister Ron Dermer and the director of Israel's Mossad spy agency David Barnea will meet Witkoff in Rome on Friday on the sidelines of the nuclear talks, two Israeli officials said. </li><li>The officials said Dermer and Barnea are traveling to Rome to coordinate positions with Witkoff and be briefed immediataely after the talks.</li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>The Israeli intelligence community has shifted just in the past few days from believing a <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/16/trump-confirms-us-gave-iran-proposal-for-nuclear-deal" target="_self">nuclear deal</a> was close to thinking talks could soon break down, Israeli sources say. </p><ul><li>Hence the urgency behind Israel's preparations to strike fast if President Trump gives a green light.</li><li>A U.S. official told Axios the Trump administration is concerned Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu might make his move even without approval from Trump.</li><li>Trump spoke to Netanyahu on Thursday and they "agreed on the need to ensure that Iran does not obtain nuclear weapons," per the Israeli readout.</li></ul><p><strong>The other side:</strong> Araghchi wrote in his letter that Iran "will take all necessary measures to protect and defend its citizens, interests, and facilities against any terrorist or sabotage actions."</p><ul><li>"Iran strongly warns against any adventurism by the Israeli Zionist regime and will respond decisively to any threats or unlawful actions by this regime. We also believe that if any attack is carried out against the nuclear facilities of the Islamic Republic of Iran by the Israeli regime, the U.S. government will be complicit and bear legal responsibility," the Iranian foreign minister wrote. </li></ul>

Todd Young (R-Ind.) told <a href="https://www.semafor.com/article/05/21/2025/senate-russia-hawks-sick-of-waiting-on-sanctions" target="_blank">Semafor's Burgess Everett</a>, adding, "And it's pretty clear to me that Putin has been jerking us around for months." </li></ul>

Title: Trump's Education Department closure and layoffs blocked by federal judge
Description: <p>A federal judge on Thursday blocked the Trump administration from dismantling the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/05/trump-federal-education-funding-map-schools" target="_blank">Department of Education</a> while a lawsuit challenging the move proceeds.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The judge's preliminary injunction said that <a href="https://www.axios.com/politics-policy/donald-trump" target="_blank">President Trump</a> and Education Secretary Linda McMahon don't have the power to shutter the agency — and that its closure runs contrary to federal laws. </p><hr><ul><li>U.S. District Judge Myong J. Joun of Massachusetts also ordered the administration to reinstate the jobs of terminated Education Department employees. </li><li>"Defendants have not pointed to any case that indicates that the Secretary's effective dismantling of the Department is within her reorganization powers," Joun <a href="https://storage.courtlistener.com/recap/gov.uscourts.mad.282419/gov.uscourts.mad.282419.45.0.pdf" target="_blank">wrote</a>. </li><li>The Trump administration will challenge Joun's ruling "on an emergency basis," Education Department spokesperson Madi Biedermann said in a statement.</li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>The judge said the administration didn't provide research to support why an <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/20/trump-order-education-department-dismantle" target="_blank">executive order</a> to dismantle the Education Department, but shuttering a federal department was slashed. </li></ul><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/25/local-schools-federal-funding-superintendents" target="_blank">Education Department cuts threaten to deepen local schools' woes</a></p><p><em>Editor's note: This story has been updated with details throughout and an Education Department statement. </em></p>

Title: 5 key takeaways from highly anticipated MAHA commission report
Description: <p><strong>President Trump's</strong> <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/02/13/trump-maha-commission-rfk-chronic-illness" target="_blank">Make America Healthy Again Commission</a> blamed factors including bad diets, chemical exposure and unnecessary medication for causing childhood chronic illness in a highly anticipated report released Thursday.</p><p><strong>Why it matters: </strong>The 68-page document from a panel led by HHS Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. seeks to lay out a unifying theory around what's causing conditions like obesity, autoimmune conditions and behavioral disorders in kids.</p><hr><ul><li>But it was developed in little more than three months and seeks to strike a balance between protecting consumers and promoting economic interests, especially when it comes to <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/rfk-roundup-weedkiller-chronic-disease-glyphosate" target="_blank">pesticides</a> and chemicals commonly used in agriculture. </li><li>"This is not, in any way, an attack on the American farmers or industry," NIH director Jay Bhattacharya, a member of the commission, told reporters Thursday. "What this is is a commitment to get excellent answers, excellent science, so that we can enable people to do the right thing." </li></ul><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>As with Kennedy's <a href="https://www.axios.com/2024/11/14/maha-movement-federal-health-agencies" target="_blank">broader health care philosophy,</a> the report blends mainstream ideas with highly controversial elements, including doubts about the current childhood vaccine schedule.</p><p><strong>Here are the key takeaways:</strong></p><p><strong>1. Ultra-processed foods. </strong>The commission, in the first and longest section, acknowledges that popular snacks and beverages save Americans time and money, but cites research that suggests <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/04/23/food-dye-ban-rfk-pepsi" target="_blank">ultra-processed foods</a> are linked to chronic diseases and says children need more "whole foods." </p><ul><li>"I think everybody wants to prioritize the ultra-processed food crisis and try to reduce our reliance on ultra-processed foods and try to improve the quality of the food," Kennedy said on Thursday. </li></ul><p><strong>2.</strong> <strong>Chemical exposures. </strong>Potential toxins in the environment are a big concern, but the Trump administration is treading lightly. </p><ul><li>Farm groups <a href="https://www.agweb.com/news/policy/politics/farmers-brace-impact-what-maha-report-could-mean-agriculture" target="_blank">worried</a> ahead of the report's release that it would target pesticides like glyphosate, which are widely used in agriculture. </li><li><strong>"</strong>American farmers rely on these products, and actions that further regulate or restrict crop protection tools beyond risk-based and scientific processes set forth by Congress must involve thoughtful consideration of what is necessary for adequate protection, alternatives, and cost of production," the report states.</li></ul><p><strong>3.</strong> <strong>More "gold-standard science." </strong>The report also portrays research on chemical exposure and chronic disease as a necessary competitive advantage for the U.S.<strong> </strong></p><ul><li>Understanding potential links between chemical exposure and chronic illness <strong>"</strong>cannot happen through a European regulatory system that stifles growth," the report says. Rather, it should happen through science done by the federal government and "through unleashing private sector innovation."</li></ul><p><strong>4. Overuse of medicine. </strong>The commission calls out kids' "overmedicalization" — and continues to cast <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/20/fda-limits-covid-boosters" target="_blank">doubt on childhood vaccines</a>. </p><ul><li>It cites a 1,400% increase in antidepressant prescriptions for American adolescents between 1987 and 2014, as well as increased prescribing of stimulants, antibiotics and asthma drugs. </li><li>Long-term research on the impact of commonly used drugs for kids is limited, but there are "contributory human data that raise important questions" about antidepressants, stimulants and other treatments, the report says. </li><li>The commission also questions the current U.S. childhood vaccine protocol and says vaccines would benefit from "more rigorous clinical trial designs." Vaccines are <a href="https://www.immunize.org/wp-content/uploads/catg.d/p2073.pdf" target="_blank">already studied</a> in large trials and subject to ongoing safety surveillance. </li></ul><p><strong>5</strong>. <strong>Corporate influence. </strong>The role of corporate interests features prominently in the report, despite assurances that it's not anti-industry. </p><ul><li>Misaligned incentives in federal regulations and significant scientific funding from food, pharmaceutical, tech and chemical companies contribute to the rise of chronic disease, the report claims. </li></ul><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>The secretaries of agriculture, education and housing, as well as the administrator of the Environmental Protection Agency and other federal officials, sit on the 14<strong>-</strong>member commission. </p><ul><li>White House deputy chief of staff <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/03/08/stephen-miller-dei-outside-trump-white-house" target="_blank">Stephen Miller</a> is a member, along with Office of Management and Budget Director Russell Vought, who co-authored the Heritage Foundation's <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/01/23/trump-executive-orders-list-project-2025-policies" target="_blank">Project 2025</a>.</li></ul><p><strong>What's next: </strong>The commission now has about 80 days to create a strategy for how the federal government should respond, per Trump's original <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/presidential-actions/2025/02/establishing-the-presidents-make-america-healthy-again-commission/" target="_blank">February order</a>. </p><ul><li>Agriculture Secretary Brooke Rollins said that updated dietary guidelines will likely be released before this fall. </li><li>"What you're going to see is a whole new day on dietary guidelines where federal nutrition advice will be sound. It will be simple, and it will be clear," Rollins said. </li></ul>

Title: Why the bond market is barfing
Description: <p>Around the world, investors are sending a clear-as-glass signal: After years of profligate debt issuance, the world's major <a href="https://www.axios.com/economy" target="_blank">economies</a> are now facing the bill.</p><p><strong>The big picture: </strong>A sell-off in bond markets over recent weeks is signaling that the long-term trajectory for interest rates is higher than it has been in decades. The drop in long-term bond prices means a rise in the interest rates governments must pay to borrow money.</p><hr><ul><li>The anticipated multitrillion-dollar widening of U.S. deficits due to the tax cut and spending legislation that passed the House early Thursday morning is part of the story, as is the <a href="https://www.axios.com/2025/05/19/moodys-credit-rating-us-debt-reason" target="_blank">Moody's downgrade</a> of the U.S. government's credit rating last week.</li><li>But it's really a bigger, global phenomenon — suggesting a step-shift in what savers demand to tie up their money in the long term across major advanced economies.</li></ul><p><strong>Driving the news: </strong>The 30-year U.S. Treasury bond yield touched 5.13% at one point Thursday morning, the highest since 2007. On Wednesday, an auction of 20-year bonds showed <a href="https://www.reuters.com/business/tepid-demand-us-treasury-auction-shows-investor-jitters-about-tax-bill-deficit-2025-05-21/" target="_blank">surprisingly soft demand</a>.</p><ul><li>In Japan, with the highest ratio on Earth of debt to the size of its economy, long-term bond yields have hit new <a href="https://www.ft.com/content/791cbe4c-2ab5-46e3-9a23-492e86edebcb" target="_blank">all-time highs</a> this week. The nation's 40-year bonds were yielding 3.69% Thursday, up more than a percentage point from early April.</li><li>Long-term rates in the U.K., Canada and Europe have similarly marched upward, if less dramatically.</li></ul><p><strong>State of play: </strong>Moves in shorter-term bonds have been more modest, meaning what has changed is <em>not </em>investors' near-term expectations for the economy, inflation, and monetary policy, but rather the riskiness of locking their money in at low rates.</p><ul><li>In general, a steeper yield curve — higher long-term rates than short-term rates — implies a stronger growth outlook. But there are reasons to think something else is afoot.</li><li>In a volatile world economy — one in which globalization marches backward or other negative supply shocks arrive — central banks might need to crank rates higher in the coming decades to keep inflation from taking off.</li><li>Moreover, investors worry there will be more government debt issuance in the coming decades than savings to absorb that debt.</li></ul><p><strong>What they're saying: </strong>"This rise has taken place not for virtuous reasons around faster growth but rather because of risks around higher inflation and the need for higher interest rates to compensate for holding long-dated dollar-denominated assets," wrote Joe Brusuelas, chief economist at RSM, in a note.</p><ul><li>"The risks and opportunities around holding such debt are part of the explanation," he added. "A structural change is taking place in the market, forcing a general repricing of risk."</li></ul><div>Data: Federal Reserve; Chart: Axios Visuals</div><p><strong>The long-term bond sell-off</strong> has serious implications for both ordinary American borrowers and the nation's long-term fiscal picture.</p><p><strong>Zoom out: </strong>Because rates on Treasury securities form the bedrock costs for all other forms of borrowing, these higher costs will eventually show up in the form of more expensive mortgages and car loans.</p><ul><li>The good news is that those forms of lending are anchored to shorter-duration rates. Even if you take out a 30-year mortgage, for example, lenders know it will likely be paid off long before that as you move or refinance.</li><li>And shorter-duration rates aren't up much.</li></ul><p><strong>Yes, but: </strong>If bond investors are correct about the long-term trajectory of rates, there will be higher borrowing costs and more lending activity crowded out by the government in the years and decades ahead.</p><p><strong>Zoom in: </strong>If the higher long-term rates hold, it implies meaningfully higher debt service costs for the U.S. government's existing debt pile. That could squeeze the government's ability to pay for other priorities, whether national defense or maintaining the social safety net.</p><p><strong>The bottom line: </strong>"Everybody I have talked to in financial markets, they are staring at the [big, beautiful] bill and they thought it was going to be much more in terms of fiscal restraint," Federal Reserve governor Christopher Waller said Thursday morning on Fox Business.</p><ul><li>"The markets are looking for a little more fiscal discipline," Waller said. "They are concerned."</li></ul>

Title: OpenAI, UAE will build massive Stargate AI center in Abu Dhabi
Description: <p>OpenAI will partner with United Arab Emirates to build Stargate UAE, a massive new Middle East data center that's part of the company's <a in the UAE, we're transforming a bold vision into reality," OpenAI CEO Sam Altman said in a statement. "It's a step toward ensuring some of this era's most important breakthroughs — safer medicines, personalized learning, and modernized energy — can emerge from more places and benefit the world."</p><p><strong>Chris Lehane, </strong>OpenAI vice president of global affairs, told Axios that OpenAI hopes the deal will help "lead as many countries as possible onto the U.S. rails, into the U.S. AI system. This is a real moment in time to do that — this is an important first brick in the road. There are two countries in the world that can build this at scale, and the U.S. has a lead."</p><p><strong>What's next:</strong> OpenAI says it wants the UAE deal to be the first of many such arrangements.</p><ul><li>OpenAI chief strategy officer Jason Kwon will kick off a road show across the Asia Pacific region next week, meeting with  governments and potential private-sector partners.</li></ul>
